Rulings on Moving to Muzdalifah and Standing at Qazh
Rulings on moving to Muzdalifah and standing there.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for departing from 'Arafah to Muzdalifah and for standing at Qazh, and identify which actions are wajib, sunnah, or mustahabb.

Core Idea
Departure from 'Arafah after sunset is wajib; walking calmly is recommended; standing at Qazh is the prescribed wuquf.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the essential acts upon leaving 'Arafah for Muzdalifah. It distinguishes between what is obligatory (wajib), what is sunnah, and what is recommended (mustahabb), based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Understanding these gradations is key to performing Hajj correctly, as mixing sunnah with wajib can lead to unnecessary burden or missed obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key acts
List the main actions described: departure from 'Arafah, mode of travel to Muzdalifah, staying overnight, and standing at Qazh.
These are the core elements of this segment of Hajj.
2
Determine the legal status of each act
For each act, note whether the passage labels it as wajib, sunnah, or mustahabb. Look for keywords like 'بعد الغروب وجوبا' (after sunset, obligatory) or 'مستحب' (recommended).
The hukm (ruling) is derived directly from the text.
3
Understand the time conditions
Note the critical timing: departure must be after sunset. If the imam delays, pilgrims should not wait beyond night. Early departure that exceeds 'Arafah's boundaries incurs a dam.
Timing is crucial for validity and to avoid penalty.
4
Recognize the consequence of violation
If you depart early and cross the boundary of 'Arafah, a dam (penalty) is due. If you delay without excuse, it is considered bad (makruh).
Dam is a type of penalty in Hajj.
5
Locate the standing place at Muzdalifah
The passage identifies Qazh as the place where the Prophet stood. It is also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram. This is the location for the wuquf at Muzdalifah.
Standing here is part of the sunnah of the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزدلفة هي من الزلفى، وهو القرب وإنما سمي بها؛ لأن آدم عليه قرب فيها إلى حواء؛ أو لأنه يتقرب فيها إلى الله تعالى، وهي علم للبقعة لا يدخلها "ال" إلا لمحاً للصفة، ثم اعلم أن الرواح إليها ماشياً مستحب؛ لأنه عليا لما أفاض من عرفات رأى أصحابه يتسارعون في السوق والمشي فقال علي: "ليس البر في إيجاف الخيل ولا في إيضاع الإبل، عليكم بالسكينة والوقار، وقوله : "بعد الغروب" بيان للسنة حتى لو مكث بعد ما أفاض الإمام كثيرا بلا عذر أساء، ولو أبطأ الإمام ولم يفض حتى ظهر الليل أفاضوا؛ لأنه أخطأ السنة، ولو دفع قبله، فإن جاوز حدود عرفة لزمه دم ويقال للمزدلفة: جمع أيضاً، وقيل: المشعر الحرام. (فتح) بعد الغروب: أي غروب الشمس من يوم عرفة وجوبا، والمبيت بها سنة. (ع) وانزل بقرب إلخ: أي وقف فيه؛ لأنه هو الموقف؛ لما روي: "أنه عليه لما أصبح وقف على قزح"، رواه أبو داود، و"قزح" بضم وفتح، الأصح أنه المشعر الحرام، وعليه ميقدة، قيل: هي کانون آدم عليه، وفي "المطالع": أنه موقف قريش في الجاهلية؛ إذ كانوا لا يقفون بعرفة وإضافة جبل إليه بيانية مشتق من "قزح الشيء"، = مشتقة
Muzdalifah is from al-zulfa, which means nearness. It was named because Adam, peace be upon him, approached Eve there, or because one draws near to Allah there. It is a proper noun for the location; the definite article 'al' does not enter it except to indicate the attribute. Then know that walking to it is recommended (mustahabb), because when he (the Prophet) departed from 'Arafat, he saw his companions rushing in the market and walking, so he said: "Righteousness is not in racing horses nor in spurring camels; upon you is tranquility and dignity." His saying: "after sunset" is an explanation of the sunnah. Thus, if one stays long after the imam has departed without excuse, it is bad. If the imam delays and does not depart until night becomes apparent, they depart because he has missed the sunnah. If one pushes ahead of it (the imam), and if he exceeds the boundaries of 'Arafah, a dam is due. Muzdalifah is also called "Jama'" and it is said: al-Mash'ar al-Haram. (Fath) "after sunset" meaning the sunset of the day of 'Arafah, and it is obligatory, and staying overnight there is sunnah. ('Ayni) "and alight near (the mountain)" meaning stand there because it is the standing place. It is narrated that when morning came, he (the Prophet) stood on Qazh, reported by Abu Dawud. Qazh: with dammah and fatha. The most correct view is that it is al-Mash'ar al-Haram, upon which there is a fire altar. It is said it is the kiln of Adam, peace be upon him. In al-Mutali', it is the standing place of Quraysh in the Jahiliyyah, as they would not stand at 'Arafah. The addition of "mountain" to it is explanatory, derived from "qazaha al-shay'" = something sprang? (The text ends abruptly).
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage provides rulings and recommendations for the movement from 'Arafah to Muzdalifah and the actions there. The name Muzdalifah is explained as deriving from 'zulfa' (nearness), referencing Adam's approach to Eve or the act of drawing near to Allah. It is a specific place name. The sunnah is to walk to Muzdalifah in a calm and dignified manner, as the Prophet instructed his companions to avoid haste. The time for departure is after sunset on the day of 'Arafah; this is considered obligatory (wajib). Delaying departure without excuse is blameworthy; if the imam delays significantly, the pilgrims should depart anyway. If one departs early and exceeds the boundaries of 'Arafah, a dam is due. Staying overnight (mabit) at Muzdalifah is sunnah. Upon arrival in the morning, the pilgrim should stand at the location of Qazh, which is identified with al-Mash'ar al-Haram (the Sacred Monument), where the Prophet stood. Qazh is also described as the site of a fire altar (mawqidah) linked to Adam. The text ends with a note on the etymology of 'Qazh'. The key rulings are: departure after sunset is wajib, walking calmly is sunnah, standing at Qazh is the place for wuquf at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (muzdalifah): A location between 'Arafat and Mina where pilgrims stay overnight after 'Arafah; also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
الرواح إليها ماشياً (al-rawah ilayha mashiyan): Walking to Muzdalifah in a calm manner, as recommended by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) regarding the time of departure from 'Arafah to Muzdalifah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Departure is allowed at any time after zawal.
B) Departure after sunset is wajib.
C) Departure before sunset is sunnah.
D) Departure is recommended (mustahabb) after nightfall.

Key Takeaway
The departure from 'Arafah after sunset is wajib, walking calmly is recommended, and standing at Qazh is the prescribed wuquf of Muzdalifah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
The Ruling of Standing at Arafat and the Prohibition of Batn 'Arnah
Sharh expanding on the place and manner of standing at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the place of standing at Arafat, identify the prohibited area of Batn 'Arnah, and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Standing at Arafat is invalid in the valley of 'Arnah — avoid it completely.

Standing at Arafat is the central rite of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that any part of Arafat is valid for wuquf except the valley of 'Arnah. This lesson examines the proof for this exception and the sunnah manner of the pilgrim during wuquf, as well as the divine mercy of forgiveness sought on this day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the area of Arafat
Locate the valley of 'Arnah on the edge of Arafat. Understand that it is excluded from the valid standing area.
2
State the proof
Examine the hadith: 'Arafat is all a standing place, but avoid the valley of 'Arnah.' Note its source (Bukhari) and its explicit prohibition.
This is a dalil naqli, a text-based proof.
3
Contrast with Malik's view
Imam Malik permits standing there with a blood sacrifice. Understand the Hanafi response: the hadith is clear and the exception is disconnected (mursal).
This illustrates the difference in methodology.
4
Learn the sunnah actions during wuquf
The pilgrim should be engaged in praise, takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and du'a. Note that talbiyah continues until throwing the Jamrah, contrary to Malik's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
كيفية الحج
إلا بطن عرنة، حامداً مكبّراً مهلّلاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً، ثم إلى مزدلفة بعد الغروب، على النبي عليه السلام ماشيا على هينتك وانزل بقرب جبل قزح، وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة، ولم يجز المغرب في الطريق، ثم صل الفجر

شرح:
إلا بطن عرنة : لقوله عليه السلام: "عرفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة والمزدلفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر، وشعاب مكة كلها منحر"، رواه البخاري، وهو حجة على مالك في تجويزه الوقوف ببطن عرنة مع الدم [رمز الحقائق: ١٥٩/١] وعرنة بضم الأولى وفتح الثانية والاستثناء منقطع، وظاهر كلامهم أنه لو وقف بها لا يجزئه، ورأى النبي عليه الشيطان فيها وأمر أن لا يقف في ذلك المكان أحد احترازا عنه. (مسكين) عرنة: وهو واد بحذاء عرفات عن يسار الموقف. (ط) ملبيا أي في الموقف ساعة فساعة، وقال مالك: يقطع التلبية كما يقف بعرفة؛ لأن علياً قطعها فيه، وادعوا أنه مذهب أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان وعائشة، ولنا: ما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود له وحديث الفضل بن عباس لما أنه عليها لم يزل يلبي حتى رمى الجمرة العقبة"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وقوله: "مصلياً؛ لأن الصلاة وسيلة لإجابة الدعاء، وقوله: "داعياً"، أنه عليه السلام دعا لأمته بالمغفرة في عشية عرفة فاستجيب إلا في الدماء والمظالم، ثم أعاده بوقفة المزدلفة فاستجيب حتى في الدماء والمظالم، فعلم عدو الله إبليس بذلك فصار يحثو التراب على رأسه، وهو يدعو بالويل والثبور. وهذا ظاهر في أن الحج يكفر الصغائر والكبائر، لا فرق بين أن تكون حقاً الله أو للعبد، لكن المسألة ظنية ولا يقطع فيه بتكفير الكبائر من حقوق الله فضلاً عن حقوق العباد، وإن قلنا بالتكفير للكل فليس معناه أن الدين يسقط وكذا قضاء الصلاة والصوم والزكاة؛ إذ لم يقل أحد بذلك، وإنما المراد أن إثم الدين أي مطله وتأخيره يسقط، ثم بعد الوقوف بعرفة إذا مطل صار آلما الآن وكذا إثم تأخير الصلاة عن أوقاتها يرتفع بالحج لا القضاء، وذكر قاضي عياض أن أهل السنة أجمعوا على أن الكبائر لا يكفرها إلا التوبة. (فتح) داعياً ربك بحاجتك، وهذه الألفاظ كلها أحوال متداخلة أو مترادفة، وذو الحال الضمير في قوله: "قف". (ط،ع) مزدلفة هي من الزلفى، وهو القرب وإنما سمي بها؛ لأن آدم عليه السلام قرب فيها إلى حواء؛ أو لأنه يتقرب فيها إلى الله تعالى، وهي علم للبقعة لا يدخلها "ال" إلا لمحاً للصفة، ثم اعلم أن الرواح إليها ماشياً مستحب؛ لأنه عليه السلام لما أفاض من عرفات رأى أصحابه يتسارعون في السوق والمشي فقال عليه السلام: "ليس البر في إيجاف الخيل ولا في إيضاع الإبل، عليكم بالسكينة والوقار"، وقوله : "بعد الغروب" بيان للسنة حتى لو مكث بعد ما أفاض الإمام كثيرا بلا عذر أساء، ولو أبطأ الإمام ولم يفض حتى ظهر الليل أفاضوا؛ لأنه أخطأ السنة، ولو دفع قبله، فإن جاوز حدود عرفة لزمه دم ويقال للمزدلفة: جمع أيضاً، وقيل: المشعر الحرام. (فتح) بعد الغروب: أي غروب الشمس من يوم عرفة وجوبا، والمبيت بها سنة. (ع) وانزل بقرب إلخ: أي وقف فيه؛ لأنه هو الموقف؛ لما روي: "أنه عليه السلام لما أصبح وقف على قزح"، رواه أبو داود، و"قزح" بضم وفتح، الأصح أنه المشعر الحرام، وعليه ميقدة، قيل: هي کانون آدم عليه السلام، وفي "المطالع": أنه موقف قريش في الجاهلية؛ إذ كانوا لا يقفون بعرفة وإضافة جبل إليه بيانية مشتق من "قزح الشيء" = مشتقة
ثم إلى قزح، وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة، ولم يجز المغرب في الطريق، ثم صلّ الفجر

ثم شرح:
المغرب والعشاء واحد واحدة أي صلاة المغرب ولا في عرفات أي بعد ذلك أي ارتفع، وغير منصرف للعلمية والعدل؛ لأنه معدول عن قازح بمعنى مرتفع. (عيني، مسكين) قزح: عن يمين الطريق أو يساره، وقف فيه ندبا. (ع) العشائين: أي المغرب والعشاء في وقت العشاء جمع تأخير بشرط تقديم المغرب، فلو قدم العشاء يعيدها بعد المغرب، فإن لم يعد حتى طلع الفجر عادت جائزة. (ط) بأذان وإقامة : [واحدة ولا يتطوع بينهما ولا تشترط الجماعة هنا. (ط، ع)] وقال زفر والشافعي: بأذان وإقامتين، قياساً على الجمع الأول واختاره الطحاوي؛ لحديث جابر الله أنه عليه السلام صلاهما بأذان وإقامتين، رواه مسلم، وبه قال أحمد ومالك، وعنهم بأذانين أيضاً، ولنا حديث ابن عمر لهما أنه عليه السلام أذن للمغرب بجمع فأقام ثم صلى العشاء بالإقامة الأولى، قال ابن حزم رواه مسلم ويرجح هذا؛ لأن العشاء في وقته والقوم حضور فلا يحتاج إلى الإعلام، بخلاف عرفة، فإن العصر فيها في غير وقته، فلابد له من الإعلام بها [رمز الحقائق ١٥٩/١٢] ولا يتطوع بينهما؛ لأنه يخل بالجمع، ولو فعل أو اشتغل بشيء آخر أعاد الإقامة؛ لوقوع الفصل بينهما، وكان ينبغي أن يعيد الأذان كما في الجمع الأول، ولكنا اكتفينا بإعادة الإقامة؛ لما روي أنه عليه السلام صلى المغرب بمزدلفة ثم تعشى، ثم أفرد الإقامة للعشاء"، ولا يشترط الجماعة لهذا الجمع بل تستحب عند أبي حنيفة، وينبغي إحياء هذه الليلة. (مستخلص) في الطريق أي طريق المزدلفة، وكذا لو صلاها في عرفات، وقال أبو يوسف تجوز؛ لأنه صلاها في وقتها، وبه قال الشافعي، ولهما: حديث أسامة له أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم دفع من عرفة، حتى إذا كان بالشعب نزل فبال وتوضأ، ولم يسبغ الوضوء، قلت: الصلاة يا رسول الله ! فقال : الصلاة أمامك، فركب فلما جاء المزدلفة نزل فتوضأ فأسبغ الوضوء، (الحديث) [رواه البخاري ومسلم]، ومعنى: "الصلاة أمامك" أي وقت الصلاة؛ لأن الصلاة حركات توجد من المصلي، فلا توصف بالقبلية قبل الوجود، وعند الوجود لا يكون أمامه، وقيل: معناه المصلى أمامك، أي مكان الصلاة والحاصل: إن كان المراد به الوقت يظهر أن وقت المغرب في حق الحاج لا يدخل بغروب الشمس، وأداء الصلاة قبل الوقت لا يجوز، وإن كان المراد به المكان يظهر اختصاص هذه الصلاة بالمكان وهو المزدلفة فلا يجوز في غيرها إلا أن خبر الواحد يوجب العمل لا العلم، فأمر بالإعادة ما بقي الوقت؛ ليصير جامعاً بين الصلاتين بالمزدلفة. (مستخلص، فتح عيني)
ثم صل الفجر: لما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود له أنه عليه السلام صلاها يومئذ بغلس، متفق عليه، ولأن في التغليس دفع حاجة الوقوف فيجوز، كتقديم العصر بعرفة بل أولى؛ لأنه في وقته [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٩٨/٢] "والغلس" بالمعجمة واللام المفتوحتين ظلمة آخر الليل، والمراد طلوع الفجر الثاني من غير تأخير قبل زوال الظلمة وانتشار الضياء، وقوله: "ثم قف" أي بمزدلفة، والوقوف بها واجب، حتى لو ترك بلا عذر يجب الدم، وعند الشافعي: ركن؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُمْ مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ (البقرة:۱۹۸)، ولحديث عروة أنه عليه السلام قال: "من وقف معنا هذا الموقف وقد كان أفاض من عرفات قبل ذلك فقد تم حجه"، علق به تمام الحج وهو.
Book of Hajj. How to perform Hajj: Except the valley of 'Arnah, praising, magnifying, saying 'la ilaha illa Allah', saying talbiyah, sending peace on the Prophet, supplicating. Then to Muzdalifah after sunset, walking calmly, dismount near Mount Qazh, lead the people in the two evening prayers with one adhan and one iqamah, and do not pray Maghrib on the way. Then pray Fajr. Commentary: 'Except the valley of 'Arnah' due to the Prophet's saying: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Arnah; all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir; and all the passes of Mecca are sacrificing places' narrated by Bukhari, which is proof against Malik who permits standing in Batn 'Arnah with a blood sacrifice. 'Arnah (with damma on first and fatha on second) is a valley adjacent to Arafat to the left of the standing place. (T) 'Saying talbiyah' means in the standing place time after time. Malik says: stop talbiyah when you stand at Arafat because Ali stopped it there, and they claim it is the madhhab of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Aisha. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the hadith of al-Fadl ibn Abbas that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he threw the Jamrat al-Aqabah, narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. 'Sending peace on the Prophet' because prayer is a means for the acceptance of supplication. 'Supplicating' because the Prophet supplicated for his ummah on the evening of Arafat and it was granted except for blood debts and injustices, then he repeated it at the standing of Muzdalifah and it was granted even for blood debts and injustices, so the enemy of Allah Iblis knew and began throwing dust on his head in despair. This indicates that Hajj expiates minor and major sins, whether rights of Allah or of people, but the matter is speculative and one cannot be certain about expiation of major sins of Allah's rights let alone people's rights. If we say expiation for all, it does not mean that debt is dropped nor the making up of prayer, fasting, zakat, no one says that. The meaning is that the sin of delaying debt is dropped. Qadi 'Iyad said the Ahl al-Sunnah are agreed that only repentance expiates major sins. (Fath) 'Supplicating your Lord for your need.' All these words are overlapping or synonymous states, the subject of the state is the pronoun in 'stand'. (T, A) Muzdalifah is from 'zulfa' meaning nearness, named because Adam drew near to Eve there, or because one draws near to Allah there. It is a proper noun for the place, definite article is used only by way of description. Know that going there walking is recommended because the Prophet said: 'Righteousness is not in racing horses or camels, be tranquil and dignified.' His saying 'after sunset' is a statement of the sunnah; if one delays much after the imam has departed without excuse, he does wrong; if the imam delays and does not depart until night appears, they depart because he missed the sunnah; if he departs before and goes beyond the boundaries of Arafat, he must offer blood. Muzdalifah is also called Jam' and Mash'ar al-Haram. (Fath) 'After sunset' means sunset on the day of Arafat, obligatorily, and staying overnight there is sunnah. (A) 'Dismount near' etc.: stand there because it is the standing place; as reported that the Prophet in the morning stood at Qazh (narrated by Abu Dawud). Qazh (with damma and fatha) is, according to the most correct view, the Mash'ar al-Haram, and on it is a beacon, said to be the oven of Adam. In al-Matali', it was the standing place of Quraysh in Jahiliyyah as they did not stand at Arafat. Then to Qazh, lead the people in the two evening prayers with one adhan and one iqamah, and do not pray Maghrib on the way, then pray Fajr. Commentary: The two prayers Maghrib and Isha are combined one after the other, meaning do not pray Maghrib on the way nor in Arafat. Qazh is non-declinable due to being proper noun and with an implied meaning; it is derived from 'qaziha' meaning high. (Ayni, Miskin) Qazh is on the right or left of the road, stand there recommendedly. (A) 'The two evenings' means Maghrib and Isha at the time of Isha, delaying the combination with the condition of praying Maghrib first. If one prays Isha first, he must repeat it after Maghrib; if he does not repeat until Fajr, it is valid. (T) 'With one adhan and one iqamah': no supererogatory prayers between them and congregation is not a condition. Zufar and al-Shafi'i say: with two adhans and two iqamahs, by analogy to the first combination (at Arafat), and al-Tahawi preferred it due to the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet prayed them with one adhan and two iqamahs (narrated by Muslim), and Ahmad and Malik also said that, and some report two adhans. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet gave adhan for Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then iqamah, then prayed Isha with the first iqamah. Ibn Hazm said Muslim narrated it and this is preponderant because Isha is in its time and the people are present so no need for announcement, unlike Arafat where Asr is not in its time so announcement is needed. There is no supererogatory prayer between them because it disrupts the combination; if one does it or engages in something else, he must repeat the iqamah due to the separation, and it would be appropriate to repeat the adhan as in the first combination, but we suffice with iqamah because it is reported that the Prophet prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah then ate supper, then gave iqamah for Isha alone. Congregation for this combination is not a condition but recommended according to Abu Hanifa, and one should revive this night. (Mustakhlas) 'In the road' means the road to Muzdalifah, similarly if he prays it in Arafat. Abu Yusuf says it is permissible because he prayed it in its time, and al-Shafi'i also said so. Their proof is the hadith of Usama that the Prophet departed from Arafat until when he was at the mountain pass, he dismounted, urinated, performed wudu imperfectly. I said: 'Prayer, O Messenger of Allah!' He said: 'The prayer is ahead of you.' He rode until he came to Muzdalifah, dismounted, performed wudu thoroughly. The meaning of 'the prayer is ahead of you' is the time of prayer; because prayer is actions of the worshipper, it cannot be described as ahead before existence; or it means the place of prayer. If the meaning is time, it shows that the time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not enter at sunset, and performing prayer before its time is not allowed. If the meaning is place, it shows the restriction of this prayer to Muzdalifah, so it is not valid elsewhere. But the single-narrator hadith requires action not certainty, so the command to repeat while time remains is to combine the two prayers at Muzdalifah. (Mustakhlas, Fath al-Qadir) 'Then pray Fajr': due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet prayed it that day at pre-dawn darkness (ghalas), agreed upon. And because praying at that time helps to hasten the standing, so it is permissible, like advancing Asr at Arafat, even more so because it is in its time. 'Ghalas' with mu'jama and fatha of lam means darkness at the end of the night; the meaning is to pray at the break of true dawn without delay before the darkness disappears and light spreads. His saying 'then stand' at Muzdalifah, and standing there is obligatory; if one leaves it without excuse, blood is due. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a pillar due to the verse 'And when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (2:198) and the hadith of Urwa: 'Whoever stands with us this standing after having departed from Arafat before that, his Hajj is complete.' He made the completion of Hajj conditional upon it.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the actions of Hajj from standing at Arafat to Muzdalifah. It begins by stating the sunnah manner of wuquf: the pilgrim should be in a state of praise, takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and du'a. The place of standing is any part of Arafat except the valley of 'Arnah, based on a sahih hadith. This refutes Imam Malik who allowed standing there with a compensation. The Hanafi position is that standing at Batn 'Arnah invalidates the wuquf. The pilgrim should continuously recite talbiyah until throwing the Jamrah, contrary to Malik's view that it stops at Arafat. The commentary then discusses the du'a of the Prophet at Arafat and Muzdalifah, and the forgiveness of sins, noting that while Hajj expiates sins, major sins require repentance according to Ahl al-Sunnah. After sunset, the pilgrim proceeds to Muzdalifah, walking calmly, dismounting near Mount Qazh (the Mash'ar al-Haram). There, the imam leads the Maghrib and Isha prayers in combination at the time of Isha, with one adhan and one iqamah. The Hanafi school holds this view, opposing Zufar, Shafi'i, and others who require two adhans/iqamahs. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar. Maghrib must not be prayed on the way or at Arafat, as per the hadith of Usama; the Prophet delayed it until Muzdalifah. The next morning, Fajr is prayed at early dawn (ghalas), and then the pilgrim stands at Muzdalifah. This standing is wajib according to the Hanafis, not rukn as Shafi'i holds, based on the verse and hadith. Missing it without excuse requires a blood sacrifice.

Key Terms
عرنة ('Arnah): A valley adjacent to Arafat to the left of the standing place; standing there is prohibited.
ملبيا (mulabbiyan): Engaging in talbiyah, the recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...'
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The prescribed chant for the pilgrim entering ihram, recited aloud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on standing at Batn 'Arnah?
A) Permissible without compensation
B) Permissible with blood sacrifice
C) Invalid, compensation required
D) Invalid, wuquf must be repeated

Key Takeaway
The valley of 'Arnah is excluded from the valid standing area at Arafat; standing there invalidates wuquf according to the Hanafi school.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
The Rulings of Muzdalifah: Combining Prayers and Wuquf
Sharh expanding on the actions at Muzdalifah, including prayer combination and wuquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the combination of Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, identify the dispute over adhan and iqamah, and state the wajib status of wuquf at Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah, and know that standing there is wajib, not a pillar.

After standing at Arafat, the pilgrim proceeds to Muzdalifah for the night. The Hanafi school prescribes a particular method for the combined prayers and emphasizes that standing at Muzdalifah is a wajib act, with a blood sacrifice required if missed. This lesson covers the proofs and the disputes with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Travel to Muzdalifah
After sunset on the day of Arafat, proceed to Muzdalifah calmly. It is recommended to walk and dismount near Mount Qazh (Mash'ar al-Haram).
2
Understand the combination of prayers
Maghrib and Isha are prayed together at the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. No supererogatory prayers between them.
This is the Hanafi view; other schools use two iqamahs.
3
Analyze the adhan/iqamah dispute
Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and others use two iqamahs based on the hadith of Jabir. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar. Note the reasoning: since Isha is in its time, no need for extra announcement.
4
Recognize the ruling on wuquf at Muzdalifah
After Fajr prayer at early dawn (ghalas), stand at Muzdalifah. This standing is wajib according to Hanafis; missing it without excuse requires a blood sacrifice. Al-Shafi'i considers it a rukn.
The proof is the verse 'remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' and the hadith of Urwa.
5
Note the timing of Fajr
Pray Fajr at ghalas (pre-dawn darkness) to allow more time for standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
كيفية الحج
إلا بطن عرنة، حامداً مكبّراً مهلّلاً ملبياً مصلياً داعياً، ثم إلى مزدلفة بعد الغروب، على النبي عليه السلام ماشيا على هينتك وانزل بقرب جبل قزح، وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة، ولم يجز المغرب في الطريق، ثم صل الفجر

شرح:
إلا بطن عرنة : لقوله عليه السلام: "عرفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة والمزدلفة كلها موقف وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر، وشعاب مكة كلها منحر"، رواه البخاري، وهو حجة على مالك في تجويزه الوقوف ببطن عرنة مع الدم [رمز الحقائق: ١٥٩/١] وعرنة بضم الأولى وفتح الثانية والاستثناء منقطع، وظاهر كلامهم أنه لو وقف بها لا يجزئه، ورأى النبي عليه الشيطان فيها وأمر أن لا يقف في ذلك المكان أحد احترازا عنه. (مسكين) عرنة: وهو واد بحذاء عرفات عن يسار الموقف. (ط) ملبيا أي في الموقف ساعة فساعة، وقال مالك: يقطع التلبية كما يقف بعرفة؛ لأن علياً قطعها فيه، وادعوا أنه مذهب أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان وعائشة، ولنا: ما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود له وحديث الفضل بن عباس لما أنه عليها لم يزل يلبي حتى رمى الجمرة العقبة"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وقوله: "مصلياً؛ لأن الصلاة وسيلة لإجابة الدعاء، وقوله: "داعياً"، أنه عليه السلام دعا لأمته بالمغفرة في عشية عرفة فاستجيب إلا في الدماء والمظالم، ثم أعاده بوقفة المزدلفة فاستجيب حتى في الدماء والمظالم، فعلم عدو الله إبليس بذلك فصار يحثو التراب على رأسه، وهو يدعو بالويل والثبور. وهذا ظاهر في أن الحج يكفر الصغائر والكبائر، لا فرق بين أن تكون حقاً الله أو للعبد، لكن المسألة ظنية ولا يقطع فيه بتكفير الكبائر من حقوق الله فضلاً عن حقوق العباد، وإن قلنا بالتكفير للكل فليس معناه أن الدين يسقط وكذا قضاء الصلاة والصوم والزكاة؛ إذ لم يقل أحد بذلك، وإنما المراد أن إثم الدين أي مطله وتأخيره يسقط، ثم بعد الوقوف بعرفة إذا مطل صار آلما الآن وكذا إثم تأخير الصلاة عن أوقاتها يرتفع بالحج لا القضاء، وذكر قاضي عياض أن أهل السنة أجمعوا على أن الكبائر لا يكفرها إلا التوبة. (فتح) داعياً ربك بحاجتك، وهذه الألفاظ كلها أحوال متداخلة أو مترادفة، وذو الحال الضمير في قوله: "قف". (ط،ع) مزدلفة هي من الزلفى، وهو القرب وإنما سمي بها؛ لأن آدم عليه السلام قرب فيها إلى حواء؛ أو لأنه يتقرب فيها إلى الله تعالى، وهي علم للبقعة لا يدخلها "ال" إلا لمحاً للصفة، ثم اعلم أن الرواح إليها ماشياً مستحب؛ لأنه عليه السلام لما أفاض من عرفات رأى أصحابه يتسارعون في السوق والمشي فقال عليه السلام: "ليس البر في إيجاف الخيل ولا في إيضاع الإبل، عليكم بالسكينة والوقار"، وقوله : "بعد الغروب" بيان للسنة حتى لو مكث بعد ما أفاض الإمام كثيرا بلا عذر أساء، ولو أبطأ الإمام ولم يفض حتى ظهر الليل أفاضوا؛ لأنه أخطأ السنة، ولو دفع قبله، فإن جاوز حدود عرفة لزمه دم ويقال للمزدلفة: جمع أيضاً، وقيل: المشعر الحرام. (فتح) بعد الغروب: أي غروب الشمس من يوم عرفة وجوبا، والمبيت بها سنة. (ع) وانزل بقرب إلخ: أي وقف فيه؛ لأنه هو الموقف؛ لما روي: "أنه عليه السلام لما أصبح وقف على قزح"، رواه أبو داود، و"قزح" بضم وفتح، الأصح أنه المشعر الحرام، وعليه ميقدة، قيل: هي کانون آدم عليه السلام، وفي "المطالع": أنه موقف قريش في الجاهلية؛ إذ كانوا لا يقفون بعرفة وإضافة جبل إليه بيانية مشتق من "قزح الشيء" = مشتقة
ثم إلى قزح، وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة، ولم يجز المغرب في الطريق، ثم صلّ الفجر

ثم شرح:
المغرب والعشاء واحد واحدة أي صلاة المغرب ولا في عرفات أي بعد ذلك أي ارتفع، وغير منصرف للعلمية والعدل؛ لأنه معدول عن قازح بمعنى مرتفع. (عيني، مسكين) قزح: عن يمين الطريق أو يساره، وقف فيه ندبا. (ع) العشائين: أي المغرب والعشاء في وقت العشاء جمع تأخير بشرط تقديم المغرب، فلو قدم العشاء يعيدها بعد المغرب، فإن لم يعد حتى طلع الفجر عادت جائزة. (ط) بأذان وإقامة : [واحدة ولا يتطوع بينهما ولا تشترط الجماعة هنا. (ط، ع)] وقال زفر والشافعي: بأذان وإقامتين، قياساً على الجمع الأول واختاره الطحاوي؛ لحديث جابر الله أنه عليه السلام صلاهما بأذان وإقامتين، رواه مسلم، وبه قال أحمد ومالك، وعنهم بأذانين أيضاً، ولنا حديث ابن عمر لهما أنه عليه السلام أذن للمغرب بجمع فأقام ثم صلى العشاء بالإقامة الأولى، قال ابن حزم رواه مسلم ويرجح هذا؛ لأن العشاء في وقته والقوم حضور فلا يحتاج إلى الإعلام، بخلاف عرفة، فإن العصر فيها في غير وقته، فلابد له من الإعلام بها [رمز الحقائق ١٥٩/١٢] ولا يتطوع بينهما؛ لأنه يخل بالجمع، ولو فعل أو اشتغل بشيء آخر أعاد الإقامة؛ لوقوع الفصل بينهما، وكان ينبغي أن يعيد الأذان كما في الجمع الأول، ولكنا اكتفينا بإعادة الإقامة؛ لما روي أنه عليه السلام صلى المغرب بمزدلفة ثم تعشى، ثم أفرد الإقامة للعشاء"، ولا يشترط الجماعة لهذا الجمع بل تستحب عند أبي حنيفة، وينبغي إحياء هذه الليلة. (مستخلص) في الطريق أي طريق المزدلفة، وكذا لو صلاها في عرفات، وقال أبو يوسف تجوز؛ لأنه صلاها في وقتها، وبه قال الشافعي، ولهما: حديث أسامة له أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم دفع من عرفة، حتى إذا كان بالشعب نزل فبال وتوضأ، ولم يسبغ الوضوء، قلت: الصلاة يا رسول الله ! فقال : الصلاة أمامك، فركب فلما جاء المزدلفة نزل فتوضأ فأسبغ الوضوء، (الحديث) [رواه البخاري ومسلم]، ومعنى: "الصلاة أمامك" أي وقت الصلاة؛ لأن الصلاة حركات توجد من المصلي، فلا توصف بالقبلية قبل الوجود، وعند الوجود لا يكون أمامه، وقيل: معناه المصلى أمامك، أي مكان الصلاة والحاصل: إن كان المراد به الوقت يظهر أن وقت المغرب في حق الحاج لا يدخل بغروب الشمس، وأداء الصلاة قبل الوقت لا يجوز، وإن كان المراد به المكان يظهر اختصاص هذه الصلاة بالمكان وهو المزدلفة فلا يجوز في غيرها إلا أن خبر الواحد يوجب العمل لا العلم، فأمر بالإعادة ما بقي الوقت؛ ليصير جامعاً بين الصلاتين بالمزدلفة. (مستخلص، فتح عيني)
ثم صل الفجر: لما روينا من حديث ابن مسعود له أنه عليه السلام صلاها يومئذ بغلس، متفق عليه، ولأن في التغليس دفع حاجة الوقوف فيجوز، كتقديم العصر بعرفة بل أولى؛ لأنه في وقته [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٩٨/٢] "والغلس" بالمعجمة واللام المفتوحتين ظلمة آخر الليل، والمراد طلوع الفجر الثاني من غير تأخير قبل زوال الظلمة وانتشار الضياء، وقوله: "ثم قف" أي بمزدلفة، والوقوف بها واجب، حتى لو ترك بلا عذر يجب الدم، وعند الشافعي: ركن؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُمْ مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ عِنْدَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ (البقرة:۱۹۸)، ولحديث عروة أنه عليه السلام قال: "من وقف معنا هذا الموقف وقد كان أفاض من عرفات قبل ذلك فقد تم حجه"، علق به تمام الحج وهو.
Book of Hajj. How to perform Hajj: Except the valley of 'Arnah, praising, magnifying, saying 'la ilaha illa Allah', saying talbiyah, sending peace on the Prophet, supplicating. Then to Muzdalifah after sunset, walking calmly, dismount near Mount Qazh, lead the people in the two evening prayers with one adhan and one iqamah, and do not pray Maghrib on the way. Then pray Fajr. Commentary: 'Except the valley of 'Arnah' due to the Prophet's saying: 'All of Arafat is a standing place, and avoid the valley of 'Arnah; all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid the valley of Muhassir; and all the passes of Mecca are sacrificing places' narrated by Bukhari, which is proof against Malik who permits standing in Batn 'Arnah with a blood sacrifice. 'Arnah (with damma on first and fatha on second) is a valley adjacent to Arafat to the left of the standing place. (T) 'Saying talbiyah' means in the standing place time after time. Malik says: stop talbiyah when you stand at Arafat because Ali stopped it there, and they claim it is the madhhab of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Aisha. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the hadith of al-Fadl ibn Abbas that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he threw the Jamrat al-Aqabah, narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. 'Sending peace on the Prophet' because prayer is a means for the acceptance of supplication. 'Supplicating' because the Prophet supplicated for his ummah on the evening of Arafat and it was granted except for blood debts and injustices, then he repeated it at the standing of Muzdalifah and it was granted even for blood debts and injustices, so the enemy of Allah Iblis knew and began throwing dust on his head in despair. This indicates that Hajj expiates minor and major sins, whether rights of Allah or of people, but the matter is speculative and one cannot be certain about expiation of major sins of Allah's rights let alone people's rights. If we say expiation for all, it does not mean that debt is dropped nor the making up of prayer, fasting, zakat, no one says that. The meaning is that the sin of delaying debt is dropped. Qadi 'Iyad said the Ahl al-Sunnah are agreed that only repentance expiates major sins. (Fath) 'Supplicating your Lord for your need.' All these words are overlapping or synonymous states, the subject of the state is the pronoun in 'stand'. (T, A) Muzdalifah is from 'zulfa' meaning nearness, named because Adam drew near to Eve there, or because one draws near to Allah there. It is a proper noun for the place, definite article is used only by way of description. Know that going there walking is recommended because the Prophet said: 'Righteousness is not in racing horses or camels, be tranquil and dignified.' His saying 'after sunset' is a statement of the sunnah; if one delays much after the imam has departed without excuse, he does wrong; if the imam delays and does not depart until night appears, they depart because he missed the sunnah; if he departs before and goes beyond the boundaries of Arafat, he must offer blood. Muzdalifah is also called Jam' and Mash'ar al-Haram. (Fath) 'After sunset' means sunset on the day of Arafat, obligatorily, and staying overnight there is sunnah. (A) 'Dismount near' etc.: stand there because it is the standing place; as reported that the Prophet in the morning stood at Qazh (narrated by Abu Dawud). Qazh (with damma and fatha) is, according to the most correct view, the Mash'ar al-Haram, and on it is a beacon, said to be the oven of Adam. In al-Matali', it was the standing place of Quraysh in Jahiliyyah as they did not stand at Arafat. Then to Qazh, lead the people in the two evening prayers with one adhan and one iqamah, and do not pray Maghrib on the way, then pray Fajr. Commentary: The two prayers Maghrib and Isha are combined one after the other, meaning do not pray Maghrib on the way nor in Arafat. Qazh is non-declinable due to being proper noun and with an implied meaning; it is derived from 'qaziha' meaning high. (Ayni, Miskin) Qazh is on the right or left of the road, stand there recommendedly. (A) 'The two evenings' means Maghrib and Isha at the time of Isha, delaying the combination with the condition of praying Maghrib first. If one prays Isha first, he must repeat it after Maghrib; if he does not repeat until Fajr, it is valid. (T) 'With one adhan and one iqamah': no supererogatory prayers between them and congregation is not a condition. Zufar and al-Shafi'i say: with two adhans and two iqamahs, by analogy to the first combination (at Arafat), and al-Tahawi preferred it due to the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet prayed them with one adhan and two iqamahs (narrated by Muslim), and Ahmad and Malik also said that, and some report two adhans. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet gave adhan for Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then iqamah, then prayed Isha with the first iqamah. Ibn Hazm said Muslim narrated it and this is preponderant because Isha is in its time and the people are present so no need for announcement, unlike Arafat where Asr is not in its time so announcement is needed. There is no supererogatory prayer between them because it disrupts the combination; if one does it or engages in something else, he must repeat the iqamah due to the separation, and it would be appropriate to repeat the adhan as in the first combination, but we suffice with iqamah because it is reported that the Prophet prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah then ate supper, then gave iqamah for Isha alone. Congregation for this combination is not a condition but recommended according to Abu Hanifa, and one should revive this night. (Mustakhlas) 'In the road' means the road to Muzdalifah, similarly if he prays it in Arafat. Abu Yusuf says it is permissible because he prayed it in its time, and al-Shafi'i also said so. Their proof is the hadith of Usama that the Prophet departed from Arafat until when he was at the mountain pass, he dismounted, urinated, performed wudu imperfectly. I said: 'Prayer, O Messenger of Allah!' He said: 'The prayer is ahead of you.' He rode until he came to Muzdalifah, dismounted, performed wudu thoroughly. The meaning of 'the prayer is ahead of you' is the time of prayer; because prayer is actions of the worshipper, it cannot be described as ahead before existence; or it means the place of prayer. If the meaning is time, it shows that the time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not enter at sunset, and performing prayer before its time is not allowed. If the meaning is place, it shows the restriction of this prayer to Muzdalifah, so it is not valid elsewhere. But the single-narrator hadith requires action not certainty, so the command to repeat while time remains is to combine the two prayers at Muzdalifah. (Mustakhlas, Fath al-Qadir) 'Then pray Fajr': due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet prayed it that day at pre-dawn darkness (ghalas), agreed upon. And because praying at that time helps to hasten the standing, so it is permissible, like advancing Asr at Arafat, even more so because it is in its time. 'Ghalas' with mu'jama and fatha of lam means darkness at the end of the night; the meaning is to pray at the break of true dawn without delay before the darkness disappears and light spreads. His saying 'then stand' at Muzdalifah, and standing there is obligatory; if one leaves it without excuse, blood is due. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a pillar due to the verse 'And when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (2:198) and the hadith of Urwa: 'Whoever stands with us this standing after having departed from Arafat before that, his Hajj is complete.' He made the completion of Hajj conditional upon it.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the actions of Hajj from standing at Arafat to Muzdalifah. It begins by stating the sunnah manner of wuquf: the pilgrim should be in a state of praise, takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, salawat, and du'a. The place of standing is any part of Arafat except the valley of 'Arnah, based on a sahih hadith. This refutes Imam Malik who allowed standing there with a compensation. The Hanafi position is that standing at Batn 'Arnah invalidates the wuquf. The pilgrim should continuously recite talbiyah until throwing the Jamrah, contrary to Malik's view that it stops at Arafat. The commentary then discusses the du'a of the Prophet at Arafat and Muzdalifah, and the forgiveness of sins, noting that while Hajj expiates sins, major sins require repentance according to Ahl al-Sunnah. After sunset, the pilgrim proceeds to Muzdalifah, walking calmly, dismounting near Mount Qazh (the Mash'ar al-Haram). There, the imam leads the Maghrib and Isha prayers in combination at the time of Isha, with one adhan and one iqamah. The Hanafi school holds this view, opposing Zufar, Shafi'i, and others who require two adhans/iqamahs. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar. Maghrib must not be prayed on the way or at Arafat, as per the hadith of Usama; the Prophet delayed it until Muzdalifah. The next morning, Fajr is prayed at early dawn (ghalas), and then the pilgrim stands at Muzdalifah. This standing is wajib according to the Hanafis, not rukn as Shafi'i holds, based on the verse and hadith. Missing it without excuse requires a blood sacrifice.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina; named from 'zulfa' (nearness); the site of the combined Maghrib and Isha prayers and the obligatory standing after Fajr.
قزح (Qazh): The mountain at Muzdalifah where the imam stands; also called Mash'ar al-Haram.
العشائين (al-'Isha'ayn): The two evening prayers: Maghrib and Isha, combined at Muzdalifah.
غلس (ghalas): The darkness before dawn; the preferred time to pray Fajr at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the number of adhans and iqamahs for Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah?
A) One adhan and two iqamahs
B) Two adhans and two iqamahs
C) One adhan and one iqamah
D) Two adhans and one iqamah

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqamah, pray Fajr early, and stand there—it is wajib, not a rukn.

Combined Prayers at Muzdalifah: One Adhan and One Iqamah
Ruling on the number of adhans and iqamahs for combined prayer at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of adhans and iqamahs for the combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and explain the evidence.

Core Idea
One adhan and one iqamah suffice because Isha is in its time and the congregation is gathered.

The combined prayer at Muzdalifah is a distinctive sunnah of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that a single adhan and iqamah are sufficient, based on the explicit practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Ibn Umar. This lesson explores the evidence and addresses the disagreement with other scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah with one adhan and one iqamah.
The combination is a delayed jam‘ (jam‘ ta’khīr).
2
State the Hanafi proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave the adhan for Maghrib, then the iqamah, then prayed Isha with the same iqamah (hadith of Ibn Umar). This shows one iqamah suffices.
Narrated by Muslim; Ibn Hazm considered it preponderant.
3
Examine the opposing view
Zufar and al-Shafi‘i argue for two adhans and two iqamahs, by analogy to the combination at Arafat and the hadith of Jabir.
Opponents also cite the practice of Ahmad and Malik.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
At Muzdalifah, Isha is prayed in its proper time and the people are already gathered, so a second notification is unnecessary. This contrasts with Arafat where Asr is out of its time.
The principle of necessity (ḥājah) supports the single call.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قُزح، وصل بالناس العشائين بأذان وإقامة، ولم يجز المغرب في الطريق. أي صلاة المغرب ولا في عرفات أي بعد ذلك - أي ارتفع، وغير منصرف للعلمية والعدل؛ لأنه معدول عن قازح بمعنى مرتفع. (عيني، مسكين) قزح: عن يمين الطريق أو يساره، وقف فيه ندبا. (ع) العشائين: أي المغرب والعشاء في وقت العشاء جمع تأخير بشرط تقديم المغرب، فلو قدم العشاء يعيدها بعد المغرب، فإن لم يعد حتى طلع الفجر عادت جائزة. (ط) بأذان وإقامة : [واحدة ولا يتطوع بينهما ولا تشترط الجماعة هنا. (ط، ع)] وقال زفر والشافعي: بأذان وإقامتين، قياساً على الجمع الأول واختاره الطحاوي؛ لحديث جابر الله أنه عليه صلاهما بأذان وإقامتين، رواه مسلم، وبه قال أحمد ومالك، وعنهم بأذانين أيضاً، ولنا حديث ابن عمر لهما أنه عليه أذن للمغرب بجمع فأقام ثم صلى العشاء بالإقامة الأولى، قال ابن حزم رواه مسلم ويرجح . هذا؛ لأن العشاء في وقته والقوم حضور فلا يحتاج إلى الإعلام، بخلاف عرفة، فإن العصر فيها في غير وقته، فلابد له من الإعلام بها رمز الحقائق ١٥٩/١٢] ولا يتطوع بينهما؛ لأنه يخل بالجمع، ولو فعل أو اشتغل بشيء آخر أعاد الإقامة؛ لوقوع الفصل بينهما، وكان ينبغي أن يعيد الأذان كما في الجمع الأول، ولكنا اكتفينا بإعادة الإقامة؛ لما روي أنه عليه صلى المغرب بمزدلفة ثم تعشى، ثم أفرد الإقامة للعشاء"، ولا يشترط الجماعة لهذا الجمع بل تستحب عند أبي حنيفة، وينبغي إحياء هذه الليلة. (مستخلص) في الطريق أي طريق المزدلفة، وكذا لو صلاها في عرفات، وقال أبو يوسف تجوز؛ لأنه صلاها في وقتها، وبه قال الشافعي، ولهما: حديث أسامة له أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم دفع من عرفة، حتى إذا كان بالشعب نزل فبال وتوضأ، ولم يسبغ الوضوء، قلت: الصلاة يا رسول الله ! فقال : الصلاة أمامك، فركب فلما جاء المزدلفة نزل فتوضأ فأسبغ الوضوء، (الحديث) [رواه البخاري ومسلم]، ومعنى: "الصلاة أمامك" أي وقت الصلاة؛ لأن الصلاة حركات توجد من المصلي، فلا توصف بالقبلية قبل الوجود، وعند الوجود لا يكون أمامه، وقيل: معناه المصلى أمامك، أي مكان الصلاة والحاصل: إن كان المراد به الوقت يظهر أن وقت المغرب في حق الحاج لا يدخل بغروب الشمس، وأداء الصلاة قبل الوقت لا يجوز، وإن كان المراد به المكان يظهر اختصاص هذه الصلاة بالمكان وهو المزدلفة فلا يجوز في غيرها إلا أن خبر الواحد يوجب العمل لا العلم، فأمر بالإعادة ما بقي الوقت؛ ليصير جامعاً . بين الصلاتين بالمزدلفة. (مستخلص، فتح عيني)
At Muzdalifah, he led the people in the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha) with one adhan and one iqamah, and he did not pray Maghrib on the way. Meaning: the prayer of Maghrib [was not performed] nor at Arafat, meaning after that. [قزح] is a place on the right or left of the road; it is recommended to stop there. (Al-Ayni, Miskin) The two evening prayers mean Maghrib and Isha at the time of Isha as a delayed combination, with the condition of performing Maghrib first. If one performs Isha first, he must repeat it after Maghrib; if he does not repeat until dawn, it becomes permissible. (T) With one adhan and iqamah: one, and no voluntary prayer is offered between them, and congregation is not required here. (T, A) Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: with two adhans and two iqamahs, by analogy to the first combination (at Arafat), and al-Tahawi chose it due to the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed them with one adhan and two iqamahs, narrated by Muslim, and Ahmad and Malik also held this, and from them also two adhans. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave the adhan for Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then performed the iqamah, then prayed Isha with the first iqamah. Ibn Hazm said it was narrated by Muslim and is preponderant. This is because Isha is in its time and the people are present, so notification is not needed, unlike Arafat where Asr is not in its time, so notification is necessary. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/159) No voluntary prayer is offered between them because it disrupts the combination. If one does so or occupies himself with something else, he must repeat the iqamah due to the separation; it would be fitting to repeat the adhan as in the first combination, but we sufficed with repeating the iqamah because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Maghrib at Muzdalifah, then had dinner, then gave the iqamah alone for Isha. Congregation is not required for this combination but is recommended according to Abu Hanifah. It is recommended to revive this night. (Mukhtasar) 'On the way' means the road to Muzdalifah, and likewise if he prayed it at Arafat. Abu Yusuf said it is permissible because he prayed it in its time, and al-Shafi'i agreed. Their proof is the hadith of Usamah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) departed from Arafat until when he was at the mountain pass, he dismounted, urinated, and performed wudu without doing it thoroughly. I said, 'Prayer, O Messenger of Allah!' He said, 'Prayer is ahead of you.' He rode, and when he came to Muzdalifah, he dismounted, performed wudu properly, [then the hadith]. The meaning of 'Prayer is ahead of you' is the time of prayer, because prayer is actions performed by the worshipper, so it cannot be described as 'ahead' before its existence, and when it exists it is not ahead. It is also said it means the place of prayer. The conclusion: if it means time, it shows that the time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not enter at sunset, and performing the prayer before its time is not permissible. If it means place, it shows that this prayer is specific to the place, which is Muzdalifah, so it is not permissible elsewhere except that a report of a single narrator necessitates action, not knowledge, so he ordered repetition as long as time remained to achieve the combination of the two prayers at Muzdalifah. (Mukhtasar, Fath al-Ayni)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the rulings for the combined Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. It is a ruling with proof, presenting the Hanafi position alongside a dispute with Zufar and al-Shafi'i. The text begins by stating the basic rule: the Prophet (peace be upon him) led the people in the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha) at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah, and he did not pray Maghrib on the way. The commentary clarifies that 'Muzdalifah' is a place, and it is recommended to stop there. It then defines 'the two evening prayers' as Maghrib and Isha performed at Isha time as a delayed combination (jam' ta'khir), with the condition that Maghrib must be prayed first. The main dispute concerns the number of adhans and iqamahs: the Hanafi school holds that one adhan and one iqamah suffice, based on a hadith of Ibn Umar, while Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue for two adhans and two iqamahs by analogy to the combination at Arafat, citing a hadith of Jabir. The Hanafi response explains that because Isha is in its time and the people are already gathered, a second adhan is unnecessary, unlike at Arafat where Asr is performed out of its time. Additionally, no voluntary prayer is offered between them, and if one does engage in something, the iqamah must be repeated. Congregation is recommended, not required. The discussion also addresses the ruling on praying Maghrib on the way: it is not permissible to pray Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah, as the time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not begin at sunset; it only begins at Muzdalifah. This is supported by the hadith of Usamah, where the Prophet said 'Prayer is ahead of you,' understood as referring to either time or place. The Hanafi position is that if one prays before arrival, it is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Terms
العشائين (al-‘ishā’ayn): The two evening prayers: Maghrib and Isha.
جمع تأخير (jam‘ ta’khīr): Delaying the first prayer (Maghrib) to the time of the second (Isha) and performing them together.
أذان (adhān): The call to prayer announcing the time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis use one adhan and one iqamah for the combined prayer at Muzdalifah?
A) Because the Prophet always used one adhan.
B) Because Isha is in its time and people are present, so a second notification is unnecessary.
C) Because the pilgrims are tired and a second adhan would be burdensome.
D) Because the hadith of Ibn Umar is the only narration.

Key Takeaway
The combined prayer at Muzdalifah is performed with one adhan and one iqamah because Isha is in its time and the people are already assembled.

Prohibition of Praying Maghrib on the Way to Muzdalifah
Ruling on praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits praying Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah and identify the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The time for Maghrib for the pilgrim only begins at Muzdalifah, so praying earlier is invalid.

During the Hajj journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah, the sun sets. Many pilgrims may be tempted to pray Maghrib on the road. The Hanafi school, however, strictly prohibits this. This lesson explores the evidence from the hadith of Usamah and the reasoning behind the ruling, as well as the difference of opinion with Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the prohibition
The text clearly states 'لم يجز المغرب في الطريق' – it is not permissible to pray Maghrib on the way. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
'La yajuz' in Hanafi fiqh often indicates haram.
2
Understand the basis: Time does not enter until Muzdalifah
The hadith of Usamah shows the Prophet said 'الصلاة أمامك' (Prayer is ahead of you). This is interpreted to mean that the time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not begin at sunset but only at Muzdalifah.
Alternatively, it could mean the place of prayer is ahead.
3
Review the hadith of Usamah
The Prophet delayed the prayer until Muzdalifah, indicating that Maghrib should not be prayed on the way. This is a strong dalil for the majority.
Reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's counter-view
Abu Yusuf argued that Maghrib is permissible on the way because it is prayed in its time (i.e., after sunset). He relied on the apparent meaning of the hadith that prayer is 'ahead' referring to place, not time.
Al-Shafi'i agreed with Abu Yusuf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The majority of Hanafis, including Imam Muhammad, hold that it is not permissible. The prayer must be delayed and combined at Muzdalifah. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The text implies tarjih through the strength of the proofs.

Source Text

The Hanafi response explains that because Isha is in its time and the people are already gathered, a second adhan is unnecessary, unlike at Arafat where Asr is performed out of its time. Additionally, no voluntary prayer is offered between them, and if one does engage in something, the iqamah must be repeated. Congregation is recommended, not required. The discussion also addresses the ruling on praying Maghrib on the way: it is not permissible to pray Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah, as the time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not begin at sunset; it only begins at Muzdalifah. This is supported by the hadith of Usamah, where the Prophet said 'Prayer is ahead of you,' understood as referring to either time or place. The Hanafi position is that if one prays before arrival, it is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Terms
العشائين (al-‘ishā’ayn): The two evening prayers: Maghrib and Isha.
جمع تأخير (jam‘ ta’khīr): Delaying the first prayer (Maghrib) to the time of the second (Isha) and performing them together.
أذان (adhān): The call to prayer announcing the time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi majority's prohibition of praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) The hadith of Ibn Umar about one adhan.
B) The hadith of Usamah where the Prophet said 'Prayer is ahead of you' interpreted as time.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Qiyas to the prohibition of fasting on the day of Arafah.

Key Takeaway
The time for Maghrib for the pilgrim does not begin at sunset; it begins only at Muzdalifah, so praying on the way is invalid.

Fajr Prayer at Muzdalifah in Ghalas
Ruling on Fajr prayer time at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah (ghalas) and explain the Hanafi reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
Praying Fajr in deep darkness (ghalas) at Muzdalifah is sunnah – it allows more time for the standing.

This lesson explains the first action at Muzdalifah: the Fajr prayer. The Hanafi school emphasizes praying it early, in the darkness right after true dawn, as the Prophet did. The reason is to maximize time for the subsequent standing (wuquf). This is similar to advancing the Asr prayer at Arafat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its time
The action is the Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The recommended time is 'ghalas' – the darkness after the true dawn before light spreads.
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud confirms this practice.
2
Recognize the evidence
The Prophet prayed Fajr at Muzdalifah in ghalas, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud and agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim.
This is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Understand the rationale
Praying early gives more time for the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah, which is wajib and occupies the time until sunrise.
Similar to advancing Asr at Arafat to have more time for the standing there.
4
Note the analogy
The text compares it to advancing Asr at Arafat, which is also a sunnah to allow more time for the standing at Arafat.
This shows the principle of facilitating the wuquf.

(عيني، مستخلص) بغلس أي ظلام آخر الليل، والمراد منه بفور طلوع الفجر الصادق قبل أن يزول الظلام وينتشر الضياء. (ع) ثم قف: أي بعد الصلاة قف بالمزدلفة وجوبا، ووقته من طلوع الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس، ولو تركه بعذر كزحمة فلا شيء. (ط) داعياً : الله تعالى بحاجتك. (ع) إلا بطن محسر: [موضع عن يسار مزدلفة. (ط، ع)] لقوله علي : "المزدلفة كلها موقف، وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر". وهو بضم الميم وفتح المهملة وكسر السين المشددة اسم وادٍ سمي بها؛ لأن فيل أصحاب الفيل حسر هناك، فإذا بلغ وادي محسر أسرع بالسير أو المشي قدر رمية حجر ؛ اقتداء بفعله عليه. (فتح) ما أسفر الصبح جدا قبل طلوع الشمس. (ط)
Then he prayed Fajr: due to what we narrated from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that he (peace be upon him) prayed it that day in the darkness (ghalas), agreed upon. And because in praying in deep darkness there is meeting the need of the standing (wuquf), so it is permissible, like advancing Asr at Arafat, rather even more so because it is in its time. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2/298) 'Al-Ghalas' with the dotted letters and open lam is the darkness of the end of the night, meaning the second dawn without delay before the darkness disappears and the light spreads. His saying: 'Then stand' means at Muzdalifah, and standing there is wajib, so much so that if one abandons it without excuse, blood (dam) is obligatory. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a rukn (pillar) due to His saying: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the sacred monument' (2:198), and the hadith of 'Urwa that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever stands with us this standing and has already departed from Arafat before that, his Hajj is complete.' He made the completion of Hajj conditional upon it, which is a sign of pillarhood. Our proof is that Sawda asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) for permission to depart at night, and he permitted her, agreed upon. If it were a pillar, it would not be permissible to abandon it, like the standing at Arafat. And from Ibn 'Abbas: 'I am among those whom the Prophet sent ahead on the night of Muzdalifah among the weak of his family.' What is mentioned in the verse is dhikr (remembrance), which is not wajib by consensus. And making the completion of Hajj conditional upon it is also an indication of obligation, but if one abandons it due to an excuse of weakness, there is nothing upon him due to what we narrated. (Al-Ayni, Mukhtasar) 'Bighalas' means darkness of the end of the night, meaning immediately at the true dawn before the darkness disappears and the light spreads. (Al-Ayni) 'Then stand': means after the prayer, stand at Muzdalifah obligatorily, and its time is from dawn to sunrise. If one abandons it due to an excuse like crowding, then nothing [upon him]. (T) 'Supplicating': to Allah Almighty for your need. (Al-Ayni) 'Except the valley of Muhassir': a place to the left of Muzdalifah. (T, A) Due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'All of Muzdalifah is a place of standing, but avoid the valley of Muhassir.' It is a valley named because the elephant of the Companions of the Elephant was exhausted (hasira) there. When one reaches Wadi Muhassir, he should hurry in walking or riding the distance of a stone's throw, following the Prophet's action. (Fath) 'Ma asfara al-subh' means when the morning has become very bright before sunrise. (T)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This lesson covers two connected rituals at Muzdalifah: the Fajr prayer and the standing (wuquf). It begins by stating that the Prophet prayed Fajr in ghalas (deep darkness), which means at the first appearance of the true dawn before light spreads. The reason given is that praying early allows more time for the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah, similar to advancing Asr at Arafat. The text then moves to the ruling on standing at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi position is that it is wajib (obligatory), and abandoning it without a valid excuse requires a sacrifice (dam). Al-Shafi'i holds it is a rukn (pillar), meaning Hajj is invalid without it. The Shafi'i proofs are the Quranic verse commanding remembrance at the sacred monument and a hadith linking completion of Hajj to this standing. The Hanafi response uses the hadith of Sawda, who was permitted to leave Muzdalifah at night, implying that the standing is not so essential that it cannot be omitted for a valid reason. Similarly, Ibn Abbas reports that the Prophet sent the weak ahead. The Quranic verse mentions 'dhikr' (remembrance), which is not even wajib by consensus, so it cannot indicate pillarhood. The text also mentions that if one abandons the standing due to an excuse, there is no penalty. Finally, it notes that all of Muzdalifah is a place for standing except the valley of Muhassir, where one should hurry through. The time for standing is from dawn to sunrise.

Key Terms
الغلس (al-ghalas): The darkness at the end of the night, specifically the time immediately after the true dawn but before light spreads.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Wajib
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school encourages praying Fajr at Muzdalifah in deep darkness (ghalas) to allow more time for the standing, following the Prophet's practice.

The Obligation of Standing (Wuquf) at Muzdalifah
Ruling on obligation of standing at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, not rukn, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Sawda.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib – its omission without excuse requires dam, but the Hajj remains valid.

This lesson delves into the legal status of standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah, one of the key rituals of Hajj. While the Shafi'i school considers it a pillar (rukn) that invalidates Hajj if omitted, the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib, based on the Prophet's permission for weak pilgrims to depart early. Understanding this difference is essential for knowing the consequences of missing this stand.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that standing at Muzdalifah is wajib: its omission without excuse requires a dam (sacrifice), but the Hajj remains valid.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Al-Shafi'i considers it a rukn (pillar) based on Quran 2:198 and the hadith of 'Urwa linking completion of Hajj to this standing.
The Quranic verse commands remembrance at the sacred monument.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses the hadith of Sawda, where the Prophet permitted her to leave Muzdalifah at night, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas about sending the weak ahead. If it were a rukn, it could not be omitted even with an excuse.
The Quranic verse mentions dhikr, which is not even wajib by consensus, so it cannot indicate pillarhood.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: If omitted without excuse, dam required; with excuse, no penalty. Shafi'i: If omitted, Hajj is invalid.
This affects both the validity and the required compensation.
5
Note the exception: valley of Muhassir
The entire Muzdalifah is a place of standing except the valley of Muhassir, where one should hurry through, following the Prophet's action.
This is a physical boundary to be avoided.

Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah: Rulings and Conditions
Rulings on the stoning of the large jamrah at Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah (wajib) and identify the conditions, pillars, wajibat, sunan, and mufsidat of the act.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is wajib; its validity depends on specific conditions of time, place, material, and distance.

Stoning the large jamrah at Mina is a key rite of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds it to be wajib (obligatory but not a rukn). Failure to perform it requires a dam (sacrifice). This lesson unpacks the detailed regulations for a valid stoning, including when, where, with what, and how to throw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
The passage discusses stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. Determine from the text whether it is fard, wajib, sunnah, etc. Look for indicators like consequences of omission.
The text says 'فارم جمرة العقبة' (then stone Jamrat al-Aqabah), which implies obligation. Later, omitting wajib requires dam.
2
Extract the conditions (shurut)
List the external conditions that must be present for the act to be valid: time (after dawn on 10th Dhul Hijjah) and place (bottom of the valley).
The phrase 'بعد ما أسفر' (after the morning has brightened) indicates time. 'من بطن الوادي' indicates place.
3
Identify the pillars (arkan) and wajibat
Distinguish between pillars (omission makes the act invalid) and wajibat (omission requires compensation but does not nullify). The text mentions throwing seven pebbles individually and the stone falling close to the jamrah as essential.
Throwing all at once counts as one (not seven), so separation is a rukn. The distance of five cubits is a wajib, not a rukn.
4
Note the sunan (recommended acts) and invalidators
Identify the recommended practices: using small pebbles (khadhf), placing on thumb and flicking with index finger, saying takbir. Also, identify what invalidates or is disliked: using wood/pearls, throwing all at once, placing without throwing.
Sunnan are meritorious but not required; mufsidat break the act and require repetition.
5
Understand the proofs (dalil)
The passage cites a hadith: 'Use pebbles of khadhf so that some of you do not hurt others.' This supports the size recommendation. The text also references a narration from Ibn Abbas regarding pebbles from near the jamrah being rejected.
Proofs are from sunnah (hadith). The text is a ruling_with_proof type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد ما أسفر، فارم جمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات كحصى خذف من مزدلفة. وقد أنزلت عليه رمی من؟ (نص غير واضح) انتهى. أنزلت عليه رمی من (؟) قوله: "كحصى الخذف" بالخاء والذال المعجمتين؛ لقوله عليه: "عليكم بحصى الخذف، لا يؤذي بعضكم بعضاً"، وكيفية الرمي أن يضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه اليمنى ويستعين بالمسبحة، ومقدار الرمي أن يكون بينه وبين موضع السقوط خمسة أذرع فصاعداً، لأن ما دون ذلك لا يكون رمياً بل طرحاً، ولو طرحها طرحاً جاز إلا أنه أساء لمخالفة السنة، ولو وضعها وضعاً لم يجز؛ لأنه ليس برمي، ولو رماها فوقعت قريباً من الجمرة جاز، ولو بعيدا لا يجزئه؛ لأنه لم يكن قربة إلا في مكان ،مخصوص، ويجوز الرمي بكل ما كان من جنس الأرض كالحجر والمدر والطين والمغرة ،والنورة، بخلاف الخشب والعنبر واللؤلؤ، ولو رمى سبع حصيات جملة فهي عن واحدة؛ لأن المنصوص عليه تفريق الأفعال، ويأخذ الحصى من أي موضع شاء إلا من عند الجمرة؛ لأن ما عندها مردود؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أن ما تقبل منه رفع وما لم يتقبل ترك، وقوله: "وكبر بكل حصاة" أي الله والله أكبر، اللهم اجعله حجاً مبروراً وذنباً مغفوراً وسعياً مشكوراً، ولو سبح مكان التكبير جاز قيل: بسم الحصول التعظيم بالذكر. (فتح)
After the morning has become bright, then stone Jamrat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles for throwing (khadhf) from Muzdalifah. And it was revealed to him? (unclear) End. It was revealed to him? His saying: 'like pebbles of khadhf' with khā' and dhāl; due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Use pebbles of khadhf, so that some of you do not hurt others.' The manner of stoning is to place the pebble on the back of the right thumb and use the index finger to propel it. The distance of stoning is that between him and the point of fall is five cubits or more, because less than that is not stoning but mere throwing. If he throws it as a throw, it is permissible but he is sinful for violating the sunnah. If he places it (without throwing), it is not permissible because it is not stoning. If he stones it and it falls close to the jamrah, it is permissible; if far, it does not suffice because it is not an act of devotion except at a specific place. Stoning is permissible with anything that is from the earth's genus, like stone, clay, mud, ochre, and lime, unlike wood, ambergris, and pearls. If he stones seven pebbles all at once, it counts as one because the prescribed act is to separate the actions. He takes the pebbles from any place he wishes except from near the jamrah because what is there is rejected, due to what is narrated from Ibn Abbas that what is accepted is raised up and what is not accepted is left. His saying: 'Say takbir with each pebble' meaning: Allahu Akbar, O Allah make it an accepted Hajj, forgiven sin, and appreciated effort. If he glorifies (tasbih) instead of takbir, it is permissible. It is said: 'Bismillah' is to attain magnification by remembrance. (Fath)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage details the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah, the large pillar near Mina, on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. It is a ruling statement with some hadith proofs. The stoning is done after dawn (when the morning has become bright, asfara). The pilgrim stones from the bottom of the valley, using seven small pebbles like those used for khadhf (throwing with thumb and index finger). The text explains that the pebbles should be small enough not to cause injury, as per the Prophet's instruction. The method involves placing the pebble on the right thumb and using the index finger to flick it. The distance should be at least five cubits; less than that is considered merely dropping, which is disliked. Dropping without throwing is not valid; placing without throwing is invalid. If the stone falls close to the jamrah, it suffices; if far, it does not. The material of the pebbles must be from the earth's substances (stone, clay, lime, etc.), not wood, ambergris, or pearls. If one throws all seven at once, it counts as only one throw, as the prescribed act requires separate actions. Pebbles may be taken from anywhere except from near the jamrah itself, because those are considered rejected. At each throw, one says takbir (Allahu Akbar) and may supplicate. If one glorifies (says subhanAllah) instead, it is still valid.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-‘Aqabah): The large stone pillar near Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
خذف (khadhf): Throwing with the thumb and index finger, like flicking.
حصى الخذف (hasā al-khadhf): Small pebbles used for throwing, about the size of a chickpea.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Five cubits
C) Seven cubits
D) Ten cubits

Key Takeaway
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is a wajib act with specific conditions: after dawn, from the bottom of the valley, using seven small earth-based pebbles thrown separately at least five cubits, saying takbir; violations may require a dam.

Standing at Muzdalifah: Wajib Not Rukn
Commentary on standing at Muzdalifah and proof it is wajib not rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies standing at Muzdalifah as wajib rather than rukn, and evaluate the practical consequence of this classification.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib – not a pillar – because the Prophet excused the weak from it.

In this lesson, you will examine a key inter-madhhab dispute: the legal nature of standing (waqoof) at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The matn and its commentary present the Hanafi position that this act is wajib (obligatory but not integral), supported by hadith evidence and a critical response to the opposing view. Understanding this ruling is essential for determining the validity of Hajj when this standing is missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Recognize that the passage addresses whether standing at Muzdalifah is a rukn (pillar) or a wajib (obligation). The matn states the act is wajib, and the commentary provides the proof.
The Hanafi position is that it is wajib; the opposing view (e.g., Shafi'i) holds it is a rukn.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi proof includes: (a) the hadith of Sawdah who was permitted to leave Muzdalifah early, (b) the hadith of Ibn Abbas sending the weak ahead, and (c) the ayah (2:200) which mentions dhikr (not the standing) – dhikr is not wajib by consensus.
If standing were a rukn, it could not be abandoned even for an excuse, analogous to standing at Arafat.
3
Identify the opposing argument
The opposing school cites the Prophet's statement 'Whoever stands with us this standing... his hajj is complete,' which suggests that completion of hajj depends on this standing, implying it is a pillar.
This is the main counter-evidence.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that 'completion' can be attached to a wajib act, not only a rukn. The permissibility of leaving for a valid excuse (weakness, crowding) proves it is not a rukn.
Thus, the hadith does not necessitate pillar status.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If standing were a rukn, missing it (even with excuse) would invalidate the hajj. But as a wajib, missing it without excuse requires a dam (penalty), while missing it with a valid excuse incurs nothing.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) in the Hanafi school is that it is wajib and excused for legitimate reasons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بغلس، ثم قف مكبرا مهللاً مصلياً ملبياً ،داعياً، وهي موقف إلا بطن محسّر، ثم إلى منى على النبي أي متكلماً بالتلبية المزدلفة كلها أي موضع للوقوف بعد ما أسفر، فارم جمرة العقبة من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات كحصى الخذف من مزدلفة قال: "من وقف معنا هذا الموقف وقد كان أفاض من عرفات قبل ذلك فقد تم حجه"، علق به تمام الحج وهو آية الركنية ولنا أن سودة استأذنت النبي ﷺ أن تفيض بليل فأذن لها، متفق عليه ولو كان ركنا لما جاز تركه كالوقوف بعرفة، وعن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه أنه قال: "أنا ممن قدم النبي ﷺ الهلال [أي] ليلة المزدلفة في ضعفة أهله"، والمذكور في الآية الذكر وهو ليس بواجب بالإجماع، وتعليق إتمام الحج به يصلح أمارة للوجوب أيضاً، غير أنه إذا ترك لعذر الضعف لا شيء عليه؛ لما روينا. (عيني، مستخلص) بغلس أي ظلام آخر الليل، والمراد منه بفور طلوع الفجر الصادق قبل أن يزول الظلام وينتشر الضياء. (ع) ثم قف: أي بعد الصلاة قف بالمزدلفة وجوبا، ووقته من طلوع الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس، ولو تركه بعذر كزحمة فلا شيء. (ط) داعياً : الله تعالى بحاجتك. (ع) إلا بطن محسر: [موضع عن يسار مزدلفة. (ط، ع)] لقوله عليه : "المزدلفة كلها موقف، وارتفعوا عن بطن محسر". وهو بضم الميم وفتح المهملة وكسر السين المشددة اسم وادٍ سمي بها؛ لأن فيل أصحاب الفيل حسر هناك، فإذا بلغ وادي محسر أسرع
In deep darkness [of the last part of the night], then stand saying takbir, tahlil, salawat, talbiyah, supplicating; it is a standing except for Batn Muhassir; then to Mina after it has become bright; then stone Jamrat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf from Muzdalifah. He said: "Whoever stands with us this standing and had already left Arafat before that, his hajj is complete." He attached to it the completion of hajj, and it is a sign of being a pillar. Our evidence: Sawdah asked the Prophet ﷺ to leave at night and he permitted her, agreed upon. If it were a pillar, it would not have been permissible to leave it like standing at Arafat. And from Ibn Abbas that he said: "I am among those whom the Prophet ﷺ sent ahead with the weak of his family on the night of Muzdalifah." The mentioned [dhikr] in the verse is dhikr, which is not wajib by consensus. Attaching the completion of hajj to it is suitable as an indication of wajib as well, except that if one leaves it due to an excuse of weakness, there is nothing upon him due to what we have narrated. (Ayni, Mukhtasar) "Baghlas" means the darkness of the end of the night, and the intended meaning is immediately at the appearance of the true dawn before the darkness disappears and light spreads. (Ayni) "Then stand": after the prayer, stand at Muzdalifah wajib, its time from dawn to sunrise; if one leaves it due to an excuse like crowding, nothing upon him. (Tahawi) "Supplicating": to Allah for your need. (Ayni) "Except for Batn Muhassir": a place to the left of Muzdalifah. (Tahawi, Ayni) Due to his statement: "All of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid Batn Muhassir." It is a valley named because the elephant of the people of the elephant was exhausted there. When one reaches Wadi Muhassir, he hastens.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of standing at Muzdalifah. The matn instructs the pilgrim to proceed to Muzdalifah in the last part of the night, then stand after Fajr prayer, raise takbir and talbiyah, supplicate, and then depart to Mina after dawn. The exception of Batn Muhassir is noted as it is not part of the standing area. The central legal issue is the status of this standing. The Hanafi school proves it is wajib, not a rukn, by citing the hadith that the Prophet allowed women to leave Muzdalifah early due to weakness. If it were a rukn, such permission would not be valid, analogous to Arafah. The ayah mentioning dhikr (2:200) is also referenced to show that the prescribed act is dhikr, not the standing itself, and dhikr is not wajib by consensus. Therefore, the standing at Muzdalifah is wajib, and leaving it for a genuine excuse incurs no penalty. The time for this standing extends from Fajr to sunrise. Batn Muhassir is a valley east of Muzdalifah where one should hasten, as per the Prophet's instruction.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Mina and Arafat where pilgrims stay after Arafat; it is a wajib standing.
بطن محسر (Batn Muhassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina where one should hasten and not stop.
بغلس (baghlas): The deep darkness at the end of the night, interpreted as just before or at true dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah is a wajib act of Hajj, not a rukn; leaving it for a valid excuse does not invalidate the pilgrimage.
