Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah: Conditions and Manner
Ruling on stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah with proof and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wajib acts for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah and apply the Hanafi conditions (shurut, wajibat, sunan) to determine the validity of a pilgrim's stoning.

Core Idea
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah requires seven pebbles, from the valley bottom, with a five-cubit throw, individually — any deviation is either makruh or invalid.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the detailed rulings for stoning the large jamrah on the Day of Nahr. The Hanafi school derives the number seven from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud, and further specifies the manner, materials, and location. Understanding these conditions is essential to perform this wajib act correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is a wajib act in Hajj. The passage details its requirements.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that establishes the number seven and the positioning. This is a sunnah ahad narration.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit action (stoning with seven pebbles while positioned with the House on his left and Mina on his right) proves the wajib number and place.
4
List the shurut (conditions) and wajibat
Identify from the text the conditions for validity: time, place, number, material, distance, landing, sequence, and pebble source. Recognize which are wajib (necessary) and which are sunnah (recommended).
Conditions b: [list from shurut]
5
Note the sunan and makruhat
Identify recommended actions (e.g., washing pebbles, taking from roadside, saying takbir) and disliked actions (e.g., stoning from above, breaking one stone into seven).

[رمز الحقائق: ١٦٠/١] (ط) الوادي: أي يكون الرمي من بطن الوادي، فلو رماها من فوق كره تنزيها (ط) بسبع حصيات لما روي عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنه أتى الجمرة الكبرى فجعل البيت عن يساره ومنى عن يمينه ورمى بسبع، وقال: "هكذا سورة البقرة"، والتقييد بسبع نفي للأقل حتى لو زاد لم يضره وإن كان خلاف السنة، ويندب غسلها وأخذها من قارعة الطريق، ولو أخذها من جمار رميت جاز وأساء، ويكره أن يكسر من حجر سبع حصاة. وقوله: "كحصى" الخذف بالخاء والذال المعجمتين؛ لقوله عليه: "عليكم بحصى الخذف، لا يؤذي بعضكم بعضاً"، وكيفية الرمي أن يضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه اليمنى ويستعين بالمسبحة، ومقدار الرمي أن يكون بينه وبين موضع السقوط خمسة أذرع فصاعداً، لأن ما دون ذلك لا يكون رمياً بل طرحاً، ولو طرحها طرحاً جاز إلا أنه أساء لمخالفة السنة، ولو وضعها وضعاً لم يجز؛ لأنه ليس برمي، ولو رماها فوقعت قريباً من الجمرة جاز، ولو بعيدا لا يجزئه؛ لأنه لم يكن قربة إلا في مكان مخصوص، ويجوز الرمي بكل ما كان من جنس الأرض كالحجر والمدر والطين والمغرة والنورة، بخلاف الخشب والعنبر واللؤلؤ، ولو رمى سبع حصيات جملة فهي عن واحدة؛ لأن المنصوص عليه تفريق الأفعال، ويأخذ الحصى من أي موضع شاء إلا من عند الجمرة؛ لأن ما عندها مردود؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه أن ما تقبل منه رفع وما لم يتقبل ترك، وقوله: "وكبر بكل حصاة" أي الله أكبر، اللهم اجعله حجاً مبروراً وذنباً مغفوراً وسعياً مشكوراً، ولو سبح مكان التكبير جاز
When the morning has become very bright before sunrise. (Tahawi) al-Aqabah: the small jamrah that is near the tree on the side of Makkah. (Ramz al-Haqaiq) al-Wadi: meaning the stoning should be from the bottom of the valley; if he stones from above, it is makruh tanzih. (Tahawi) With seven pebbles because of what is reported from Ibn Mas'ud that he came to the large jamrah and placed the House to his left and Mina to his right and stoned with seven, saying: "Thus (he stoned) the one who sent down Surah al-Baqarah." The restriction to seven negates less; if he adds more, it does not harm him, though it is against the sunnah. It is recommended to wash them and take them from the roadside; if he takes them from already thrown pebbles, it is permissible but he does wrong. It is disliked to break one stone into seven pebbles. His saying: "like pebbles of khadhf" with kh and dh, because of his statement: "You must use pebbles of khadhf, so that none of you injure another." The manner of stoning: he places the pebble on the back of his right thumb and uses his index finger. The distance of stoning: there should be five cubits or more between him and the falling place, because less than that is not stoning but dropping. If he drops it, it is permissible but he has done wrong by violating the sunnah. If he places it, it is not valid because it is not stoning. If he throws it and it falls near the jamrah, it is valid; if far, it is not sufficient because it is not a devotion except in a specific place. It is permissible to stone with anything from the category of earth, like stone, clod, clay, ochre, and lime, unlike wood, ambergris, and pearl. If he throws seven pebbles at once, they count as one because the prescribed is to separate actions. He may take pebbles from any place except from near the jamrah because what is there is rejected; as reported from Ibn Abbas that what is accepted is raised and what is not accepted is left. His saying: "And say takbir with each pebble" meaning Allahu Akbar; O Allah, make it an accepted hajj, a forgiven sin, and a thanked striving. If he glorifies (subhanallah) instead of takbir, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage details the rulings for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr. The time for stoning begins after dawn and after arriving at Mina; the commentator clarifies that 'asfar' means when the morning is fully bright before sunrise. The Jamrat al-Aqabah is identified as the small stone pillar near the tree on the Makkah side. Stoning must be performed from the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi); stoning from above is makruh tanzih. Exactly seven pebbles are required; adding more does not invalidate but is against the sunnah, while using fewer is insufficient. The pebbles should be of the khadhf type—small enough to be thrown with the fingertips—to avoid injury. The method: place the pebble on the right thumb and release with the index finger. The throw must cover at least five cubits; mere dropping is insufficient, and placing is invalid. If the pebble lands near the jamrah, it counts; if far, it does not. Only earth-based materials (stone, clay, etc.) are valid; valuable items like pearls are not. All seven pebbles must be thrown individually; throwing them all at once counts as only one. Pebbles may be collected from anywhere except from the base of the jamrah itself, as those are rejected. It is recommended to say takbir with each throw, though tasbih is sufficient.

Key Terms
الخذف (al-khadhf): Pebbles of a small size that can be thrown with the fingertips, typically the size of a date stone.
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqabah): The large stone pillar near Makkah, stoned on the Day of Nahr.
بطن الوادي (batin al-wadi): The lowest part of the valley, where the stoner should stand to throw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Seven cubits
D) Ten cubits

Key Takeaway
Stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah is a wajib act with specific conditions: seven earth-based pebbles, thrown individually from the valley bottom, covering at least five cubits, landing near the jamrah.

When to Cut the Talbiyah
Rulings on when to end talbiyah and the obligation/desirability of sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when to end the talbiyah during Hajj and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
The talbiyah ends at the first pebble of stoning the jamrah.

One of the key sequential rites in Hajj is the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah. Upon beginning this act, the pilgrim must stop reciting the talbiyah. The Hanafi school, following the majority, holds that the talbiyah ends with the first pebble, not after completing all seven. This lesson examines the evidence and the scholarly dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rite in sequence
The passage describes the order after the stoning: al-khadhf, takbir, cutting talbiyah, then sacrifice. Focus on the cutting of talbiyah.
The term 'al-khadhf' refers to the size of the pebbles.
2
Locate the Hanafi ruling
The text states: 'اقطع التلبية بأولها' (cut the talbiyah at its beginning). The commentator explains that 'بأولها' means with the first pebble.
The command indicates the recommended timing.
3
Understand the madhhab dispute
The majority (including Hanafi) hold that the talbiyah ends with the first pebble, while Imam Ahmad and some Shafi'is say after completing all seven pebbles.
The Hanafi response: the first pebble marks the beginning of the stoning ritual.
4
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The evidence is the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: 'Do not stone the jamrah until the sun rises,' and the Prophet stoned at duha (forenoon). This implies the stoning act begins with the first pebble, so the talbiyah ends then.
The time for stoning is from dawn to sunset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخذف، وكبر بكل حصاة، واقطع التلبية بأولها ثم اذبح ثم احلق أو قصر، والحلق أحب أي بعد الفراغ من الرمي الخذف بالخاء والذال المعجمتين، وهو مقدار النواة يرمى برؤوس الأصابع. (ط، ع) وكبر: أي قل الله أكبر مع رمي كل حصاة ولو سبّح أجزأه (ط) واقطع أي اتركها ولا تقل من بعد. (محشي) بأولها: أي مع أولها، اختلف العلماء في أنه هل يقطع التلبية مع رمي أول حصاة أو عند تمام الرمي، فذهب إلى الأول الجمهور، وإلى الثاني أحمد وبعض أصحاب الشافعي، ووقت الرمي من طلوع الفجر إلى غروب الشمس، ويكره قبل طلوع الشمس، ويستحب بعده إلى الزوال، ويباح بعد الزوال إلى الغروب وقال الشافعي: يجوز الرمي بعد النصف الأخير من الليل، ولنا ما رواه ابن عباس رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم "أي بني لا ترموا الجمرة حتى تطلع الشمس"، رواه أبو داود، وصححه الترمذي، ورمى رسول الله ضحى، متفق عليه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٦٠/١] (فتح) ثم اذبح وهذا مستحب للمفرد، وواجب على القارن والمتمتع. (ط) أي بعد الفراغ من الرمي؛ لحديث جابر رضي الله عنه أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لما رمى جمرة العقبة انصرف إلى المنحر، فنحر بيده ثلاثاً وستين وأمر علياً فنحر ما بقي، وأشركه في هديه، وكان ما بقي سبعاً وثلاثين بدنة تمام المائة، والحكمة في نحره عليه ثلاثاً وستين بدنة أنه كان له يومئذ ثلاث وستون سنة، فنحر لكل سنة بدنة. (فتح)
Al-khadhf, and say takbir with each pebble, and cut off the talbiyah at the beginning of it, then sacrifice, then shave or shorten, and shaving is more beloved. Meaning after finishing the stoning. Al-khadhf with kh and dh, it is the size of a date stone thrown with fingertips. (Tahawi, Ayni) And say takbir: meaning say Allahu Akbar with each pebble thrown, and if he glorifies, it suffices. (Tahawi) And cut: meaning leave it and do not say it after. (Hashiyah) At its beginning: meaning with its first [pebble]. The scholars differed as to whether he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble or at the completion of the stoning. The majority hold the first, while Ahmad and some Shafi'is hold the second. The time for stoning is from dawn to sunset; it is disliked before sunrise, recommended after it until noon [zawal], and permitted after noon until sunset. Ash-Shafi'i said: stoning is allowed after the latter half of the night. Our evidence: what Ibn Abbas narrated from the Prophet ﷺ: "O sons, do not stone the jamrah until the sun rises," reported by Abu Dawud and authenticated by at-Tirmidhi, and the Messenger of Allah stoned at duha (forenoon), agreed upon. Then sacrifice: this is recommended for the mufrid and obligatory for the qarin and mutamatti' (Tahawi), meaning after finishing the stoning; based on the hadith of Jabir that when he stoned Jamrat al-Aqabah, he went to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed with his own hand sixty-three [camels] and ordered Ali to sacrifice the rest, and he included him in his sacrificial animals. The number remaining was thirty-seven, completing one hundred. The wisdom behind his sacrificing sixty-three was that he was sixty-three years old that day, so he sacrificed a camel for each year.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage continues the sequence of rites. After completing the stoning, the pilgrim cuts off the talbiyah. There is a difference of opinion: the majority (including Hanafi) hold that talbiyah ends with the first pebble, while Ahmad and some Shafi'is say at the end of all seven. The Hanafi evidence is the hadith that the Prophet stoned at duha (forenoon) and that stoning should not be done before sunrise. The time for stoning is from dawn to sunset, with specific preferences. After stoning, the sacrifice (dhabh) is performed. For a mufrid (one performing only Hajj), it is mustahab; for a qarin (performing Hajj and Umrah together) and mutamatti' (performing Umrah then Hajj), it is wajib. The hadith of Jabir describes the Prophet's own sacrifice of 63 camels, one for each year of his life, and Ali sacrificed the remaining 37.

Key Terms
التلبية (at-talbiyah): The proclamation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should a pilgrim stop reciting the talbiyah?
A) After completing all seven pebbles
B) With the first pebble of Jamrat al-Aqabah
C) After the sacrifice
D) After shaving the head

Key Takeaway
The talbiyah ends at the first pebble of stoning, per the Hanafi school based on the Prophet's practice.

The Obligation of Sacrifice in Hajj
Rulings on when to end talbiyah and the obligation/desirability of sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the ruling on sacrifice (dhabh) for the three types of ihram: mufrid, qarin, and mutamatti', and cite the prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
Sacrifice is wajib for the qarin and mutamatti', and mustahab for the mufrid.

After stoning and cutting the talbiyah, the pilgrim proceeds to sacrifice. The passage specifies that this act is recommended for one performing only Hajj (mufrid) but obligatory for one performing Hajj and Umrah together (qarin) or Umrah followed by Hajj (mutamatti'). This lesson explores the evidence from the Prophet's own sacrifice and the wisdom behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sequence
The passage: 'ثم اذبح ثم احلق أو قصر' – after stoning, sacrifice, then shave or trim.
The sacrifice is part of the rites on the Day of Sacrifice.
2
Note the differentiation in ruling
The text states: 'وهذا مستحب للمفرد، واجب على القارن والمتمتع' – recommended for the mufrid, wajib for the qarin and mutamatti'.
The words 'مستحب' (mustahab) and 'واجب' (wajib) indicate different levels of obligation.
3
Understand the basis
The evidence is the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's sacrifice of 63 camels after stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, showing its importance.
The hadith demonstrates the Prophet's practice.
4
Appreciate the wisdom
The Prophet sacrificed a camel for each year of his life (63 years), indicating the magnitude of the act.
This is not a legal requirement but shows devotion.

Key Terms
المفرد (al-mufrid): One who performs only Hajj, not Umrah, in the same ihram.
القارن (al-qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in one ihram.
المتمتع (al-mutamatti'): One who performs Umrah first, then Hajj in the same year with a break of ihram.
الذبح (adh-dhabh): The sacrifice of an animal during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The mufrid
B) The qarin
C) The mufrid and qarin
D) The mufrid and mutamatti'

Key Takeaway
The sacrifice is an obligatory rite for the qarin and mutamatti', and a recommended act for the mufrid.

Shaving and Trimming Hair in Hajj: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Proof
Ruling with proof on shaving/trimming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that shaving or trimming is wajib, identify the minimum required amount (one-fourth of the head), and explain the evidence from the hadith of the Prophet.

Core Idea
The minimum wajib in shaving or trimming is one-fourth; shaving all is superior.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the final rite of Hajj: shaving or trimming the hair. The Hanafi school considers this act wajib, with a specific minimum requirement of one-fourth of the head. The Prophet's ﷺ practice and supplication provide the primary evidence, and the text also covers exceptional cases like baldness or wounds. Understanding this ruling ensures that pilgrims fulfill their obligation correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir) the hair after Hajj/Umrah. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet's hadith: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave' repeated twice, then including 'and those who trim'. This is the primary proof.
Hadith is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The repetition of 'those who shave' indicates preference for shaving, but the inclusion of trimmers shows both are acceptable. The Hanafi school uses the principle that a general command indicates obligation, but the minimum is derived from the quarter-rule.
The quarter-rule: 'one-fourth has the ruling of the whole.'
4
Note the minimum requirement
It suffices to shave (or trim) one-fourth of the head. Shaving the entire head is better (afdal). For men, shaving is more beloved; for women, only trimming is allowed.
Exception: bald or wounded persons must pass the razor if possible; otherwise the obligation drops.
5
Evaluate the evidence
The hadith shows preference but does not prescribe a quantity. The Hanafi ruling of one-fourth is based on the legal maxim that a quarter stands for the whole, derived from other contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احلق أنه روي عنه ﷺ قال للحلاق: "خذ" وأشار إلى جانبه الأيمن ثم الأيسر، ثم جعل يعطيه الناس. (رواه مسلم) (ع) أراد بالحلق إزالة الشعر، واستعمال الموسى مستحب، ويجب إجراء الموسى على رأس أقرع وذي قروح إن أمكن، وإلا سقط، والتقصير : أن يأخذ الرجل والمرأة من رؤوس الشعر مقدار الأنملة، والحلق أحب في حق الرجال والتقصير في حق النساء لا غير، وكون الحلق أحب في حقهم؛ لقوله عليه : "اللهم اغفر للمحلقين"، قالوا: "يا رسول الله، والمقصرين"؟ قال: "اللهم اغفر للمحلقين"، قالوا: يا رسول الله، والمقصرين؟ قال: "والمقصرين"، متفق عليه، ويكتفي بحلق ربع الرأس؛ لأن للربع حكم الكل، وحلق الكل أولى؛ اقتداء به عليه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/١] تنبيه: عن وكيع قال: قال لي أبو حنيفة: أخطأت في ستة أبواب من المناسك علمنيها حجام، وذلك أنني حين أردت أن أحلق رأسي وقفت على حجام، فقلت له بكم تحلق رأسي؟ فقال لي: أعراقي أنت؟ فقلت: نعم، قال لي: النسك لا يشارط عليه اجلس فجلست منحرفا عن القبلة، فقال لي حول وجهك إلى القبلة فحولته، وأردت أن يحلق رأسي من الجانب الأيسر، فقال لي أدر الشق الأيمن من رأسك فأدرته، وجعل يحلق وأنا ساكت، فقال لي: كبر، فجعلت أكبر حتى قمت أذهب فقال لي: أين تريد؟ فقلت رحلي، فقال: ادفن شعرك، ثم صل ركعتين، ثم امض، فقلت له: من أين لك ما أمرتني ؟ فقال: رأيت عطاء بن أبي رباح يفعل هذا. (عيني، فتح) أو قصر : بأن تأخذ من كل شعرة قدر الأنملة ،وجوبا، وتقصير الكل مندوب، والربع واجب. (ط) أحب من التقصير للرجال، ويكتفى بالربع والكل أفضل. (ط)
Then shave: Indeed it is narrated from him ﷺ that he said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to his right side then left, then he gave it to the people. (Muslim) (Ayni) He intended by shaving: removing the hair. Using the razor is recommended. It is obligatory to pass the razor over the head of a bald person or one with sores if possible; otherwise it is dropped. Trimming: it is that a man and woman take from the ends of the hair the length of a finger joint. Shaving is more beloved for men, and trimming for women exclusively. That shaving is more beloved for them because of his statement: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, and those who trim?' He said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, and those who trim?' He said: 'And those who trim.' Agreed upon. It suffices to shave one-fourth of the head because the fourth has the ruling of the whole; shaving all is better, following his example. (Ramz al-Haqaiq) A note: from Waki' that Abu Hanifa told him: I made mistakes in six chapters of the rituals, which a barber taught me. When I wanted to shave my head, I stood by a barber and said: How much do you charge to shave my head? He said: Are you an Iraqi? I said: Yes. He said: The ritual is not bargained over. Sit. So I sat turning away from the qibla. He said: Turn your face to the qibla. I turned. I wanted him to shave from the left side. He said: Turn the right side of your head. I turned. He began shaving while I was silent. He said: Say takbir. So I kept saying takbir until I got up to leave. He said: Where are you going? I said: To my luggage. He said: Bury your hair, then pray two rak'ahs, then go. I said: From where do you have what you commanded me? He said: I saw Ata ibn Abi Rabah doing this. (Ayni, Fath) Or trim: that you take from each hair the length of a finger joint, wajib. Trimming all is recommended, the quarter is wajib. (Tahawi) [Shaving] is more beloved than trimming for men; the quarter suffices but the whole is better.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage covers the final rite: shaving or trimming the hair. Shaving is recommended for men, while women only trim. The proof is the Prophet's prayer for those who shave, mentioning trimmers second. The minimum requirement is shaving one-fourth of the head (or trimming one-quarter of the hair length for women). The anecdote about Imam Abu Hanifa highlights the proper method: no bargaining, face qibla, start from right side, say takbir, bury hair, pray two rak'ahs. This shows the practical sunnahs of shaving. The passage also notes that for a bald person or one with wounds, passing the razor over the head is obligatory if possible; otherwise, it falls away. Trimming for men is sufficient but shaving is superior.

Key Terms
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head completely; preferred for men.
التقصير (at-taqsir): Cutting a finger-joint length from each hair; for women only.
الأنملة (al-anmulah): The tip of the finger, used as a measure for trimming hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Prophet said 'O Allah, forgive those who shave' twice
B) The Prophet trimmed his own hair
C) The Prophet said 'Shaving is better'
D) The Quran commands shaving

Key Takeaway
The essential point is that shaving or trimming after Hajj is wajib, and one-fourth of the head suffices, with shaving all being superior.

The Sunnahs of Shaving: Lessons from Imam Abu Hanifa's Teacher
Anecdote on proper method of shaving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five sunan acts observed during shaving after Hajj and justify each with the anecdote of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Shaving is a ritual act: no bargaining, face qibla, start right side, say takbir, bury hair, pray two rak'ahs.

A famous anecdote narrates Imam Abu Hanifa's learning from a barber who followed the practice of Ata ibn Abi Rabah. This story encapsulates several sunnan of the shaving ritual, offering practical guidance for every pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Extract each sunnah from the anecdote
Read the anecdote carefully and list every action the barber instructed or corrected.
Actions include: not bargaining, facing qibla, starting from right, saying takbir, burying hair, praying two rak'ahs.
2
Determine the fiqh status of each act
Classify each as sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), mustahabb (recommended), or adab (etiquette) based on standard Hanafi works.
Most are sunnah muakkadah according to later Hanafi texts.
3
Note the authority chain
The barber learned from Ata ibn Abi Rabah, a Tabi'i and mufti of Makkah. His practice is considered authoritative (qawl sahabi) and forms a source of sunnah.
Imam Abu Hanifa himself followed this guidance.
4
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider how a pilgrim today should implement these sunnan when going to a barber in Makkah.
Modern barbers may not be aware; the pilgrim should guide them.

(رواه مسلم) (ع) أراد بالحلق إزالة الشعر، واستعمال الموسى مستحب، ويجب إجراء الموسى على رأس أقرع وذي قروح إن أمكن، وإلا سقط، والتقصير : أن يأخذ الرجل والمرأة من رؤوس الشعر مقدار الأنملة، والحلق أحب في حق الرجال والتقصير في حق النساء لا غير، وكون الحلق أحب في حقهم؛ لقوله عليه : "اللهم اغفر للمحلقين"، قالوا: "يا رسول الله، والمقصرين"؟ قال: "اللهم اغفر للمحلقين"، قالوا: يا رسول الله، والمقصرين؟ قال: "والمقصرين"، متفق عليه، ويكتفي بحلق ربع الرأس؛ لأن للربع حكم الكل، وحلق الكل أولى؛ اقتداء به عليه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/١] تنبيه: عن وكيع قال: قال لي أبو حنيفة: أخطأت في ستة أبواب من المناسك علمنيها حجام، وذلك أنني حين أردت أن أحلق رأسي وقفت على حجام، فقلت له بكم تحلق رأسي؟ فقال لي: أعراقي أنت؟ فقلت: نعم، قال لي: النسك لا يشارط عليه اجلس فجلست منحرفا عن القبلة، فقال لي حول وجهك إلى القبلة فحولته، وأردت أن يحلق رأسي من الجانب الأيسر، فقال لي أدر الشق الأيمن من رأسك فأدرته، وجعل يحلق وأنا ساكت، فقال لي: كبر، فجعلت أكبر حتى قمت أذهب فقال لي: أين تريد؟ فقلت رحلي، فقال: ادفن شعرك، ثم صل ركعتين، ثم امض، فقلت له: من أين لك ما أمرتني ؟ فقال: رأيت عطاء بن أبي رباح يفعل هذا. (عيني، فتح) أو قصر : بأن تأخذ من كل شعرة قدر الأنملة ،وجوبا، وتقصير الكل مندوب، والربع واجب. (ط) أحب من التقصير للرجال، ويكتفى بالربع والكل أفضل. (ط)
Then shave: Indeed it is narrated from him ﷺ that he said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to his right side then left, then he gave it to the people. (Muslim) (Ayni) He intended by shaving: removing the hair. Using the razor is recommended. It is obligatory to pass the razor over the head of a bald person or one with sores if possible; otherwise it is dropped. Trimming: it is that a man and woman take from the ends of the hair the length of a finger joint. Shaving is more beloved for men, and trimming for women exclusively. That shaving is more beloved for them because of his statement: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, and those who trim?' He said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, and those who trim?' He said: 'And those who trim.' Agreed upon. It suffices to shave one-fourth of the head because the fourth has the ruling of the whole; shaving all is better, following his example. (Ramz al-Haqaiq) A note: from Waki' that Abu Hanifa told him: I made mistakes in six chapters of the rituals, which a barber taught me. When I wanted to shave my head, I stood by a barber and said: How much do you charge to shave my head? He said: Are you an Iraqi? I said: Yes. He said: The ritual is not bargained over. Sit. So I sat turning away from the qibla. He said: Turn your face to the qibla. I turned. I wanted him to shave from the left side. He said: Turn the right side of your head. I turned. He began shaving while I was silent. He said: Say takbir. So I kept saying takbir until I got up to leave. He said: Where are you going? I said: To my luggage. He said: Bury your hair, then pray two rak'ahs, then go. I said: From where do you have what you commanded me? He said: I saw Ata ibn Abi Rabah doing this. (Ayni, Fath) Or trim: that you take from each hair the length of a finger joint, wajib. Trimming all is recommended, the quarter is wajib. (Tahawi) [Shaving] is more beloved than trimming for men; the quarter suffices but the whole is better.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage covers the final rite: shaving or trimming the hair. Shaving is recommended for men, while women only trim. The proof is the Prophet's prayer for those who shave, mentioning trimmers second. The minimum requirement is shaving one-fourth of the head (or trimming one-quarter of the hair length for women). The anecdote about Imam Abu Hanifa highlights the proper method: no bargaining, face qibla, start from right side, say takbir, bury hair, pray two rak'ahs. This shows the practical sunnahs of shaving. The passage also notes that for a bald person or one with wounds, passing the razor over the head is obligatory if possible; otherwise, it falls away. Trimming for men is sufficient but shaving is superior.

Key Terms
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head completely; preferred for men.
التقصير (at-taqsir): Cutting a finger-joint length from each hair; for women only.
الأنملة (al-anmulah): The tip of the finger, used as a measure for trimming hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Imam Abu Hanifa do wrong when he first approached the barber?
A) He bargained over the price
B) He sat facing away from qibla
C) He wanted shaving from left side
D) He forgot to say takbir

Key Takeaway
The sunan of shaving after Hajj include facing qibla, starting from the right, saying takbir, burying hair, and praying two rak'ahs, all learned from the practice of the pious predecessors.

Sequence of Acts After Ramy al-Jamrah
Describes the manner of throwing, takbir, cutting talbiyah, slaughter, and shaving/trimming.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sequence of acts after throwing at Jamrat al-Aqabah, explain the ruling on cutting talbiyah, and apply the dalil for the time of ramy.

Core Idea
The pilgrim cuts talbiyah with the first pebble and must not throw before sunrise; shaving a quarter of the head suffices.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the obligatory order of actions after completing the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah. It covers the method of throwing, the cutting of talbiyah, the timing of ramy, and the rulings on slaughter and shaving. Understanding this sequence is essential for the validity of Hajj rites, as each step has a specific time and manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed sequence
List the acts in order: ramy (with khadhf and takbir), cut talbiyah, slaughter (if required), shave or shorten.
The sequence is wajib; skipping an order may require compensation.
2
Pinpoint the ruling on cutting talbiyah
Note that the talbiyah is cut with the first pebble. This is the Hanafi position supported by the majority and a hadith.
The imperative 'waqta'' indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the proof for the time of ramy
Examine the hadith 'لا ترموا الجمرة حتى تطلع الشمس' and how it sets the earliest time for ramy after sunrise.
The hadith is sahih and used as a proof for prohibition before sunrise.
4
Analyze the madhhab dispute
Compare the Hanafi view (ramy after sunrise, talbiyah cut with first pebble) with the Shafi'i view (ramy allowed after last half of night, talbiyah cut after completion).
The thamarah al-khilaf is the permissibility of ramy before dawn.
5
Apply the rulings on shaving
Distinguish between shaving (preferred for men) and shortening (for women). Identify that shaving a quarter of the head suffices but shaving all is better.
The anecdote of Abu Hanifa learning from a barber illustrates the proper practice.

Source Text

الخذف، وكبر بكل حصاة، واقطع التلبية بأولها ثم اذبح ثم احلق أو قصر، والحلق أحب أي بعد الفراغ من الرمي الخذف بالخاء والذال المعجمتين، وهو مقدار النواة يرمى برؤوس الأصابع. (ط، ع) وكبر: أي قل الله أكبر مع رمي كل حصاة ولو سبّح أجزأه (ط) واقطع أي اتركها ولا تقل من بعد. (محشي) بأولها: أي مع أولها، اختلف العلماء في أنه هل يقطع التلبية مع رمي أول حصاة أو عند تمام الرمي، فذهب إلى الأول الجمهور، وإلى الثاني أحمد وبعض أصحاب الشافعي، ووقت الرمي من طلوع الفجر إلى غروب الشمس، ويكره قبل طلوع الشمس، ويستحب بعده إلى الزوال، ويباح بعد الزوال إلى الغروب وقال الشافعي: يجوز الرمي بعد النصف الأخير من الليل، ولنا ما رواه ابن عباس اما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم " أي بني لا ترموا الجمرة حتى تطلع الشمس"، رواه أبو داود، وصححه الترمذي، ورمى رسول الله الله ضحی، متفق عليه. (فتح) ثم اذبح وهذا مستحب للمفرد، وواجب على القارن والمتمتع. (ط)] أي بعد الفراغ من الرمي؛ لحديث جابر الله لما عليها أنه لما رمى جمرة العقبة انصرف إلى المنحر، فنحر بيده ثلاثاً وستين وأمر علياً فنحر ما غبر، وأشركه في هديه، وكان ما غير سبعاً وثلاثين بدنة تمام المائة، والحكمة في نحره عليه ثلاثاً وستين بدنة أنه كان له يومئذ ثلاث وستون سنة، فنحر لكل سنة بدنة. (فتح) ثم احلق الما أنه روي عليه قال للحلاق: "خذ" ، وأشار إلى جانبه الأيمن ثم الأيسر، ثم جعل يعطيه الناس. (رواه مسلم) (ع)] أراد بالحلق إزالة الشعر، واستعمال الموسى مستحب، ويجب إجراء الموسى على رأس أقرع وذي قروح إن أمكن، وإلا سقط، والتقصير : أن يأخذ الرجل والمرأة من رؤوس الشعر مقدار الأنملة، والحلق أحب في حق الرجال والتقصير في حق النساء لا غير، وكون الحلق أحب في حقهم؛ لقوله عليه : "اللهم اغفر للمحلقين"، قالوا: "يا رسول الله، والمقصرين"؟ قال: "اللهم اغفر للمحلقين"، قالوا: يا رسول الله، والمقصرين؟ قال: "والمقصرين"، متفق عليه، ويكتفي بحلق ربع الرأس؛ لأن للربع حكم الكل، وحلق الكل أولى؛ اقتداء به عليه. تنبيه: عن وكيع قال: قال لي أبو حنيفة: أخطأت في ستة أبواب من المناسك علمنيها حجام، وذلك أنني حين أردت أن أحلق رأسي وقفت على حجام، فقلت له بكم تحلق رأسي؟ فقال لي: أعراقي أنت؟ فقلت: نعم، قال لي: النسك لا يشارط عليه اجلس فجلست منحرفا عن القبلة، فقال لي حول وجهك إلى القبلة فحولته، وأردت أن يحلق رأسي من الجانب الأيسر، فقال لي أدر الشق الأيمن من رأسك فأدرته، وجعل يحلق وأنا ساكت، فقال لي: كبر، فجعلت أكبر حتى قمت أذهب فقال لي: أين تريد؟ فقلت رحلي، فقال: ادفن شعرك، ثم صل ركعتين، ثم امض، فقلت له: من أين لك ما أمرتني ؟ فقال: رأيت عطاء بن أبي رباح يفعل هذا. (عيني، فتح) أو قصر : بأن تأخذ من كل شعرة قدر الأنملة ،وجوبا، وتقصير الكل مندوب، والربع واجب. (ط) أحب من التقصير للرجال، ويكتفى بالربع والكل أفضل. (ط)
Khadhf, and say takbir with each pebble, and cut the talbiyah at its beginning, then slaughter, then shave or shorten, and shaving is more beloved. That is after finishing the ramy. Khadhf: with khā and dhāl, it is the size of a date pit, thrown with the fingertips. Takbir: say 'Allahu akbar' with each pebble, and if he says subhanallah it suffices. Cut: leave it and do not say after. With its beginning: i.e. with its beginning. The scholars differed whether one cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble or upon completing the ramy. The majority went to the first, Ahmad and some Shafi'i followers to the second. The time of ramy is from dawn to sunset, disliked before sunrise, recommended after it until noon, permitted after noon until sunset. Al-Shafi'i said it is permissible after the last half of the night. Our proof is what Ibn Abbas narrated from the Prophet (s): 'O my sons, do not throw the jamrah until the sun rises,' reported by Abu Dawud and authenticated by Tirmidhi. And the Messenger of Allah (s) threw at forenoon, agreed upon. Then slaughter: this is recommended for the individual pilgrim (mufrid) and obligatory for the qārin and mutamatti'. After finishing the ramy, due to the hadith of Jabir that when he (s) threw Jamrat al-Aqabah he went to the place of sacrifice and slaughtered sixty-three with his hand and ordered Ali to slaughter the remainder, and he made him a partner in his sacrificial animals, and the remainder were thirty-seven, completing one hundred. The wisdom in his slaughtering sixty-three was that he was sixty-three years old that day, so he slaughtered a camel for each year. Then shave: for it is narrated that he said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to his right side then left, then he gave to the people. (Muslim). He intended by shaving removal of hair, and using a razor is recommended. It is obligatory to pass the razor over the head of a bald person or one with sores if possible, otherwise it is dropped. Shortening (taqsir): that a man and woman take from the ends of their hair the amount of a fingertip. Shaving is more beloved for men and shortening for women exclusively. Shaving is more beloved for them due to his statement: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, and those who shorten?' He said: 'O Allah, forgive those who shave.' They said: 'O Messenger of Allah, and those who shorten?' He said: 'And those who shorten,' agreed upon. And it suffices to shave a quarter of the head because the quarter has the ruling of the whole, and shaving all is better in imitation of him. Note: Waki' said: Abu Hanifa said to me: I was mistaken in six chapters of the rituals, which a barber taught me. When I wanted to shave my head, I stopped at a barber and said: 'How much do you charge to shave my head?' He said: 'Are you an Iraqi?' I said: 'Yes.' He said: 'The ritual cannot be bargained over. Sit.' So I sat facing away from the qibla. He said: 'Turn your face to the qibla,' so I turned. I wanted him to shave from the left side, he said: 'Turn the right side of your head,' so I turned. He started shaving while I was silent. He said: 'Say takbir,' so I started saying takbir until I got up to leave. He said: 'Where are you going?' I said: 'To my saddle.' He said: 'Bury your hair, then pray two rak'ahs, then go.' I said: 'Where did you get what you commanded me?' He said: 'I saw 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah do this.' Or shorten (taqsir): that one takes from each hair the amount of a fingertip, obligatorily, and shortening all is recommended, and the quarter is obligatory. It is more beloved than shortening for men, and the quarter suffices and all is better.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering the sequence of actions after throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah. The author begins by defining the manner of throwing (khadhf): using small pebbles the size of a date pit, thrown with the fingertips. He states that takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') accompanies each pebble, and that saying other remembrance suffices. The key ruling on cutting talbiyah (the pilgrim's chant) is presented: one cuts it with the first pebble. The author notes a disagreement: most scholars (jumhur) agree with this, while Ahmad and some Shafi'is say it is cut upon completing the ramy. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'Do not throw until the sun rises,' indicating the time for ramy begins after sunrise, and the Prophet's own practice of throwing at forenoon. The time for ramy is from dawn to sunset, with disliked, recommended, and permissible intervals. Then the author addresses slaughter (dhabh): it is recommended for the mufrid (single pilgrim) and wajib for qarin and mutamatti'. The proof is the hadith of Jabir detailing the Prophet's slaughter of 63 camels. Next, shaving (halq) or shortening (taqsir) is discussed. Shaving is preferred for men, shortening for women. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet praying for those who shave, then including those who shorten. The amount that suffices is a quarter of the head, but shaving all is better. An anecdote about Imam Abu Hanifa learning from a barber illustrates proper practice: facing qibla, shaving right side first, saying takbir, burying hair, and praying two rak'ahs. The passage concludes with the ruling on taqsir: it is obligatory to take at least a fingertip length from each hair, and the quarter suffices.

Key Terms
الخذف (al-khadhf): Throwing small pebbles using the fingertips, pebbles about the size of a date pit.
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The chant 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head completely or at least a quarter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should the pilgrim cut the talbiyah during the ramy of Jamrat al-Aqabah?
A) After completing all seven pebbles
B) With the first pebble
C) After slaughter
D) At sunset

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes that the talbiyah is cut with the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqabah, ramy must be after sunrise, and shaving a quarter of the head suffices.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Ruling, Time, and Conditions
Rulings on the time, conditions, and components of Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, identify its time, and list its conditions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn of Hajj; four circuits are fard, three are wajib, and it must be performed within the days of sacrifice.

This passage from the Hanafi text explains the essential tawaf of Hajj, known as Tawaf al-Ziyarah. It clarifies its time, the number of circuits, and the conditions for its validity. Understanding these details ensures the pilgrim performs this key rite correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its overall ruling
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn of Hajj. Determine its hukm level (fard, wajib, etc.) noting that four circuits are rukn (fard) and three are wajib.
The text says: 'seven circuits, four of which are rukn and the remainder wajib.'
2
Determine the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah
The passage states the time is from dawn of the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah) to the end of life, with the best being the days of sacrifice (10th-12th). Identify the proof from Quranic conjunction.
Quran 22:28-29 links tawaf to slaughter, limiting its time to the days of sacrifice.
3
List the conditions for valid tawaf
From the text, identify the conditions: being standing and walking, in a state of purity, and covering the awrah. Also note that if these are missed, a dam is required.
Riding or fleeing invalidates unless necessary; then dam applies.
4
Note the consequences of omissions
If a rukn (four circuits) is missed, tawaf is invalid. If a wajib (three circuits or conditions) is missed, a dam is required. Perfume, on the other hand, is already permissible after ramy and shaving.
This step links to the next lesson on permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحلّ لك غيرُ النساء، ثم إلى مكة يوم النحر أو غداً أو بعده، فطف للركن سبعة أشواط بلا رمل وسعى إن قدّمتهما وإلا فعلا، وحل لك النساء، في الطواف وإن لم تكن قدمتهما حل لك كل شيء من محظورات الإحرام. (ط) غير النساء [ أي غير الجماع بهن ودواعيه كالمس والقبلة. (ط)] وقال مالك: لا يحل له الطيب أيضاً؛ لأنه من دواعي الجماع، ولنا: ماروت عائشة ما قالت: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إذا رميتم وذبحتم فقد حل لكم كل شيء إلا النساء، وحل لكم الثياب والطيب"، رواه الدار قطني، وخبر الواحد يترك به القياس، ثم الرمي ليس بسبب التحليل عندنا، وقال الشافعي: هو سبب التحليل أيضاً؛ لأنه يتوقت بيوم النحر كالحلق، فيكون بمنزلته في التحليل ولنا أن ما يكون محللاً يكون جناية في غير أوانه كالحلق، والرمي ليس كذلك. (عيني، مستخلص) أو بعده: [ أي بعد غد النحر، وأولها أفضلها. (ط،ع)] وهذه الأيام الثلاث، أي من عاشر ذي الحجة إلى ثاني عشر منه أيام النحر، وهي وقت طواف الزيارة؛ لأن الله تعالى عطف الطواف على الذبح والأكل منه، فقال: ﴿فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ (الحج: ۲۸)، ثم قال: ﴿ وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بالبيت العتيق (الحج: ۲۹)، والعطف يقتضي المشاركة في الحكم بين المعطوف والمعطوف عليه إذا كان بحرف الواو، والذبح مؤقت بأيام النحر فكذا الطواف، فكان وقتهما واحداً، وأولها أفضلها. رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/١] لقوله عليه: "أيام النحر ثلاثة أفضلها أولها ، وطواف الركن هو الطواف المفروض في الحج وهو ركن فيه، ويسمى طواف الزيارة وطواف الإفاضة وطواف يوم النحر (مستخلص للركن أي إذا أتيت مكة طف لأجل طواف الركن، ووقته من طلوع فجر النحر إلى آخر العمر. (ط،ع) سبعة أشواط والركن منها أربع، والباقي واجب. (ط)] يجب أن يكون قائماً ماشياً، ولو طاف ناصباً أنصاف ساقيه فقط أو محمولاً أو راكباً وسعى كذلك، لزمه دم ولا يجوز لو طاف هارباً من عدو أو طالباً لغريم، وكذا يجب أن يكون على طهارة وأن يكون مستور العورة. وقوله: "بلا رمل وسعي إن قدمتهما ؛ لأن التكرار فيهما لم يشرع. (فتح) قدمتهما: أي الرمل والسعي في طواف القدوم رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/١] (ط) وإلا فعلا: أي الرمل والسعي في طواف الزيارة، وكان ينبغي أن يقول: وإلا افعلهما بصيغة الأمر - وصل ركعتين عقب هذا الطواف. (ط،ع) وحل لك النساء: [بالحلق السابق لا بهذا الطواف حتى لو طاف قبل الحلق لم يحل له شيء، فلو قلم ظفره مثلاً كان جناية. (ط)] أي إذا طفت طواف الركن حل لك النساء لإجماع الأمة على ذلك؛ لأن المنع كان للحج و قد تم، وحلة النساء إنما هو بالحلق السابق لا بالطواف؛ لأن المحلل دون الطواف غير أنه أخر عمله إلى هو ما بعد الطواف، فإذا حصل الطواف عمل الحلق عمله كالطلاق الرجعي أخر عمله إلى انقضاء العدة؛ لحاجته إلى الاسترداد، فإذا انقضت عمل الطلاق عمله فبانت منه تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۱/۲] والطواف ركن من أركان الحج، والتحليل عن العبادات لا يكون بركن، بل بما هو محظور في تلك العبادة. (عيني، مستخلص)
And permissible for you is other than women, then to Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice or the following day or after it, and perform tawaf for the pillar (rukn) seven circuits without raml and sa'y if you have already performed them, otherwise do them, and women become permissible for you in the tawaf, and if you have not performed them, everything from the prohibitions of ihram becomes permissible for you. (T) Other than women: i.e. other than intercourse with them and its causes like touching and kissing. (T) Malik said: Perfume is not permissible for him either because it is a cause of intercourse. Our proof: Aisha narrated that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When you have thrown (the jamrah) and slaughtered, everything becomes permissible for you except women, and clothes and perfume become permissible for you,' reported by al-Daraqutni. A khabar wahid is used to abandon qiyas. Then ramy is not a cause of tahlil according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: It is also a cause of tahlil because it is restricted to the Day of Sacrifice like shaving, so it is like it in tahlil. Our proof: What is a cause of tahlil would be a violation if done out of its time like shaving, but ramy is not like that. Or after it: i.e. after the day following the Day of Sacrifice, and the first of them is best. These three days, i.e. from the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah to the 12th, are the days of sacrifice, and they are the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah because Allah has joined tawaf to slaughter and eating from it, saying: 'Then eat thereof and feed the miserable poor' (22:28), then He said: 'And let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' (22:29). Conjunction implies sharing in the ruling between the conjoined and the conjoined to when with the letter waw. Slaughter is confined to the days of sacrifice, so likewise tawaf, so their time is one, and the first of them is best. Due to his statement: 'The days of sacrifice are three, the best of them is the first.' Tawaf al-rukn is the obligatory tawaf in Hajj, and it is a rukn therein, and it is called Tawaf al-Ziyarah, Tawaf al-Ifadah, and Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr. (Mukhtasar for rukn: when you come to Mecca, perform tawaf for the sake of Tawaf al-Rukn, and its time is from dawn of the Day of Sacrifice to the end of life. (T, A) Seven circuits, four of which are rukn and the remainder wajib. (T)] It is necessary to be standing and walking. If one performs tawaf sitting, only the lower half of his legs, or carried, or riding, and sa'y likewise, a dam is required, and it is not permissible if he is fleeing from an enemy or seeking a debtor. Likewise, it is necessary to be in a state of purity and to have the 'awrah covered. His statement: 'without raml and sa'y if you have already performed them' because repetition of them is not prescribed. (Fath) 'If you have already performed them' i.e. raml and sa'y in Tawaf al-Qudum. (T) 'Otherwise do them' i.e. raml and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah. It would have been better to say: 'otherwise do them' in the imperative form. - And pray two rak'ahs after this tawaf. (T, A) And women become permissible for you: (by the previous shaving, not by this tawaf, so if he performed tawaf before shaving, nothing becomes permissible for him. If he cut his nail, for example, it would be a violation. (T)] i.e. when you perform Tawaf al-Rukn, women become permissible for you by consensus of the Ummah; because the prohibition was due to Hajj and it has been completed. The permissibility of women is by the previous shaving, not by tawaf; because the cause of tahlil (shaving) is prior to tawaf, but it delays its effect until after tawaf, like revocable divorce delays its effect until the end of the waiting period. When the waiting period ends, the divorce takes effect and she becomes irrevocably separated. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 3/311) And tawaf is a rukn of Hajj, and tahlil from acts of worship is not by a rukn, but by that which is prohibited in that worship. (Ayni, Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah) and what becomes permissible after it. The author begins by stating that after shaving, the pilgrim goes to Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice or the following days to perform seven circuits of tawaf. Raml (quick pace) and sa'y are not repeated if already performed in Tawaf al-Qudum. The key ruling: after this tawaf, women become permissible (excluding intercourse until after shaving? Actually the text clarifies it is by shaving, but the permission is actualized after tawaf). The author addresses a dispute with Malik regarding perfume. Malik argues perfume remains prohibited because it is a cause of intercourse. The Hanafi proof is the hadith from Aisha: 'When you have thrown and slaughtered, everything becomes permissible except women, and clothes and perfume become permissible.' This khabar wahid overrides qiyas. Another dispute with Shafi'i: he considers ramy itself a cause of tahlil, but Hanafi refutes by analogy: shaving out of time is a violation (requires dam), but ramy out of time is not similarly a violation. The author then explains the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah: from the 10th to the 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah, with the 10th being best. The proof is Quranic: the conjunction of tawaf with slaughter in Surah al-Hajj. The tawaf consists of seven circuits, four of which are rukn (pillar) and three are wajib. Conditions: one must be standing, walking, in a state of purity, and with 'awrah covered. If any condition is missed (e.g., riding), a dam is required. The author concludes by affirming that the permissibility of women is through shaving, but its effect is postponed until tawaf is performed, analogous to revocable divorce. Tawaf is a rukn, and tahlil is not achieved by a rukn but by something prohibited in ihram (like shaving).

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The essential tawaf of Hajj performed after coming from Mina on the 10th-12th of Dhul Hijjah.
التحليل (al-tahlil): The state of being permissible after ihram restrictions are lifted.
الرمي (al-ramy): Throwing pebbles at the jamarat.

D) Only before sunset on the 12th

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn of Hajj with four fard circuits and three wajib circuits; it must be performed standing, walking, pure, and with awrah covered; its time extends from dawn of the 10th to end of life.

Tahlil: When Perfume and Women Become Permissible
Disputes over permissibility of perfume and women, and the role of ramy in tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when perfume and women become permissible after Hajj and evaluate the Maliki and Shafi'i counter-arguments.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, perfume is permissible after ramy and slaughter, based on a hadith that overrides qiyas; women become permissible after tawaf al-ziyarah by way of shaving.

This passage addresses a key question: when does the pilgrim become fully permissible to use perfume and engage in marital relations? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the permissibility of perfume (after ramy and shaving) and women (after tawaf), relying on a hadith from Aisha. It also addresses the role of ramy (stoning) in tahlil, rejecting the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on perfume
The Hanafi school holds that perfume becomes permissible immediately after ramy and slaughter, even before tawaf. This is based on the hadith: 'When you have thrown and slaughtered, everything becomes permissible... except women, and clothes and perfume become permissible.'
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) that overrides qiyas.
2
Understand the Maliki objection
Malik argued that perfume is a cause of intercourse, so it should remain prohibited until women become permissible. The Hanafi response is that the hadith (khabar wahid) takes precedence over qiyas.
This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle: khabar wahid over qiyas.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i view on ramy
Al-Shafi'i considered ramy itself a cause of tahlil, by analogy to shaving. The Hanafi response is that a cause of tahlil would be a violation if done out of time, but ramy is not a violation out of time.
Ramy has a specific time, but missing it does not require dam like shaving out of time.
4
Determine when women become permissible
The text clarifies that women become permissible after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, but the actual cause is shaving. Tawaf simply activates the effect, similar to revocable divorce taking effect after the waiting period.
Thus, shaving is the primary cause; tawaf is required for permission to take effect.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
According to Hanafi, a pilgrim can use perfume after ramy and slaughter; according to Maliki, not until after tawaf. This affects the pilgrim's actions in Mina.
Also, Shafi'i considers ramy as a cause, so the pilgrim has more flexibility in timing?

Rulings of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling with proof on Tawaf al-Ziyarah: timing, conditions, and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, explain its timing and conditions, and differentiate between the Hanafi position and opposing schools on perfume and the cause of tahlil.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory rukn of Hajj; it permits everything except women, but tahlil from women is achieved by halq, delayed until tawaf.

This passage from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq commentary expands on Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah or Tawaf al-Rukn. It details the time for this tawaf, the conditions for its validity, and the disputes with Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding what becomes permissible after the preliminary acts on Yawm al-Nahr. Particularly important is the Hanafi emphasis that tahlil (permissibility) from women is not directly caused by the tawaf but by halq (shaving), whose effect is delayed until the tawaf is performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage to determine what act is being discussed (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) and its legal classification (fard, rukn of Hajj). Note that it is obligatory (fard 'ayn) and a pillar without which Hajj is invalid.
The passage also mentions alternative names: Tawaf al-Ifadah and Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr.
2
Determine the time and conditions
Extract the timing: from dawn of 10th Dhul Hijjah until the end of life, with the first of the three days of Nahr being best. Identify the conditions: performed standing and walking, in a state of purity, with 'awrah covered; violation requires a dam.
Also note that raml and sa'y are included if not performed earlier in Tawaf al-Qudum.
3
Analyze the disputes with Malik and al-Shafi'i
Read the arguments: Malik prohibited perfume even after ramy and dhabh; the Hanafi response cites the hadith from 'Aisha (radiyallahu 'anha). Al-Shafi'i considered ramy a cause of tahlil; the Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes ramy from halq.
The Hanafi principle: khabar al-wahid supersedes qiyas.
4
Understand the role of halq in tahlil
Note the distinction: tawaf is a rukn, but tahlil from women is by halq. The effect of halq is delayed until tawaf is performed, analogous to revocable divorce where the divorce acts only after the 'iddah.
This is a key Hanafi unique position.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi position
Synthesize: Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn performed during the days of Nahr; after ramy and dhabh, everything except women is halal; after tawaf, women become halal due to halq; conditions and penalties apply.
The relied-upon view is based on the hadith and Hanafi usul.

كتاب الحج
كيفية الحج
وحلّ لك غيرُ النساء، ثم إلى مكة يوم النحر أو غداً أو بعده، فطف للركن سبعة أشواط بلا رمل وسعى إن قدمتهما وإلا فعلا، وحل لك النساء، في الطواف إن لم تكن قدمتهما حل لك كل شيء من محظورات الإحرام. (ط) غير النساء [ أي غير الجماع بهن ودواعيه كالمس والقبلة. (ط)] وقال مالك: لا يحل له الطيب أيضاً؛ لأنه من دواعي الجماع، ولنا: ماروت عائشة ما قالت: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إذا رميتم وذبحتم فقد حل لكم كل شيء إلا النساء، وحل لكم الثياب والطيب"، رواه الدار قطني، وخبر الواحد يترك به القياس، ثم الرمي ليس بسبب التحليل عندنا، وقال الشافعي: هو سبب التحليل أيضاً؛ لأنه يتوقت بيوم النحر كالحلق، فيكون بمنزلته في التحليل ولنا أن ما يكون محللاً يكون جناية في غير أوانه كالحلق، والرمي ليس كذلك. (عيني، مستخلص) أو بعده: [ أي بعد غد النحر، وأولها أفضلها. (ط،ع)] وهذه الأيام الثلاث، أي من عاشر ذي الحجة إلى ثاني عشر منه أيام النحر، وهي وقت طواف الزيارة؛ لأن الله تعالى عطف الطواف على الذبح والأكل منه، فقال: ﴿فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأَطْعِمُوا الْبَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ (الحج: ۲۸)، ثم قال: ﴿ وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بالبيت العتيق (الحج: ۲۹)، والعطف يقتضي المشاركة في الحكم بين المعطوف والمعطوف عليه إذا كان بحرف الواو، والذبح مؤقت بأيام النحر فكذا الطواف، فكان وقتهما واحداً، وأولها أفضلها. رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/١] لقوله عليه: "أيام النحر ثلاثة أفضلها أولها"، وطواف الركن هو الطواف المفروض في الحج وهو ركن فيه، ويسمى طواف الزيارة وطواف الإفاضة وطواف يوم النحر (مستخلص للركن أي إذا أتيت مكة طف لأجل طواف الركن، ووقته من طلوع فجر النحر إلى آخر العمر. (ط،ع)
سبعة أشواط والركن منها أربع، والباقي واجب. (ط)] يجب أن يكون قائماً ماشياً، ولو طاف ناصباً أنصاف ساقيه فقط أو محمولاً أو راكباً وسعى كذلك، لزمه دم ولا يجوز لو طاف هارباً من عدو أو طالباً لغريم، وكذا يجب أن يكون على طهارة وأن يكون مستور العورة. وقوله: "بلا رمل وسعي إن قدمتهما ؛ لأن التكرار فيهما لم يشرع. (فتح) قدمتهما: أي الرمل والسعي في طواف القدوم رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/١] (ط) وإلا فعلا: أي الرمل والسعي في طواف الزيارة، وكان ينبغي أن يقول: وإلا افعلهما بصيغة الأمر - وصل ركعتين عقب هذا الطواف. (ط،ع) وحل لك النساء: [بالحلق السابق لا بهذا الطواف حتى لو طاف قبل الحلق لم يحل له شيء، فلو قلم ظفره مثلاً كان جناية. (ط)] أي إذا طفت طواف الركن حل لك النساء لإجماع الأمة على ذلك؛ لأن المنع كان للحج و قد تم، وحلة النساء إنما هو بالحلق السابق لا بالطواف؛ لأن المحلل دون الطواف غير أنه أخر عمله إلى هو ما بعد الطواف، فإذا حصل الطواف عمل الحلق عمله كالطلاق الرجعي أخر عمله إلى انقضاء العدة؛ لحاجته إلى الاسترداد، فإذا انقضت عمل الطلاق عمله فبانت منه تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۱/٢] والطواف ركن من أركان الحج، والتحليل عن العبادات لا يكون بركن، بل بما هو محظور في تلك العبادة. (عيني، مستخلص)
Book of Hajj. Manner of Hajj. And permitted for you is other than women, then to Mecca on the Day of Nahr or the next day or after it, and perform tawaf for the corner seven circuits without raml and sa'y if you had performed them earlier, otherwise do them, and women become permitted for you. In the tawaf, if you had not performed them earlier, everything which was prohibited during ihram becomes permitted for you, except women. (T) except women [i.e., except intercourse with them and its foreplay like touch and kiss. (T)] Malik said: Perfume is also not permitted for him because it is a foreplay to intercourse. Our proof: 'Aisha narrated that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'When you have thrown the stones and sacrificed, everything becomes permitted for you except women, and garments and perfume become permitted for you.' Reported by al-Daraqutni, and the solitary report supersedes analogy. Then throwing stones is not a cause of tahlil according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: It is also a cause of tahlil because it is time-specific to the Day of Nahr like shaving, so it takes its place in tahlil. Our proof: That which is a cause of tahlil would be an offense if done out of its proper time, like shaving, and throwing stones is not like that. (al-'Ayni, Mukhtasar) Or after it: [i.e., after the day after Nahr, and the first of them is the best. (T, 'A)] And these three days, i.e., from the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah to the 12th of it, are the days of Nahr, and they are the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah because Allah the Almighty connected the tawaf to the slaughtering and eating from it, saying: 'So eat of them and feed the miserable poor' (22:28), then He said: 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House' (22:29). And the conjunction requires sharing in the ruling between the conjoined and the conjoined-to when it is with the letter waw. The slaughtering is time-bound to the days of Nahr, so likewise the tawaf. Thus their time is one, and the first of them is the best. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 161/1) Due to his statement ﷺ: 'The days of Nahr are three, the best of them is the first.' And Tawaf al-Rukn is the obligatory tawaf in Hajj and it is a rukn in it, and it is called Tawaf al-Ziyarah, Tawaf al-Ifadah, and Tawaf Yawm al-Nahr. (Mukhtasar for 'arm'? i.e., when you come to Mecca, perform tawaf for the sake of the rukn tawaf, and its time is from the dawn of the Day of Nahr until the end of one's life. (T, 'A) Seven circuits, and the rukn from them is four, and the remainder is wajib. (T) It must be performed standing and walking, and if one performed tawaf resting on half of his shins only, or carried, or riding, and likewise sa'y, then a dam is due, and it is not permissible if one performed tawaf fleeing from an enemy or seeking a debtor. Likewise, it must be performed in a state of purity and with the 'awrah covered. And his statement: 'without raml and sa'y if you had performed them earlier' because repetition in them is not legislated. (Fath) 'if you had performed them earlier' i.e., raml and sa'y in Tawaf al-Qudum (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 161/1) (T) 'otherwise do them' i.e., raml and sa'y in Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and it would have been better if he said 'otherwise do them' in the imperative form. And pray two rak'ahs after this tawaf. (T, 'A) 'And women become permitted for you' [by the previous shaving, not by this tawaf, such that if he performed tawaf before shaving, nothing becomes permitted for him. So if he trimmed his nail, for example, it would be an offense. (T)] i.e., when you perform Tawaf al-Rukn, women become permitted for you due to the consensus of the Ummah on that, because the prohibition was due to Hajj and it has been completed. And the permissibility of women is only by the previous shaving, not by the tawaf, because the thing that permits is less than the tawaf, except that it delays its effect until after the tawaf. So when the tawaf occurs, shaving acts as it would, like revocable divorce which delays its effect until the expiration of the 'iddah due to the need for revocation; when the 'iddah ends, the divorce acts and she becomes irrevocably divorced. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 311/2) And tawaf is a rukn of the pillars of Hajj, and tahlil from acts of worship is not by a rukn, but rather by that which is prohibited in that worship. (al-'Ayni, Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah or Tawaf al-Rukn), its timing, conditions, and effects. The author begins by citing the matn that after performing the actions on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah) or the following days, one performs seven circuits of tawaf without raml (quick walking) and sa'y if these were already done in Tawaf al-Qudum; otherwise one performs them. Then he explains that the permissibility of everything except women (specifically intercourse) is achieved by the tawaf if sa'y and raml were not done earlier. The commentary then addresses a dispute with Imam Malik, who held that perfume is also prohibited even after tawaf because it is a foreplay to intercourse. The Hanafi response cites a hadith from 'Aisha (radiyallahu 'anha) reported by al-Daraqutni that the Prophet ﷺ specifically included perfume as permissible after ramy and dhabh. The text asserts that the solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) supersedes analogy. Then a dispute with al-Shafi'i is presented: he considered ramy (stoning) as also a cause of tahlil because it is time-specific like halq. The Hanafi rebuttal is that only halq (or taqsir) is a valid cause of tahlil; performing ramy out of its time is not an offense, whereas shaving out of time is, so the analogy is invalid. The passage then defines the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah as the three days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah), citing the verse (22:28-29) where tawaf is conjoined to dhabh with the waw, implying they share the same time. The first day is best, based on a hadith. Tawaf al-Rukn is the obligatory tawaf (fardh) and is a rukn; it has other names. Its time extends from dawn on the 10th until the end of life. Four circuits are the rukn, the remaining three are wajib. Conditions include walking (based on ability), purity, covering 'awrah. Violations necessitate a dam (sacrificial penalty). Finally, the passage clarifies that the tahlil (permissibility) regarding women is actually achieved by halq, not tawaf, but halq's effect is delayed until tawaf is performed, analogous to revocable divorce where the effect of divorce is delayed until the 'iddah ends. The tawaf itself is a rukn, and tahlil from the state of ihram is not by the rukn but by the prohibited act (i.e., halq). This technical distinction is important.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed after coming from 'Arafah and Muzdalifah to Mecca during the days of Nahr; it is a rukn of Hajj.
رمي الجمار (Ramy al-Jimar): The act of throwing pebbles at the three jamarat in Mina on specific days.
حلق (Halq): Shaving the head (or taqsir: trimming) after ramy and dhabh on Yawm al-Nahr; it is the primary cause of tahlil from ihram in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary cause of tahlil (permissibility to resume prohibited acts) after ihram?
A) Ramy al-Jimar
B) Tawaf al-Ziyarah
C) Halq (shaving/trimming hair)
D) Slaughtering the sacrifice

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn of Hajj performed during the days of Nahr; its performance with proper conditions is essential, and tahlil from women is ultimately achieved by halq, not by tawaf itself.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Timing and Order of Ramy al-Jimar
Ruling with proof on ramy al-jimar timing and order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the time, order, and sunan of ramy al-jimar, and apply the compensation rules for delay or omission.

Core Idea
Stone after zawaal in order; stand and supplicate at the first two jamarat, but not at al-Aqaba.

Ramy al-jimar is a wajib act of Hajj performed on the days of Tashriq. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the preferred time (after zawaal), the sequence of stoning the three jamarat, and the sunnah of standing and making du'a at the first two. It also covers what to do if the ramy is delayed and the compensation (dam) required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ramy al-jimar (stoning the three pillars) during Ayyam al-Tashriq. It is wajib in the Hanafi school – omission requires a dam (sacrifice).
Wajib falls short of fard but still obligatory; missing it intentionally or unintentionally requires compensation.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from 'Aisha describing the Prophet's practice of stoning after zawaal, and from Jabir confirming that on the Day of Nahr he stoned in the forenoon but on following days after zawaal.
The dalil is ahad but its meaning (dalala) is clear, establishing the rule.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent action of stoning after zawaal on the Tashriq days indicates that this is the optimal time. The hadith explicitly states he did so after zawaal, making it the preferred (afdal) time.
Hanafi usul: فعل النبي (fi‘l al-nabi) when continuous and without a known reason indicates wujub or at least nadb (recommendation). Here it indicates wujub of the act itself, but the timing is a condition of perfection.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A narration from Abu Hanifa holds that stoning after zawaal is only wajib (not a strict condition), meaning stoning before zawaal suffices but is makruh. The well-known (mashhur) view is that after zawaal is the proper time and stoning before is valid but disliked.
The text says 'the apparent is the first' (الظاهر الأول), indicating the mashhur view is relied upon.
5
Determine the consequences of delay
If all ramy is delayed until the fourth day (13th), he must stone in order and owes one dam. If delayed beyond sunset of the last day, the obligation drops and one dam is due.
The order must be preserved even when making up; compensation (dam) is single according to Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فارم الجمار: لما روي عن عائشة لما أنها قالت: "أفاض النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من يومه حتى صلى الظهر، ثم رجع إلى منى، فمكث بها أيام التشريق يرمي الجمار، فإذا زالت الشمس يرمي كل جمرة بسبع حصيات، يكبر مع كل حصاة، ويقف عند الأولى والثانية، فيطيل القيام ويتضرع ويرمي الثالثة ولا يقف عندها"، رواه أبو داود، وقال جابر : "رأيت رسول الله يرمي على راحلته يوم النحر ضحى، وأما بعد ذلك فبعد زوال الشمس"، رواه مسلم. [تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۲/۲] الثلاث وهي الجمرة الأولى والوسطى والأخيرة. (ع) بعد الزوال: [في الصحيح إلى طلوع الشمس من ا غدا الغد، فلو رمي صح، وكره. (ط)] بيان لأول وقت الرمي، وهذا هو المشهور عن الإمام وعنه أنه واجب فقط، حتى لو رمى قبله أجزأه والمروي من فعله عليها لبيان الأفضل، والظاهر الأول، وآخره عند طلوع الشمس من ليلاً صح وكره، ولو أخر رمي الجمار كلها إلى اليوم الرابع رماها على الترتيب؛ لأن أيام التشريق كلها وقت الرمي، فيقضي مرتباً، وعليه دم واحد عند الإمام، ولو أخرها حتى غابت الشمس من آخر أيام التشريق سقط؛ لانقضاء وقته وعليه دم واحد يلي المسجد أي مبتدئا بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف استنانا. (ط، ع) ثم بما يليها: أي بالجمرة التي تلي الجمرة الأولى، وهي الجمرة الوسطى. (ط ، ع) بجمرة العقبة بسبع حصيات كذلك ورد الآثار. (ط،ع) وقف عند كل إلخ [حامداً مكبراً مهللاً مصلياً داعياً قدر قرأة البقرة. (ط)] وهو ما سوى جمرة العقبة، فإنه لا رمي بعدها، فلا يقف عندها، ويقف عند الجمرتين الأوليين، فيحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويهلل ويكبر ويصلي على النبي ويدعو لحاجته، ويرفع يديه في الدعاء؛ لقوله عليه: "لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن"، وذكر من جملتها عند الجمرتين، وينبغي أن يستغفر للمؤمنين في دعائه في هذا الموقف؛ لأن النبي عليه قال: "اللهم اغفر للحاج ولمن استغفر له الحاج"، فالحاصل أن كل رمي بعده رمي يقف عندها؛ لأنه في وسط العبادة فيتأدى بالدعاء فيه، وكل رمي لا يقف عنده؛ لأن العبادة انتهت ولهذا لا يقف عند الجمرة العقبة في يوم النحر وبعده. (مستخلص) ثم غداً كذلك: أي ارم في غد ثاني النحر وهو : ثالث أيام النحر ، يعني الثاني عشر من ذي الحجة. (ط،ع) ليس بعده رمي
So stone the jamarat: because of what is narrated from 'Aisha that she said: 'The Prophet ﷺ performed tawaf al-ifadah from his day until he prayed Dhuhr, then returned to Mina, and stayed there during the days of Tashriq stoning the jamarat. When the sun passed the meridian, he stoned each jamrah with seven pebbles, saying Allahu Akbar with each pebble. He stood at the first and second and lengthened the standing and supplicated, and he stoned the third and did not stand at it.' Reported by Abu Dawud. And Jabir said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah stoning on his mount on the Day of Nahr in the forenoon, but afterwards after the sun's decline.' Reported by Muslim. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 312/2] The three, namely the first, middle, and last jamrah. ('A) After zawaal: [In Sahih, until sunrise of the day after the next day, so if he stoned, it is valid but disliked. (T)] Explanation of the beginning time of stoning, and this is the well-known from the Imam, and from him it is that it is only wajib, so if he stoned before it, it suffices him, and what is reported of his action on her is to show the best. The apparent is the first. And its end is at sunrise, so if he stones at night, it is valid but disliked. And if he delayed all the stoning of the jamarat until the fourth day, he stones them in order, because all the days of Tashriq are time for stoning, so he makes them up in order, and upon him is one dam according to the Imam. And if he delayed them until the sun set from the last day of Tashriq, it is dropped due to the expiration of its time, and upon him is one dam. 'Adjacent to the mosque', i.e., beginning with the jamrah that is adjacent to the mosque of al-Khayf as a sunnah. (T, 'A) 'Then what is next to it', i.e., the jamrah that is next to the first jamrah, which is the middle jamrah. (T, 'A) 'At Jamrat al-'Aqaba with seven pebbles', as the reports have come. (T, 'A) 'He stands at each, etc.' [praising Allah, declaring His greatness, saying La ilaha illallah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and supplicating for the duration of reciting al-Baqarah. (T)] And this is other than Jamrat al-'Aqaba, for there is no stoning after it, so he does not stand at it. He stands at the first two jamarah, and he praises Allah and thanks Him, and declares His greatness, and sends blessings on the Prophet, and supplicates for his need, and raises his hands in supplication, because of his statement ﷺ: 'Do not raise hands except in seven situations', and he mentioned among them at the two jamarat. And it is recommended to ask forgiveness for the believers in his supplication in this standing, because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'O Allah, forgive the pilgrim and the one for whom the pilgrim asks forgiveness.' The conclusion is that every stoning after which there is stoning, he stands at it, because he is in the midst of the worship so he occupies himself with supplication; and every stoning after which there is no stoning, he does not stand at it, because the worship has ended. For this reason he does not stand at Jamrat al-'Aqaba on the Day of Nahr and after it. (Mukhtasar) 'Then the next day likewise', i.e., stone on the day after the second of Nahr, which is the third day of Nahr, meaning the 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah. (T, 'A) After it there is no stoning.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed exposition of the ramy al-jimar (stoning of the jamarat) during the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah). It begins by citing a hadith from 'Aisha (radiyallahu 'anha) describing the Prophet's ﷺ practice: after performing Tawaf al-Ifadah on the Day of Nahr, he returned to Mina and, during the days of Tashriq, stoned the three jamarat after the sun's decline (zawaal). He stood and supplicated at the first and second jamarat but not at the third (Jamrat al-'Aqaba). Another hadith from Jabir confirms that stoning on the Day of Nahr is in the forenoon, but for the following days after zawaal. The preferred time for stoning is after zawaal, and this is the well-known view of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, there is a narration from him that it is only wajib (i.e., stoning before zawaal suffices but is less than optimal). The end time for stoning each day is until sunrise of the next day; if one stones at night (after sunset?), it is valid but disliked. If a pilgrim delays all stonings until the fourth day (13th), he must stone them in order (first, then middle, then 'Aqaba) because all the days of Tashriq are a time for ramy. In this case, a single dam is due according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If he delays until after sunset on the last day (13th), the ramy is dropped (no longer required) but a dam is due. The passage then explains the order: start with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf (the first), then the middle, then Jamrat al-'Aqaba, each with seven pebbles. At the first two jamarat, it is sunnah to stand and make lengthy supplication (praising Allah, saying takbeer, tahlil, sending blessings on the Prophet, and raising hands), based on hadith. No standing at Jamrat al-'Aqaba because there is no ramy after it. The purpose of standing is to be engaged in dhikr and dua while in the midst of the worship; since at 'Aqaba the worship ends, there is no standing. Also, it is recommended to ask forgiveness for all believers, citing a hadith. The passage concludes by clarifying that 'then the next day likewise' refers to the 12th (third day of Nahr), and after that there is no ramy (i.e., those who leave on the 12th do not stone on the 13th).

Key Terms
الجمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-'Aqaba): The last of the three jamarat in Mina, located nearest to Mecca; on the Day of Nahr it is stoned in the forenoon, and on the following days after zawaal, but no standing is performed there.
أيام التشريق (Ayyam al-Tashriq): The three days following Yawm al-Nahr: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhu al-Hijjah, during which ramy al-jimar is performed.
دم (Dam): A sacrificial animal required as compensation for omitting or delaying ramy al-jimar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only the third ('Aqaba)

Key Takeaway
Ramy al-jimar is wajib; the time after zawaal is preferred, and standing with du'a is sunnah at the first two jamarat, but not at Jamrat al-'Aqaba.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

8 min
Ruling on Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute over Dam
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and qiyas proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying tawaf al-ziyarah, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a dam is required, and explain the proof from qiyas.

Core Idea
Delaying tawaf beyond days of Nahr is makruh; Abu Hanifa holds dam is wajib, Sahibayn disagree.

Tawaf al-ziyarah is a pillar of Hajj that must be performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah or the following days. But what if a pilgrim delays it beyond the days of Nahr? This lesson examines the ruling according to the Hanafi school, focusing on the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
The act is delaying tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of Nahr (10th–12th of Dhul Hijjah) without a valid excuse.
2
Determine the hukm level
According to the text, such delay is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked) if without excuse.
Abu Hanifa adds a wajib penalty (dam).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa requires a dam; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not require a dam.
The text presents both views without explicit tarjih.
4
Analyze the proof
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas: just as the sacrifice (udhiyah) is tied to the days of Nahr, so is tawaf al-ziyarah, because both are conjoined in Quranic verse.
The Sahibayn presumably do not accept the strength of this qiyas.
5
Practical consequence
If a pilgrim delays tawaf without excuse, a dam is due according to Abu Hanifa; no dam according to the Sahibayn.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is not specified in the text.
