كتاب الحج
كيفية الحج
وكره تأخيره عن أيام النحر، ثم إلى منى فارم الجمار الثلاث في ثاني النحر بعد تحريماً أي طواف الركن ولزمه دم رح من مكة أي أيام الزوال باديا بما يلي المسجد، ثم بما يليها، ثم بجمرة العقبة، وقف عند كل رمي بعده رمي، ثم غداً كذلك. أي كما رميت في ثاني النحر وكره تأخيره أي تأخير طواف الزيارة عن أيام النحر - وهي يوم النحر واليومان بعده – مكروه حيث كان لغير عذر، ولزمه بالتأخير عند دم أبي حنيفة خلافاً لصاحبيه؛ لأن الذبح مؤقت بأيام النحر، فكذا الطواف مؤقت بهما؛ لأنه معطوف عليها في الآية كما تقدم، والركن منه أربعة أشواط، فلو طاف أربعة أشواط قبل الغروب لا شيء عليه، وقيل: إن آخره آخر أيام التشريق، وفي "الغاية": إن آخره عند محمد غير مؤقت. (عيني، فتح) فارم الجمار: لما روي عن عائشة لما أنها قالت: "أفاض النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من يومه حتى صلى الظهر، ثم رجع إلى منى، فمكث بها أيام التشريق يرمي الجمار، فإذا زالت الشمس يرمي كل جمرة بسبع حصيات، يكبر مع كل حصاة، ويقف عند الأولى والثانية، فيطيل القيام ويتضرع ويرمي الثالثة ولا يقف عندها"، رواه أبو داود، وقال جابر : "رأيت رسول الله يرمي على راحلته يوم النحر ضحى، وأما بعد ذلك فبعد زوال الشمس"، رواه مسلم. [تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۲/۲] الثلاث وهي الجمرة الأولى والوسطى والأخيرة. (ع) بعد الزوال: [في الصحيح إلى طلوع الشمس من ا غدا الغد، فلو رمي صح، وكره. (ط)] بيان لأول وقت الرمي، وهذا هو المشهور عن الإمام وعنه أنه واجب فقط، حتى لو رمى قبله أجزأه والمروي من فعله عليها لبيان الأفضل، والظاهر الأول، وآخره عند طلوع الشمس من ليلاً صح وكره، ولو أخر رمي الجمار كلها إلى اليوم الرابع رماها على الترتيب؛ لأن أيام التشريق كلها وقت الرمي، فيقضي مرتباً، وعليه دم واحد عند الإمام، ولو أخرها حتى غابت الشمس من آخر أيام التشريق سقط؛ لانقضاء وقته وعليه دم واحد يلي المسجد أي مبتدئا بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف استنانا. (ط، ع) ثم بما يليها: أي بالجمرة التي تلي الجمرة الأولى، وهي الجمرة الوسطى. (ط ، ع) بجمرة العقبة بسبع حصيات كذلك ورد الآثار. (ط،ع) وقف عند كل إلخ [حامداً مكبراً مهللاً مصلياً داعياً قدر قرأة البقرة. (ط)] وهو ما سوى جمرة العقبة، فإنه لا رمي الغد، فلو رمي اتفاقاً . (فتح) بعدها، فلا يقف عندها، ويقف عند الجمرتين الأوليين، فيحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويهلل ويكبر ويصلي على النبي ويدعو لحاجته، ويرفع يديه في الدعاء؛ لقوله عليه: "لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن"، وذكر من جملتها عند الجمرتين، وينبغي أن يستغفر للمؤمنين في دعائه في هذا الموقف؛ لأن النبي عليه قال: "اللهم اغفر للحاج ولمن استغفر له الحاج"، فالحاصل أن كل رمي بعده رمي يقف عندها؛ لأنه في وسط العبادة فيتأدى بالدعاء فيه، وكل رمي لا يقف عنده؛ لأن العبادة انتهت ولهذا لا يقف عند الجمرة العقبة في يوم النحر وبعده. (مستخلص) ثم غداً كذلك: أي ارم في غد ثاني النحر وهو : ثالث أيام النحر ، يعني الثاني عشر من ذي الحجة. (ط،ع) ليس بعده رمي

ثم بعده كذلك إن مكثت ولو رميت في اليوم الرابع قبل الزوال صح، وكل رمي أي كما رميت في اليومين قبله الجمار الثلاث بعده رمی فارم ماشيا وإلا راكبا رخص بعد طلوع الشمس إن مكثت: [في منى ؛ لأنه مخير في المكث؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ تَعَجَلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ تَأَخَّرَ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ لِمَنِ اتَّقَى ﴾ (البقرة :۲۰۳) (ع)] فيه إيماء إلى تخييره بين المكث ،وعدمه، والمكث أفضل اقتداء بفعله عليه؛ لقوله تعالى: فَمَنْ تَعَجَّلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ ﴾ (البقرة:۲۰۳) الآية، ولك أن تنفر ما لم يطلع الفجر من اليوم الرابع، فإذا طلع الفجر لا يحل لك أن تنفر؛ لدخول وقت الرمي، وقال الشافعي: إذا غربت الشمس من اليوم الثالث لا يحل لك النفر حتى ترمي الجمار الثلاث في اليوم الرابع، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأن النفر أبيح في اليوم؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ تَعَجَّلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عليه لا في الليل، وجه الظاهر: أنه نفر في وقت لا يجب فيه الرمي ولا يجوز، فجاز له النفر كالنهار. (مسكين، فتح) الثالث اليوم: وهو أيام الرمي. (ع) صح: أي عند الإمام، وعندهما: لا من اعتباراً بسائر الأيام، وإنما يصح له فيه في النفر، فإذا لم يترخص بالنفر التحق بسائر الأيام، ومذهبه مروي عن ابن عباس ما؛ ولأنه لما ظهر أثر التخفيف فيه في حق ترك الرمي فلأن يظهر جوازه في الأوقات كلها أولى بخلاف اليوم الأول والثاني من أيام التشريق؛ حيث لا يجوز فيهما إلا بعد الزوال؛ لأنه يجوز تركه فيهما فكذا لا يجوز تقديمه، ولا كلام في أفضلية الرمي بعد الزوال. [تبيين الحقائق: ٣١٤/٢] (فتح) رمي: كرمي الجمرتين الأولى والوسطى في الأيام الثلاث. رمز الحقائق ١٦٢/١] فارم ماشياً: [حال كونك ماشيا ندبا، فلو رميتها راكبا جاز. (ط) مسكين)] لأن ما ورد من أنه عليها رمى جمرة العقبة راكباً، يدل على ذلك، وعن ابن عمر لما أنه كان يرمي جمرة العقبة يوم النحر راكباً، وسائر ذلك ماشياً، ويخبرهم أنه عليه كان يفعل ذلك، وقال بعضهم: الأفضل الرمي ماشياً في زماننا؛ لأنه أقرب إلى التضرع والتواضع، وذكر إبراهيم بن الجراح وهو من أكبر تلامذة عطاء بن أبي رباح تلميذ ابن عباس، وكان عالماً بالمناسك، قال: دخلت على أبي يوسف وقد أغمي عليه، فأفاق، فلما رآني قال: يا إبراهيم ما تقول في رمي الجمار يرميها الحاج راكباً أو ماشياً؟ فقلت: يرميها ماشياً، فقال: أخطأت فقلت: يرميها راكباً، فقال: أخطأت قلت فما يقول الإمام: قال: كل رمي ماشياً، وكل رمي ليس بعده رمي يرميها راكباً، فخرجت من عنده، فسمعت بكاء الناس في داره، فقيل لي: قضي أبو يوسف عليه، فتعجبت من حرصه على العلم في هذه الحالة. (مستخلص، فتح) وإلا : أي وإن لم يكن بعده رمي كجمرة العقبة يوم النحر والجمرة الأخيرة في الأيام الثلاث. (ع) راكباً [ أي ارم حال كونك راكباً (ع)] يدل عليه ما روي أنه علي رمى جمرة العقبة راكباً يوم النحر، وهذا بيان الأفضلية، وأما الجواز فثابت كيف ما كان رمز الحقائق: ١٦٢/١] وقال في النهر: إن الرمي راكباً أفضل مطلقاً عند الإمام ومحمد؛ لأن الثابت عنه عليها إنما هو الرمي راكباً فحينئذ الرمي ماشياً خلاف السنة، قلنا: إنما فعله ليكون أظهر للناس حتى يقتدوا به فيما يشاهدونه منه عليه. (فتح)
رمي يرميها
بعده
Book of Hajj. The manner of Hajj. It is disliked to delay (tawaf) beyond the days of Nahr, then to Mina and stone the three jamarat on the second day of Nahr after (the tawaf) is (obligatory?) meaning the pillar tawaf, and a sacrifice becomes due... (detailed translation of the whole passage would be very long; abbreviated here for brevity)
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of ramy al-jimar (stoning the pillars) and the delay of tawaf al-ziyarah. It begins by stating that it is disliked (makruh) to delay tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of Nahr (10th to 12th of Dhul Hijjah) without an excuse. According to Abu Hanifa, delaying it necessitates a dam (sacrifice), but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, holding that no dam is required. The reasoning is that just as the sacrifice is tied to these days, so is the tawaf, as it is linked in the Quranic verse. The pillar (rukn) of this tawaf is four circuits; if one performs four circuits before sunset, nothing is due. Then the text discusses the stoning ritual: it is based on the hadith of Aisha and Jabir describing the Prophet's practice. The three jamarat are the first, middle, and last (al-Aqaba). The time for stoning begins after zawaal (noon) according to the well-known view, up to sunrise of the next day; stoning before noon is valid but disliked. If one delays all stoning to the fourth day, he stones in order, and one dam is due according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If he delays until after sunset of the last day, the stoning is waived and one dam is due. The sequence: start with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then al-Aqaba. One should stand in supplication at the first two after stoning, but not at al-Aqaba. Then for the next day (12th), do the same. For those who stay (the 13th), stoning is valid even before zawaal according to Abu Hanifa. As for walking or riding: it is recommended to walk when stoning, except for the jamrah after which there is no stoning (i.e., al-Aqaba on the 10th and the last jamrah on later days), where one should ride. This is based on the practice of the Prophet and the ruling of Abu Yusuf as narrated. There is a difference of opinion on the best mode; some say walking is better for humility.

Key Terms
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The three days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba after returning from Mina, performed on 10th or following days.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for certain omissions or delays in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the consequence of delaying tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of Nahr without excuse?
A) The tawaf becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) A dam (sacrificial animal) becomes wajib.
C) The pilgrim must fast three days.
D) No penalty is required.

Key Takeaway
Delaying tawaf al-ziyarah without excuse is makruh tanzih, and Abu Hanifa requires a dam, but Sahibayn do not.

Rulings on Ramy al-Jimar: Timing, Sequence, and Mode
Expansion on stoning rulings with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the preferred time for stoning, the order of the jamarat, the recommended supplication, and the ruling on walking versus riding based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).

Core Idea
Stone after noon; stand at first two jamarat; walk except for final stoning; before noon is valid but disliked.

The stoning of the three pillars in Mina is a multi-faceted ritual. The Prophet's practice, as narrated by Aisha and Jabir, provides guidance on timing, sequence, and posture. This lesson unpacks the recommended actions and the scope of valid but disliked acts, including the difference of opinion on walking versus riding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time for stoning
The well-known view: stoning should be after zawaal (noon). Stoning before noon is valid but makruh (disliked). The time extends until sunrise of the next day for each jamrah.
The hadith of Aisha shows the Prophet stoned after zawaal.
2
Determine the sequence of the jamarat
Start with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf (the first), then the middle, then al-Aqaba (the large pillar). This order is mustahabb.
Stoning out of order is valid but makruh.
3
Note the standing (wuquf) at the first two jamarat
After stoning the first and second jamarat, it is recommended to stand and make supplication, raising hands, for the duration of reciting Surah al-Baqarah. Do not stand at al-Aqaba.
The hadith of Aisha and the practice of the Prophet are evidence.
4
Analyze walking vs riding
It is recommended to walk while stoning, except for the jamrah after which there is no further stoning (e.g., al-Aqaba on the 10th, and the final jamrah on later days) – for these, it is recommended to ride.
There is a difference: some scholars consider riding better overall.
5
Review the intra-Hanafi nuance on stoning before noon on the 13th
According to Abu Hanifa, stoning on the 13th is valid before zawaal, contrary to the Sahibayn who consider it valid only after zawaal like other days.
Abu Hanifa's view is based on the principle of alleviation (rukhsah) for those who choose to stay.

(فتح) بعدها، فلا يقف عندها، ويقف عند الجمرتين الأوليين، فيحمد الله تعالى ويثني عليه ويهلل ويكبر ويصلي على النبي ويدعو لحاجته، ويرفع يديه في الدعاء؛ لقوله عليه: "لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن"، وذكر من جملتها عند الجمرتين، وينبغي أن يستغفر للمؤمنين في دعائه في هذا الموقف؛ لأن النبي عليه قال: "اللهم اغفر للحاج ولمن استغفر له الحاج"، فالحاصل أن كل رمي بعده رمي يقف عندها؛ لأنه في وسط العبادة فيتأدى بالدعاء فيه، وكل رمي لا يقف عنده؛ لأن العبادة انتهت ولهذا لا يقف عند الجمرة العقبة في يوم النحر وبعده. (مستخلص) ثم غداً كذلك: أي ارم في غد ثاني النحر وهو : ثالث أيام النحر ، يعني الثاني عشر من ذي الحجة. (ط،ع) ليس بعده رمي

ثم بعده كذلك إن مكثت ولو رميت في اليوم الرابع قبل الزوال صح، وكل رمي أي كما رميت في اليومين قبله الجمار الثلاث بعده رمی فارم ماشيا وإلا راكبا رخص بعد طلوع الشمس إن مكثت: [في منى ؛ لأنه مخير في المكث؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ تَعَجَلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ تَأَخَّرَ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ لِمَنِ اتَّقَى ﴾ (البقرة :۲۰۳) (ع)] فيه إيماء إلى تخييره بين المكث ،وعدمه، والمكث أفضل اقتداء بفعله عليه؛ لقوله تعالى: فَمَنْ تَعَجَّلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ ﴾ (البقرة:۲۰۳) الآية، ولك أن تنفر ما لم يطلع الفجر من اليوم الرابع، فإذا طلع الفجر لا يحل لك أن تنفر؛ لدخول وقت الرمي، وقال الشافعي: إذا غربت الشمس من اليوم الثالث لا يحل لك النفر حتى ترمي الجمار الثلاث في اليوم الرابع، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأن النفر أبيح في اليوم؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ تَعَجَّلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عليه لا في الليل، وجه الظاهر: أنه نفر في وقت لا يجب فيه الرمي ولا يجوز، فجاز له النفر كالنهار. (مسكين، فتح) الثالث اليوم: وهو أيام الرمي. (ع) صح: أي عند الإمام، وعندهما: لا من اعتباراً بسائر الأيام، وإنما يصح له فيه في النفر، فإذا لم يترخص بالنفر التحق بسائر الأيام، ومذهبه مروي عن ابن عباس ما؛ ولأنه لما ظهر أثر التخفيف فيه في حق ترك الرمي فلأن يظهر جوازه في الأوقات كلها أولى بخلاف اليوم الأول والثاني من أيام التشريق؛ حيث لا يجوز فيهما إلا بعد الزوال؛ لأنه يجوز تركه فيهما فكذا لا يجوز تقديمه، ولا كلام في أفضلية الرمي بعد الزوال. [تبيين الحقائق: ٣١٤/٢] (فتح) رمي: كرمي الجمرتين الأولى والوسطى في الأيام الثلاث. رمز الحقائق ١٦٢/١] فارم ماشياً: [حال كونك ماشيا ندبا، فلو رميتها راكبا جاز. (ط) مسكين)] لأن ما ورد من أنه عليها رمى جمرة العقبة راكباً، يدل على ذلك، وعن ابن عمر لما أنه كان يرمي جمرة العقبة يوم النحر راكباً، وسائر ذلك ماشياً، ويخبرهم أنه عليه كان يفعل ذلك، وقال بعضهم: الأفضل الرمي ماشياً في زماننا؛ لأنه أقرب إلى التضرع والتواضع، وذكر إبراهيم بن الجراح وهو من أكبر تلامذة عطاء بن أبي رباح تلميذ ابن عباس، وكان عالماً بالمناسك، قال: دخلت على أبي يوسف وقد أغمي عليه، فأفاق، فلما رآني قال: يا إبراهيم ما تقول في رمي الجمار يرميها الحاج راكباً أو ماشياً؟ فقلت: يرميها ماشياً، فقال: أخطأت فقلت: يرميها راكباً، فقال: أخطأت قلت فما يقول الإمام: قال: كل رمي ماشياً، وكل رمي ليس بعده رمي يرميها راكباً، فخرجت من عنده، فسمعت بكاء الناس في داره، فقيل لي: قضي أبو يوسف عليه، فتعجبت من حرصه على العلم في هذه الحالة. (مستخلص، فتح) وإلا : أي وإن لم يكن بعده رمي كجمرة العقبة يوم النحر والجمرة الأخيرة في الأيام الثلاث. (ع) راكباً [ أي ارم حال كونك راكباً (ع)] يدل عليه ما روي أنه علي رمى جمرة العقبة راكباً يوم النحر، وهذا بيان الأفضلية، وأما الجواز فثابت كيف ما كان رمز الحقائق: ١٦٢/١] وقال في النهر: إن الرمي راكباً أفضل مطلقاً عند الإمام ومحمد؛ لأن الثابت عنه عليها إنما هو الرمي راكباً فحينئذ الرمي ماشياً خلاف السنة، قلنا: إنما فعله ليكون أظهر للناس حتى يقتدوا به فيما يشاهدونه منه عليه. (فتح)
رمي يرميها
بعده
Book of Hajj. The manner of Hajj. It is disliked to delay (tawaf) beyond the days of Nahr, then to Mina and stone the three jamarat on the second day of Nahr after (the tawaf) is (obligatory?) meaning the pillar tawaf, and a sacrifice becomes due... (detailed translation of the whole passage would be very long; abbreviated here for brevity)
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of ramy al-jimar (stoning the pillars) and the delay of tawaf al-ziyarah. It begins by stating that it is disliked (makruh) to delay tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the days of Nahr (10th to 12th of Dhul Hijjah) without an excuse. According to Abu Hanifa, delaying it necessitates a dam (sacrifice), but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, holding that no dam is required. The reasoning is that just as the sacrifice is tied to these days, so is the tawaf, as it is linked in the Quranic verse. The pillar (rukn) of this tawaf is four circuits; if one performs four circuits before sunset, nothing is due. Then the text discusses the stoning ritual: it is based on the hadith of Aisha and Jabir describing the Prophet's practice. The three jamarat are the first, middle, and last (al-Aqaba). The time for stoning begins after zawaal (noon) according to the well-known view, up to sunrise of the next day; stoning before noon is valid but disliked. If one delays all stoning to the fourth day, he stones in order, and one dam is due according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If he delays until after sunset of the last day, the stoning is waived and one dam is due. The sequence: start with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then al-Aqaba. One should stand in supplication at the first two after stoning, but not at al-Aqaba. Then for the next day (12th), do the same. For those who stay (the 13th), stoning is valid even before zawaal according to Abu Hanifa. As for walking or riding: it is recommended to walk when stoning, except for the jamrah after which there is no stoning (i.e., al-Aqaba on the 10th and the last jamrah on later days), where one should ride. This is based on the practice of the Prophet and the ruling of Abu Yusuf as narrated. There is a difference of opinion on the best mode; some say walking is better for humility.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqaba): The large pillar representing Satan at Mina, stoned on the Day of Nahr and the following days.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Nahr: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
زوال الشمس (zawal al-shams): The moment when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline, marking the start of the time for stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended mode of stoning for the first and second jamarat on a day of tashriq?
A) Walking.
B) Riding.
C) Either walking or riding equally.
D) Running.

Key Takeaway
Stoning after zawaal is sunnah; stand only at first two jamarat; walk except for the final stoning of the day.

Ruling on Stoning on the Fourth Day and Preferred Manner of Stoning
Ruling on timing of stoning on fourth day and recommendation of walking vs riding for stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of stoning before noon on the fourth day of Tashriq and explain the recommended manner of stoning (walking vs riding) with their proofs.

Core Idea
A pilgrim who stays may stone before noon on the fourth day; walk for stonings that are followed, ride for the final.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, the author explains two important details of the Hajj stoning rituals: the validity of stoning before noon on the fourth day if the pilgrim chooses to stay in Mina, and the sunnah manner of stoning—walking for the first two jamarat, riding for the final. The ruling is supported by Quranic evidence from Surah al-Baqarah and the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ). We will explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement and the Shafi'i difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
First, the ruling on the validity of stoning before noon on the fourth day if the pilgrim stays. Second, the recommended manner of stoning (walking vs riding).
Both rulings are derived from textual evidence and practice.
2
Locate the primary dalil
For the first ruling: Quran 2:203 (choice between two days). For the second: hadith of Prophet stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba riding and Ibn Umar's practice.
The Quranic verse gives general permission; the hadith provides specific sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse indicates a choice (takhyir) between departure in two days or three days; this leniency extends to allow stoning before noon on the fourth day. For the manner, the Prophet's action indicates a sunnah distinction.
Abu Hanifa's view is based on the apparent meaning (zahir) of the verse and the general leniency of the fourth day.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Sahibayn analogize to other days requiring stoning after noon. Abu Hanifa's view is preferred (mufta bihi) due to the distinct nature of the fourth day. Also note the Shafi'i opposition.
The preferred view is that of Abu Hanifa, as supported by Ibn Abbas and the principle of leniency.

Source Text

إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ تَأَخَّرَ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ لِمَنِ اتَّقَى﴾ (البقرة:۲۰۳) فيه إيماء إلى تخييره بين المكث، وعدمه، والمكث أفضل اقتداء بفعله عليه؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ تَعَجَّلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ﴾ (البقرة:۲۰۳) الآية، ولك أن تنفر ما لم يطلع الفجر من اليوم الرابع، فإذا طلع الفجر لا يحل لك أن تنفر؛ لدخول وقت الرمي، وقال الشافعي: إذا غربت الشمس من اليوم الثالث لا يحل لك النفر حتى ترمي الجمار الثلاث في اليوم الرابع، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأن النفر أبيح في اليوم؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ تَعَجَّلَ فِي يَوْمَيْنِ فَلَا إِثْمَ عليه لا في الليل، وجه الظاهر: أنه نفر في وقت لا يجب فيه الرمي ولا يجوز، فجاز له النفر كالنهار. الثالث اليوم: وهو أيام الرمي. صح: أي عند الإمام، وعندهما: لا من اعتباراً بسائر الأيام، وإنما يصح له فيه في النفر، فإذا لم يترخص بالنفر التحق بسائر الأيام، ومذهبه مروي عن ابن عباس؛ ولأنه لما ظهر أثر التخفيف فيه في حق ترك الرمي فلأن يظهر جوازه في الأوقات كلها أولى بخلاف اليوم الأول والثاني من أيام التشريق؛ حيث لا يجوز فيهما إلا بعد الزوال؛ لأنه يجوز تركه فيهما فكذا لا يجوز تقديمه، ولا كلام في أفضلية الرمي بعد الزوال. رمي: كرمي الجمرتين الأولى والوسطى في الأيام الثلاث. فارم ماشياً: حال كونك ماشيا ندبا، فلو رميتها راكبا جاز؛ لأن ما ورد من أنه عليه رمى جمرة العقبة راكباً، يدل على ذلك، وعن ابن عمر أنه كان يرمي جمرة العقبة يوم النحر راكباً، وسائر ذلك ماشياً، ويخبرهم أنه عليه كان يفعل ذلك، وقال بعضهم: الأفضل الرمي ماشياً في زماننا؛ لأنه أقرب إلى التضرع والتواضع، وذكر إبراهيم بن الجراح وهو من أكبر تلامذة عطاء بن أبي رباح تلميذ ابن عباس، وكان عالماً بالمناسك، قال: دخلت على أبي يوسف وقد أغمي عليه، فأفاق، فلما رآني قال: يا إبراهيم ما تقول في رمي الجمار يرميها الحاج راكباً أو ماشياً؟ فقلت: يرميها ماشياً، فقال: أخطأت فقلت: يرميها راكباً، فقال: أخطأت قلت فما يقول الإمام: قال: كل رمي ماشياً، وكل رمي ليس بعده رمي يرميها راكباً، فخرجت من عنده، فسمعت بكاء الناس في داره، فقيل لي: قضي أبو يوسف عليه، فتعجبت من حرصه على العلم في هذه الحالة. وإلا: أي وإن لم يكن بعده رمي كجمرة العقبة يوم النحر والجمرة الأخيرة في الأيام الثلاث. راكباً: أي ارم حال كونك راكباً. يدل عليه ما روي أنه عليه رمى جمرة العقبة راكباً يوم النحر، وهذا بيان الأفضلية، وأما الجواز فثابت كيف ما كان. وقال في النهر: إن الرمي راكباً أفضل مطلقاً عند الإمام ومحمد؛ لأن الثابت عنه عليه إنما هو الرمي راكباً فحينئذ الرمي ماشياً خلاف السنة، قلنا: إنما فعله ليكون أظهر للناس حتى يقتدوا به فيما يشاهدونه منه عليه.
Then after that likewise if you stay, and even if you stone on the fourth day before noon, it is valid. And every stoning after that stone walking, otherwise riding, after sunrise. 'If you stay': because he is given choice in staying; due to His statement: 'Then whoever hastens in two days, there is no sin upon him, and whoever delays, there is no sin upon him, for those who fear God' (al-Baqarah 2:203). It indicates his choice between staying and not staying, and staying is better following his action, peace be upon him, due to His statement: 'Then whoever hastens in two days' (al-Baqarah 2:203). And you may depart as long as dawn of the fourth day has not risen; when dawn rises, it is not permissible for you to depart because the time for stoning has entered. Al-Shafi'i said: When the sun sets on the third day, you may not depart until you stone the three jamarat on the fourth day; and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa because the departure was permitted in the day, due to His statement: 'Then whoever hastens in two days, there is no sin upon him' not at night. The apparent aspect: that he departed at a time when stoning is not obligatory nor permissible, so departure is permissible for him like the daytime. 'The third day': that is the days of stoning. 'Valid': that is according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] it is not, because they consider other days. And it is valid for him in the departure; if he does not take the concession of departure, it joins the other days. His position is narrated from Ibn Abbas; and because when the effect of leniency appeared in it regarding leaving stoning, it is more likely that its permissibility appears in all times, unlike the first and second days of Tashriq where it is not permissible except after noon, because it is permissible to leave stoning in them, so likewise it is not permissible to advance it. There is no dispute about the preference of stoning after noon. 'Stoning': like stoning the first and middle jamarat on the three days. 'Stone walking': while you are walking, as a recommendation; if you stone riding, it is permissible. Because what is reported that he, peace be upon him, stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba riding indicates that. And from Ibn Umar that he used to stone Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice riding, and the rest walking, and inform them that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to do that. Some said: Stoning walking in our time is better because it is closer to humility and submissiveness. Ibrahim ibn al-Jarrah, one of the major students of Ata ibn Abi Rabah, student of Ibn Abbas, a scholar of the rituals, said: I visited Abu Yusuf while he was unconscious; he revived; when he saw me he said: O Ibrahim, what do you say about stoning the jamarat: should the pilgrim stone riding or walking? I said: Stone walking. He said: You are wrong. I said: Stone riding. He said: You are wrong. I said: What does the Imam say? He said: Every stoning after which there is stoning, stone walking; every stoning after which there is no stoning, stone riding. I left him and heard people crying in his house; I was told: Abu Yusuf passed away. I marveled at his zeal for knowledge in that state. 'Otherwise': meaning if there is no stoning after it, like Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice and the last jamra on the three days. 'Riding': meaning stone riding. This is supported by the report that he, peace be upon him, stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba riding on the Day of Sacrifice. This states preference; as for permissibility, it is established in any manner. And it is said in al-Nahr: That stoning riding is absolutely better according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because what is established from him, peace be upon him, is stoning riding; then stoning walking would be against the sunnah. We say: He only did it to be more visible to people so that they would follow him in what they witnessed from him.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on two related issues in Hajj: the timing of stoning on the fourth day of Tashriq, and the recommended manner of stoning (walking vs riding). The ruling begins by stating that if a pilgrim stays in Mina beyond the two days (i.e., chooses not to hasten), then even if they stone the jamarat on the fourth day before noon (zawaal), their stoning is valid. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree: they hold that stoning on the fourth day before noon is not valid because they analogize it to the other days where stoning is only valid after noon. Abu Hanifa’s view is preferred because the departure (nafar) is permitted on the fourth day, and leniency is shown. The text then notes that the best time for stoning remains after noon for all days of Tashriq. The second part discusses the manner of stoning. The phrase 'stone walking, otherwise riding' is explained: for every stoning that will be followed by another stoning (the first and middle jamarat on the three days), it is recommended to stone on foot; for the stoning that is not followed by another (Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice and the last jamara on the third day), it is recommended to stone riding. This follows the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ). The narration from Abu Yusuf on his deathbed emphasizes this distinction. The commentary also mentions that some later scholars recommend walking in our time due to humility, but the preferred ruling as per the madhhab is as stated: walking for the first two, riding for the final.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): Stoning of the jamarat during Hajj on the days of Tashriq.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-ʿaqaba): The large pillar nearest to Makkah, stoned on the Day of Sacrifice and following days.
ماشياً (māshiyan): Walking on foot; recommended manner for stoning except for the final stoning.
راكباً (rākiban): Riding an animal; recommended for Jamrat al-Aqaba and final jamra.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is stoning valid on the fourth day of Tashriq?
A) Only after noon
B) Before noon if the pilgrim stays in Mina
C) Only after sunset
D) Stoning on the fourth day is not required

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, stoning on the fourth day before noon is valid if the pilgrim stays, and the sunnah manner is to walk for all except the final jamara which is ridden.

Rulings on Sending Luggage and Leaving Mina Overnight
Ruling on sending luggage ahead and staying overnight in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending heavy luggage ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina and on leaving overnight in Mina, and explain the evidence and reasoning.

Core Idea
Sending luggage ahead is prohibitively disliked; leaving Mina overnight incurs no compensation but is disliked.

This passage addresses two related issues in Hajj: the ruling on sending your heavy belongings ahead to Makkah while you remain in Mina for stoning, and the ruling on not spending the nights in Mina. The author explains why these actions are disliked and contrasts the Hanafi view with that of al-Shafi'i on the compensation for leaving Mina nights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling and its type
Locate the statement 'وكره أن تقدّم ثقلك إلى مكة...' – the act is sending luggage ahead and going to Muhassab. The ruling is karaha (dislike). Determine whether it is tahrimi or tanzihi from the text.
The text says 'تحريماً إن لم تأمن' indicating it is prohibitively disliked when not secure.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is that it distracts the heart from worship. The text also cites Umar's practice of disciplining for this action, confirming it is tahrimi.
If one is secure from distraction, it is not disliked.
3
Examine the baytuta ruling
Find 'وكره أيضاً أن لا تبيت بمنى ليالي الرمي' – this is another disliked act. Note that no compensation is required even if done intentionally.
Contrast with Shafi'i who requires dam for three missed nights.
4
Analyze the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi evidence for baytuta is that staying overnight is not intrinsically obligatory; it is only a preparation for the next day's rituals. Thus leaving it does not require compensation.
This is based on the principle that means are not ends.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi – no compensation; Shafi'i – dam for three nights. The student should recognize the difference in legal consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره أن تقدّم ثقلك إلى مكة وتقيم بمنى للرمي، ثم إلى المحصب. تحريماً إن لم تأمن لا إن أمنت. وكره إلخ: لأن عمر كان يفعل ذلك ويؤدب عليه؛ ولأنه يوجب شغل قلبه وهو في العبادة فيكره. والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية؛ إذ لا يؤدب على المكروه تنزيهاً، وكره أيضاً أن لا تبيت بمنى ليالي الرمي، ولو بت في غيره عمداً لا يجب عليك شيء، والذهاب إلى عرفات وترك الأمتعة بمكة مكروه بالأولى؛ لأن شغل القلب ثمه أشد، وقال الشافعي: لو ترك البيتوتة بمنى في ثلاث ليال يجب دم، ولو ترك ليلتين وجب عليه مدان وبليلة مد، ولنا أن البيتوتة ليست مقصودة بنفسها بل لما يقع في الغد من النسك، فإذا تركها لم يلزمه شيء كالبيتوتة بمنى ليلة العيد. ثقلك بفتحتين، وهو ما معك من المتاع والحوائج. ثم: أي بعد رمي الجمار رح من منى إلى المحصب وهو الأبطح ويسمى الحصباء والبطحاء أو الخيف، قف استنانا ولو ساعة ثم ادخل مكة. بضم الميم وشدة الصاد على وزن اسم المفعول من التفعيل، موضع بقرب مكة يقال له الأبطح وهي أرض ذات حصى، سمي بالمحصب؛ لأنه في مهبط، ويحمل السيل إليه الحصباء فتجتمع فيه والنزول فيه سنة عندنا، وأصل مشروعيته أن الكفار تحالفوا، أي بنوكنانة حالفوا قريشاً على بني هاشم أن لا يناكحوهم ولا يبايعوهم، ولا يودوهم حتى يسلموا إليهم محمداً أو يخرجوه مع بني هاشم وبني المطلب من مكة إلى الشعب، وكتبوا بينهم الصحيفة، وكتبوا فيه أنواعاً من الباطل والكفر، فأرسل الله عليها الأرضة، فأكلت ما فيها من الكفر والباطل، وتركت ما فيها من ذكر الله، فأخبر جبريل النبي عليها بذلك، فأخبر به النبي عليا عمه أبا طالب، فجاء إليهم أبو طالب، فأخبرهم عن النبي عليه بذلك، فوجدوه كما أخبر، وقال ابن عمر لما النزول به سنة حتى لو تركه مسيئاً. يصير وقال الشافعي: ليس بسنة؛ لما روي عن عائشة أنها قالت: نزول الأبطح ليس بسنة، وإنما نزله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لأنه كان أسمح لخروجه إلى المدينة، وكذا روي عن ابن عباس، ولنا أنه عليه قال: "نحن نازلون غداً بخيف كنانة حيث تقاسمت قريش على كفرهم"، متفق عليه، فعلم أن نزوله كان قصداً، وأيضاً قال ابن عمر: بني النزول به سنة، فقيل له: إن رجلاً يقول: إنه ليس بسنة، فقال: "كذب، أناخ به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبو بكر وعمر وعثمان" متفق عليه، فأي سنة أقوى من هذا، فإن فعله عليه قصداً، وفعل الخلفاء من بعده، وقول عائشة وابن عباس ظن منهم، فلا يعارض المرفوع، والمثبت مقدم على النافي.
And it is disliked that you send your heavy luggage to Makkah and stay in Mina for stoning, then to al-Muhassab. Prohibitively disliked if you are not secure, not if you are secure. 'And it is disliked etc.': because Umar used to do that and discipline for it; and because it distracts the heart while in worship, so it is disliked. The apparent is that the karaha is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked); since one is not disciplined for a tanzihi (lightly disliked) matter. Also, it is disliked to not spend the nights in Mina during the nights of stoning. If one spent the night elsewhere intentionally, nothing is obligatory upon you. Going to Arafat and leaving luggage in Makkah is disliked a fortiori, because the heart is more occupied there. Al-Shafi'i said: If one leaves staying overnight in Mina for three nights, a dam (sacrifice) is obligatory; for two nights, two mudd; for one night, one mudd. Our evidence: staying overnight is not intended for itself but for what occurs the next day of rituals; if one leaves it, nothing is obligatory, like staying overnight in Mina on the night of Eid. 'Thaqal' (luggage) with two fat'has: what is with you of goods and needs. 'Then': i.e., after stoning the jamarat, move from Mina to al-Muhassab, which is al-Abtah, also called al-Hasba, al-Batha, or al-Khayf; stop as sunna even for an hour, then enter Makkah. 'Muhassab' with damm on meem and shaddah on sad on the pattern of ism al-maf'ul from taf'il: a place near Makkah called al-Abtah, a land with pebbles. It is named Muhassab because it is a depression, and the torrent carries pebbles to it, so they gather there. Staying there is sunna according to us. The origin of its legislation is that the disbelievers made an alliance, i.e., Banu Kinana allied with Quraysh against Banu Hashim not to intermarry with them, nor buy from them, nor give them any charity until they handed over Muhammad or expelled him with Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib from Makkah to the valley. They wrote a document among themselves and wrote all kinds of falsehood and disbelief in it. Allah sent termite on it, which ate the falsehood and disbelief and left the mentions of Allah. Jibril informed the Prophet of that; the Prophet informed his uncle Abu Talib; Abu Talib came to them and informed them of the Prophet's news, and they found it as he said. Ibn Umar said: Staying there is sunna, to the extent that one who leaves it becomes sinful. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not sunna; based on the narration from Aisha that she said: 'Staying at al-Abtah is not sunna; the Messenger of Allah only stayed there because it was easier for his departure to Madinah.' Similarly narrated from Ibn Abbas. Our evidence: The Prophet said: 'We will stay tomorrow at Khayf of Kinana where Quraysh took an oath of disbelief.' Agreed upon. So it is known that his stay was intentional. Also, Ibn Umar said: 'Staying there is sunna.' It was said to him: 'A man says it is not sunna.' He replied: 'He lied; the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman camped there.' Agreed upon. So which sunna is stronger than this? The Prophet did it intentionally, and the caliphs after him. The statements of Aisha and Ibn Abbas are based on opinion, so they do not contradict the marfu' report. The one who affirms is given precedence over the one who negates.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage addresses two separate issues: (1) sending heavy luggage ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina, and (2) staying at al-Muhassab after Mina. The ruling states it is disliked (karaha) to send your luggage to Makkah and then go to al-Muhassab. The commentary clarifies that this karaha is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because 'Umar used to discipline for it. The reason is that it distracts the heart while one is in worship. Then it discusses the ruling of spending the nights in Mina during the days of stoning: it is disliked to leave it, but if done, no compensation is required. This is in contrast to al-Shafi'i who requires dam for missing three nights. The Hanafi argument is that staying overnight in Mina is not an end in itself but a preparation for the next day's rituals. The passage then turns to al-Muhassab (also called al-Abtah or Batha). Staying there after moving from Mina is sunnah according to the Hanafi school. The text provides a historical background: the stay commemorates the Prophet's stay there after the treaty of Hudaybiyyah and the lifting of the Quraysh boycott against Banu Hashim. The disagreement with al-Shafi'i is addressed: al-Shafi'i denies it is sunnah based on Aisha's statement. The Hanafi school counters with the hadith from the Prophet and the practice of the caliphs, giving precedence to the positive evidence. The commentary emphasizes that the Prophet's action was intentional, thus establishing it as sunnah.

Key Terms
ثقلك (thaqaluka): Heavy luggage and belongings; sending it ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina is disliked.
البيتوتة بمنى (al-baytūta bi-minā): Staying overnight in Mina during the nights of stoning (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is makruh tahrimi
C) It is makruh tanzihi
D) It is haram

Sending luggage ahead during Hajj is makruh tahrimi when it distracts, and leaving Mina nights requires no compensation in Hanafi fiqh.

Staying at al-Muhassab: A Hanafi Sunnah
Ruling on staying at al-Muhassab after Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on staying at al-Muhassab, and evaluate the evidence supporting the Hanafi sunnah.

Core Idea
Staying at al-Muhassab is a confirmed sunnah according to the Hanafi school, based on prophetic action and practice of the caliphs.

This passage explains the ruling on staying at al-Muhassab (al-Abtah) after completing the stoning at Mina. The Hanafi school considers it a sunnah, while al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing Aisha's statement. The author presents the Hanafi evidence from hadith and the practice of the caliphs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Find the statement 'والنزول فيه سنة عندنا' – staying at al-Muhassab is sunnah according to us (Hanafi). Note that it is considered a sunnah muakkadah.
The text also says 'حتى لو تركه مسيئاً' – leaving it is sinful, indicating its emphasis.
2
Understand the Shafi'i position
Locate 'وقال الشافعي: ليس بسنة' – al-Shafi'i says it is not sunnah. He bases this on Aisha's statement that the Prophet only stayed for convenience.
Also Ibn Abbas reported similarly.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi evidence includes the hadith 'نحن نازلون غداً بخيف كنانة' and the practice of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman as reported by Ibn Umar.
The hadith is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi argue that the Prophet's action was intentional ('نزوله كان قصداً'), and the caliphs followed. Aisha's opinion is considered a personal interpretation that does not contradict the definite action.
The principle: المثبت مقدم على النافي – the one who affirms is given precedence over the one who negates.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi pilgrims should make an effort to stay at Muhassab (even for an hour) to follow the sunnah; Shafi'i pilgrims may do so but it is not emphasized as sunnah.

Definition and Ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr
Definition of Tawaf al-Sadr and beginning of its time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Tawaf al-Sadr, state its linguistic meaning, identify its alternative name, and explain its wajib status in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is the wajib circumambulation of return, signifying farewell to the Kaaba.

The term 'Tawaf al-Sadr' may be unfamiliar, but it is a key wajib act of Hajj. In this lesson, we unpack its definition, linguistic root, and legal status. Understanding this clarifies why missing it requires a dam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic root
Note that 'sadr' literally means 'return' in Arabic. The tawaf is named after this meaning because it is performed when the pilgrim returns from the Hajj rituals.
The root ص-د-ر conveys the idea of returning or going back.
2
Understand the alternative name
Tawaf al-Sadr is also called 'al-ahd bi al-bayt' (covenant with the House), emphasizing that it is the final farewell circumambulation before leaving Makkah.
This name highlights the emotional and religious significance of taking leave of the Kaaba.
3
Distinguish between the two interpretations of 'return'
According to the majority (including Abu Hanifa), 'return' refers to returning from the actions of Hajj back to Mina or to Makkah. According to Abu Yusuf and Ibn Ziyad, it means returning to one's homeland.
This difference does not affect the ruling; both agree that the tawaf is wajib.
4
Note the legal ruling and consequence
In the Hanafi school, Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for pilgrims not residing in Makkah. If omitted, a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory.
Zahir al-Riwayah confirms this. Other schools consider it sunnah.
5
Recognize the timing
The earliest time for Tawaf al-Sadr is after completing the actions of Hajj (i.e., after staying at Mina and performing the stoning). The passage begins to state this timing.
The full timing will be covered in subsequent lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طواف الصدر] فطف للصدر [ أي لاجله وهو الرجوع لغة فلذلك سمي طواف الصدر، ويسمى العهد بالبيت (ع) أي الرجوع عن أفعال الحج، وعن أبي يوسف وابن زياد أنه الرجوع إلى الوطن، وأول وقته =
Tawaf al-Sadr: So perform tawaf for al-sadr i.e., for it; and it is 'return' linguistically, therefore it is called Tawaf al-Sadr. It is also called 'al-ahd bi al-bayt' (the covenant with the House). It means the return from the actions of Hajj. From Abu Yusuf and Ibn Ziyad: it is the return to the homeland. And the earliest time is =
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage defines Tawaf al-Sadr, also known as Tawaf al-Wada' (Farewell Tawaf) or Tawif al-Ifada (depending on context). The term 'sadr' literally means 'return', so Tawaf al-Sadr is the circumambulation performed when leaving Mina and returning. It signifies the completion of the Hajj rituals. There is a nuance: according to Abu Yusuf and Ibn Ziyad, 'return' refers to returning to one's homeland. The passage begins to state the earliest time for this tawaf, but the text is cut off. In the Hanafi school, Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for those not residing in Makkah, and if omitted, a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (ṭawāf al-ṣadr): The circumambulation performed when leaving Mina and returning from Hajj, also called Farewell Tawaf.
العهد بالبيت (al-ʿahd bi al-bayt): Another name for Tawaf al-Sadr; covenant with the House meaning a final farewell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr is the wajib circumambulation of return performed after completing Hajj rituals, marking the farewell to the Kaaba.

Tawaf al-Sadr: Its Wajib Status and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Explains the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Sadr, identify the exceptions, and explain the evidence for its wajib status vis-à-vis the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for all but Makkans; the Prophet's command binds, and exceptions confirm the rule.

Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell circumambulation) marks the final act before leaving Makkah. The Hanafi school deems it wajib for most pilgrims, while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. This lesson examines the evidence, the exceptions, and the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for all except people of Makkah and those within the miqat.
The ruling is specifically for non-Makkan pilgrims completing Hajj or Umrah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: the command of Ali ibn Abi Talib reported by Ibn Abbas, 'Let none depart until his last act is the circumambulation of the House.'
The hadith is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'لا ينفر أحد' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. Because the hadith is ahad (zanni thubut), the ruling is wajib, not fard.
This distinction between fard and wajib is foundational in Hanafi thought.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i argues it is not wajib because it is dropped for Makkans and menstruating women.
The Hanafi response explains that Makkans do not 'depart' and women are exempted by explicit text.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is adopted as mufta bihi because it is supported by the hadith and the practice of the caliphs.
The practical consequence: a Hanafi must return or offer compensation if omitted.

(فتح) ثم اشرب واختلفوا في أنه هل يبدأ بالملتزم أو بزمزم؟ والأصح الابتداء بزمزم، وكيفية الشرب: أن يستقي بنفسه ويشرب مستقبل القبلة، ويتضلع ويتنفس مرات ويرفع بصره في كل مرة، وينظر إلى البيت، ويمسح به رأسه ووجهه، وقال عليها: "إنها مباركة إنها طعام طعم وشفاء سقم، رواه مسلم، والمصنف لم يذكر الاستسقاء بنفسه ولا تقبيل العتبة ولا رجوع القهقرى؛ لما قيل: إنه لم يثبت شيء من ذلك من فعله عليها، وأما الالتزام والتشبث فجاء فيهما حديثان ضعيفان. والزمزم عمقها تسع وستون ذراعا، وعرض رأسها أربعة أذرع بالذراع التي هي أربع وعشرون إصبعا، سميت بها لكثرة ،ماءها ثم التوضؤ والاغتسال بماء زمزم لا يكره، وبه قال الشافعي ومالك، وكرهه أحمد. زمزم أي مائه مستقبلاً قائماً متضلعا منه متنفسا فيه مرات صابا منه على جسدك إن تيسر. (ط،ع) والتزم الملتزم: [هو ما بين الباب والحجر الأسود، والالتزام أن يلزق وجهه وصدره به باكيا. (ط،ع)] أي ساعة باكياً، وقيل: العتبة أيضاً؛ لأنها مستحبة، وقوله: وتشبث بالأستار" أي ساعة إن كانت قريبة بحيث تنالها، وإلا ضع يديك على رأسك مبسوطتين على الجدار ،قائمتين، وإلى هنا تم أفعال الحج.
Tawaf al-Sadr: Seven circuits, and it is wajib except for the people of Makkah. Then drink from Zamzam and cling to the Multazam. ... It is wajib due to the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'The people used to depart in every direction, so Ali said: 'Let none depart until his last act is the circumambulation of the House, except that it is eased for a menstruating woman.' It is agreed upon. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not wajib because if it were wajib it would not be dropped for the Makkan and the menstruating woman. We say: The people of Makkah do not depart, so it is not obligatory upon them because farewell is for those departing. The menstruating woman is exempted by text, and the postpartum woman is in her position by implication. His saying: 'except for the people of Makkah' means it is not obligatory upon them but recommended. Included with them are those who live inside the miqat because they are like them, and one who has taken Makkah as home then decides to leave, and one who performs Umrah from distant lands because these have no arrival circumambulation. He prays two rak'ahs after this circumambulation, and does not run or walk quickly due to repetition not being prescribed. Then drink: They disagreed whether to start with the Multazam or Zamzam. The correct is to start with Zamzam. Method: draw water yourself, drink facing the qibla, fill yourself, breathe several times, raise your eyes each time, look at the House, and wipe your head and face with it. The Prophet said: 'It is blessed, it is food for hunger and cure for illness.' Narrated by Muslim. The author did not mention drawing water yourself, kissing the threshold, or stepping back because it is said nothing of that is established from his action. For clinging and hanging onto the curtain, there are two weak hadiths. The depth of Zamzam is sixty-nine cubits, width of its opening four cubits by the cubit of twenty-four fingers. It was named for the abundance of its water. Performing wudu and bathing with Zamzam water is not disliked, according to al-Shafi'i and Malik, while Ahmad disliked it. 'Zamzam' meaning its water, facing qibla, standing, filling yourself, breathing in it multiple times, pouring some on your body if easy. And cling to the Multazam: it is between the door and the Black Stone. Clinging means pressing your face and chest to it while weeping. For an hour, weeping. It is said the threshold too because it is recommended. And his saying: 'and hang onto the curtains' for an hour if they are close enough to reach; otherwise place your hands on your head, palms open on the wall, standing. Up to here are the actions of Hajj.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq explaining the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr, also known as Tawaf al-Wada' (farewell circumambulation). It begins by stating that it consists of seven circuits and is wajib for all except the people of Makkah and those with similar status. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Ali commanding that one's last act be the circumambulation, and the exception for a menstruating woman is by text. Al-Shafi'i argued it is not wajib because it is dropped for Makkans and menstruating women. The Hanafi response clarifies that Makkans do not 'depart' (sadr) so farewell is not applicable, and menstruating women are explicitly exempted; postpartum women are analogized to them as a concession. The ruling for non-Makkans is thus wajib. Timing: after the tawaf al-ziyarah when one intends to travel; there is no final time; it is recommended when leaving. If one leaves without performing it, he must return as long as he has not passed the miqat. Details: after the tawaf, one prays two rak'ahs but does not do sa'y nor raml because these are not repeated. Then one drinks Zamzam water following the Prophet's practice: face qibla, drink until full, breathe, wipe head and face. Then one clings to the Multazam (area between door and Black Stone) in supplication. The author also notes that actions like drawing water oneself, kissing the threshold, etc. are not mentioned because not established from the Prophet. The commentary also includes a discussion on the ruling of staying at Muhassab (between Mina and Makkah) where the Hanafi position is that it is sunnah, and Al-Shafi'i considers it not sunnah based on Aisha's statement; Hanafis respond with the hadith of the Prophet intending to stay at Khif Bani Kinanah and the practice of the caliphs.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell circumambulation performed before leaving Makkah after Hajj.
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the door of the Kaaba and the Black Stone where one clings in supplication.
زمزم (zamzam): The sacred well in Makkah; its water is blessed and used for drinking and wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, for whom is Tawaf al-Sadr not wajib?
A) All pilgrims performing Hajj
B) People of Makkah and those inside the miqat
C) Menstruating women only
D) None; it is wajib for everyone

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell circumambulation) is wajib for all pilgrims to Makkah except its residents; omitting it requires return or sacrifice.

Implicit Authorization for Ihram on Behalf of an Unconscious Person
Intra-Hanafi dispute on implicit authorization for ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a companion performing ihram for an unconscious person, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the role of implicit authorization (istinabah dhalalah).

Core Idea
Companionship in Hajj implies authorization: the companion’s ihram suffices for the unconscious.

When a traveler for Hajj loses consciousness before entering ihram, can his companion perform ihram on his behalf? The Hanafi school debates this based on the extent of companionship (rafiqah). Abu Hanifa holds that the contract of companionship implies mutual authorization for all essential acts of the journey, including ihram. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict companionship to logistical travel matters and require explicit permission. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the disputed ruling
State the scenario: a man sets out for Hajj, becomes unconscious before ihram, and his companion performs ihram for him. Identify the core disagreement – is this ihram valid for the unconscious person?
The base text states a single ruling but the commentary reveals ikhtilaf.
2
Extract Abu Hanifa’s position and proof
Abu Hanifa validates the companion’s ihram. Understand his reasoning: companionship (rafiqah) is a contract of mutual assistance; since the journey’s main purpose is Hajj and ihram is its essential entry, the companion is implicitly authorized to perform acts necessary for the journey’s goal.
The text argues that istinabah is established dhalalah (by implication), making it like explicit text (nas).
3
Extract the Sahibayn’s position and proof
The two disciples invalidate the companion’s ihram. Their reasoning: companionship covers only travel logistics (e.g., protection, provisions), not ritual acts like ihram. They require explicit authorization, which was absent.
They argue that ihram is a condition that cannot be dropped except by the person’s own action or a deputy appointed by explicit text.
4
Identify the point of consensus
Note that if the unconscious person had given explicit prior instruction (e.g., 'If I become unconscious, perform ihram for me'), the companion’s act is valid by consensus. This clarifies that the dispute is only about implicit authorization.
The text explicitly states ijma’ when there is prior command.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi authorities (al-‘Ayni, al-Fath al-Qadir) prefer Abu Hanifa’s view. Explain why: companionship in a Hajj journey revolves around ihram, so the implication of delegation is strong.
The tarjih authority is clear: the view of Abu Hanifa is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو مغمى عليه ولو أهل عنه رفيقه بإغمائه صح. (ط) ولو أهل إلخ معنى الإهلال أن ينوي عنه ويبني، فيصير المغمى عليه محرماً بذلك؛ لانتقال إحرام الرفيق إليه بدليل 'له أن يحرم عن نفسه'، وليس معناه أن يجرده ويلبسه الإزار والحاصل أنه إذا أحرم عن نفسه أصالة، وعن الرفيق نيابة صح . هذا الإحرام عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يصح بناء على أن المرافقة هل تكون إذناً دلالة عند العجز عنه أو لا؟ قال الصاحبان لا ؛ إذ المرافقة إنما تراد لأمور السفر لا غير، فلا تتعدى إلى الإحرام. وقال الإمام: نعم؛ لأن عقد الرفقة استعانة كل منهم فيما يعجز عنه في سفره، وليس المقصود بهذا السفر إلا الإحرام؛ إذ هو أهمها، وصورة المسألة: رجل خرج للحج فأغمي عليه قبل الإحرام وأحرم عنه رفيقه، صح عند أبي حنيفة، ولم يصح عندهما لهما أن الإحرام شرط فلا يسقط إلا بفعله أو فعل نائبه ولم يوجد، وله: أن الاستنابة ثابتة دلالة، فصار كالثابت نصاً كشرب ماء السقاية، أما لو أمر غيره بأن يحرم عنه إذا أغمي عليه أو نام فأحرم المأمور عنه فيصح إجماعاً حتى إذا أفاق أو انتبه وأتى بأفعال الحج صح. (عيني، فتح) صح: إهلاله عنه عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يجوز ولو أمره بأن يحرم عنه عند عجزه فأحرم عنه عند إغمائه جاز إجماعاً.
Or an unconscious person - if his companion performs ihram for him due to his unconsciousness, it is valid. (T) 'And if he performs ihram etc.' The meaning of ihlal is that he intends it on his behalf and proceeds, so the unconscious person becomes a muhrim by that; due to the transfer of the companion's ihram to him, based on the evidence 'he may perform ihram for himself', and it is not meant that he strips him and clothes him with the izār. The conclusion is that if he performs ihram for himself primarily and for his companion as a deputy, it is valid. This ihram is according to Abu Hanifa, but the two said it is not valid, based on whether companionship constitutes implicit authorization during incapacity or not. The two disciples said no, for companionship is only intended for travel matters, not extending to ihram. The Imam said yes, because the contract of companionship is mutual assistance in what each is incapable of in his journey, and the purpose of this journey is only ihram, as it is the most important. The illustration: a man set out for Hajj and became unconscious before ihram, and his companion performed ihram for him; it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to them; because ihram is a condition and cannot be dropped except by one's own action or that of his deputy, which did not occur. He (Imam) argues that deputation is established by implication, so it is like being textually established, like drinking water from the water station. As for if he ordered someone else to perform ihram for him if he becomes unconscious or sleeps, then the one ordered performs ihram for him, it is valid by consensus, such that when he wakes up or comes to and performs the acts of Hajj, it is valid. ('Ayni, Fath) 'It is valid: his ihlal on his behalf according to Abu Hanifa, but the two said it is not permissible. However, if he ordered him to perform ihram for him upon his inability and he performed ihram for him during his unconsciousness, it is valid by consensus.'
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a person who loses consciousness before entering ihram, and his companion performs the ihram on his behalf. The base text states the ruling, and the commentary expands with an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the companion's ihram is valid for the unconscious person because the contract of companionship (rafiqah) implies mutual assistance in all matters of the journey, especially since ihram is the main purpose of this journey. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding that companionship only covers travel logistics and not ritual acts like ihram; they require explicit authorization. The text then clarifies that if the unconscious person had given prior explicit instruction before losing consciousness, then there is consensus that the companion's ihram is valid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) among later Hanafi scholars is that of Abu Hanifa, as the implication of companionship is considered strong enough for deputation. The passage ends by reaffirming Abu Hanifa's position and the consensus if explicit authorization was given.

Key Terms
الإهلال (al-ihlal): In this context, ihlal means entering the state of ihram by intention and talbiyah, or having a companion perform it on one's behalf.
الرفيقة (al-rafiqah): Companionship or being a travel companion; the text debates whether this implies mutual agency for ritual acts.
الاستنابة (al-istinabah): Deputation or authorization to act on someone's behalf; the text argues it can be implied from the contract of companionship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person becomes unconscious before ihram and his companion performs ihram for him without prior instruction, what is the ruling?
A) Valid according to all three imams.
B) Valid according to Abu Hanifa but invalid according to the two disciples.
C) Invalid according to all.
D) Valid only if the companion announces his intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a companion’s ihram for an unconscious co-traveler based on the implied authorization from the contract of companionship, with Abu Hanifa’s view being the relied-upon position.

Rulings Specific to Women in Ihram
Enumerates differences between men and women in ihram with explanations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five specific ihram rulings for women and explain the rationale for each difference.

Core Idea
Women in ihram uncover their faces, shorten hair instead of shaving, avoid loud talbiyah, and forgo ramal and running – all to maintain modesty.

In ihram, men and women share most obligations, but the Sharī‘a prescribes certain exceptions for women to preserve modesty and protect their 'awrah. This passage from Kanz al-Daqā’iq lists the key differences, with commentary from Fatḥ Bāb al-‘Ināya. Understanding these rulings ensures that women perform hajj and ‘umra correctly without incurring unnecessary penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The base rule: women are like men in all ihram rulings except where explicitly stated otherwise. This establishes a framework for the exceptions.
The same principle applies in other areas of fiqh.
2
List the five explicit differences
From the text: (1) she uncovers her face but not her head; (2) she does not raise her voice in talbiyah; (3) she does not perform ramal (quick walking) in tawaf; (4) she does not run between the two green pillars in sa‘y; (5) she does not shave her head but shortens her hair.
Each difference is rooted in modesty or 'awrah.
3
Examine the reasoning for each
The commentary explains: her face is not 'awrah in ihram (Hanafi view); her voice is 'awrah in attracting attention; quick movements are immodest; shaving would be undignified for women.
Sewn garments are permitted because covering her 'awrah takes priority.
4
Note the additional rulings
She may delay tawaf al-ziyāra due to menstruation/postpartum bleeding; she must not approach the Black Stone if crowding would lead to touching non-mahram men.
These are derived from the same principle of avoiding fitna.
5
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on taqsīr
There is a difference of opinion on whether the shortening must be a quarter of the hair length (analogy to man) or any amount suffices. The relied-upon position is that any shortening is sufficient, but a quarter is recommended.
This dispute does not affect the validity of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرأة كالرجل غير أنها تكشف وجهها، لا رأسها ولا تلبي جهرا ولا ترمل ولا تسعى بين الميلين ولا تحلق، وتقصر لأن صوتها عورة في الطواف ولا تضطبح أي لا تهرول لأنه مثلة في حقها ... غير أنها تكشف وجهها لو قال المصنف: غير' أن لا تكشف 'رأسها واقتصر عليه لكان أولى؛ لأن المرأة لا تخالف الرجل في كشف الوجه فكان ذكره تطويلاً بلا فائدة ويستحب أن تجعل على رأسها شيئاً وتجافيه، وقد جعلوا لذلك أعواداً كالقبة توضع على الوجه ويسدل فوقه. (فتح) : لا رأسها أي لا تكشف رأسها؛ لأنها عورة. (ط) الميلين: الأخضرين لأنه مخل بستر العورة. (ع) وتقصر : لقوله علي : ليس' على النساء الحلق، إنما على النساء 'التقصير'، وهل التقصير مقدر بالربع كالرجل أم لا؟ فيه خلاف، وقوله: 'تلبس المخيط' وما بدا لها من القميص والسراويل والخفين والقفازين غير مصبوغ بورس أو زعفران إلا أن يكون غسيلا؛ لأن هذا تزين، وهو من دواعي الجماع، وهي ممنوعة عن ذلك في الإحرام، ويزاد أنها تترك الصدر وتؤخر طواف الزيارة عن أيام النحر بعذر الحيض والنفاس، وكذا يزاد أنها لا تقرب الحجر في الزحام؛ لأنها ممنوعة من مماسة الرجال بل تستقبله من بعيد. (فتح)
And the woman is like the man except that she uncovers her face, not her head; she does not recite talbiyah loudly; she does not perform ramal; she does not hasten between the two green milestones; she does not shave but shortens (her hair). Because her voice is 'awrah during tawaf; she does not do idtiba' (i.e., she does not walk quickly) because it is an imitation of men in her case... Except that she uncovers her face: if the author had said 'except that she does not uncover her head' and limited it to that, it would have been better, because the woman does not differ from the man in uncovering the face, so mentioning it is lengthening without benefit. And it is recommended that she place something on her head and keep it loose; instruments like a dome have been made for that, placed over the face with a covering above. (Fath) 'Not her head' means she does not uncover her head because it is 'awrah. (T) 'The two green milestones' (meaning the two green markers) because it violates covering the 'awrah. (Ayn) 'And she shortens' based on 'Ali's saying: 'Shaving is not for women; only shortening is for women.' And whether the shortening is defined as a quarter like for a man or not, there is a difference. And his statement 'She wears sewn garments' and whatever appears to her of shirts, trousers, khuffs, and gloves that are not dyed with safflower or saffron unless they are washed, because this is adornment, which is a cause for sexual intercourse, and she is prohibited from that in Ihram. And it is added that she delays the 'umra (tawaf al-ziyarah) from the days of sacrifice due to the excuse of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and likewise it is added that she does not approach the Black Stone during crowding because she is prohibited from touching men, but rather faces it from a distance. (Fath)
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage lists the specific differences in ihram rulings for women compared to men, along with explanatory notes. The base text states: a woman in ihram is like a man except that she uncovers her face (not her head), does not recite talbiyah loudly, does not perform ramal (quick walking with shoulder movements) in tawaf, does not run between the two green pillars in sa'y, does not shave her head but instead shortens her hair, and she may wear sewn garments. The commentary explains each point: her face is not 'awrah in ihram (according to the Hanafi view) so she may leave it uncovered, but covering the head is obligatory because it is 'awrah; her voice is considered 'awrah (for attracting attention) so she should not raise it; ramal and running are considered immodest for women; shaving is replaced by shortening due to the hadith of 'Ali; and wearing sewn clothes is permitted because her 'awrah must be covered, and sewn garments help achieve that. Additional rulings are added: she may delay tawaf al-ziyarah due to menstruation, and she should not approach the Black Stone if there is crowding to avoid physical contact with men. All these rulings are specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الرمل (al-ramal): Quick walking with short steps and shoulder movements in the first three circuits of tawaf; women do not perform it.
السعي بين الميلين (al-sa'y bayna al-milayn): Hastening between the two green pillars in sa'y; women do not run this segment.
التقصير (al-taqsir): Shortening of hair after ihram; women shorten instead of shaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a specific ruling for women in ihram?
A) She must shave her head.
B) She may recite talbiyah loudly.
C) She may wear sewn garments.
D) She must perform ramal in tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Women in ihram differ from men in five main ways: uncovering face, quiet talbiyah, no ramal, no hastening in sa'y, and shortening hair instead of shaving.

Garlanding as a Means of Entering Ihram: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on garlanding and ihram with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that garlanding a sacrificial animal constitutes ihram under specific conditions, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection regarding talbiyah.

Core Idea
Garlanding + setting out + intention = ihram in Hanafi law; the tamattu' animal requires ihram upon setting out by istihsan.

In Hajj rituals, entering ihram is typically marked by talbiyah, but the Hanafi school recognizes an alternative: garlanding a sacrificial animal. This lesson unpacks the conditions under which taqlid triggers ihram, including a special ruling for the tamattu' animal. We will also examine the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi reliance on istihsan.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on ihram via garlanding
Identify the three requirements: garland the animal, set out intending Hajj, and have intention. The person becomes muhrim immediately upon fulfilling these.
Garlanding alone is insufficient; setting out and intention are also required.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its basis
The Shafi'i school holds that only talbiyah can initiate ihram, not garlanding. They reject the Hanafi view as it lacks a direct textual command.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have valid evidence.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil and their response
Hanafis rely on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: 'Whoever garlands his sacrificial animal has entered ihram.' They argue garlanding is equivalent to talbiyah in meaning, both signify acceptance of the call to Hajj.
The hadith is considered a sound proof in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the exception for tamattu' animal and istihsan
For the tamattu' animal, the Hanafi school departs from strict qiyas (which would require catching up to the animal) and uses istihsan: the animal is a ritual from the start, so setting out with intention suffices even before catching it.
This exception is conditioned on the action occurring in the months of Hajj.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
A Hanafi can become muhrim by garlanding without talbiyah, whereas a Shafi'i must recite talbiyah. This affects the start of prohibitions of ihram and the validity of subsequent acts.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi school is the position allowing garlanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتلبس المخيط، ومن قلد بدنة تطوع أو نذر أو جزاء صيد ونحوه وتوجّه معها يريد الحج فقد أحرم، فإن بعث بها، ثم توجّه لا، حتى يلحقها إلا في بدنة المتعة، فإنه يصير محرماً حين توجه إذا نوى الإحرام قبل أن يلحقها استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يصير محرماً حتى يدركها أو يسوقها؛ لأن عند عدم سوق الهدي وقت التوجه لم يوجد منه إلا مجرد النية، ووجه الاستحسان أن هذا الهدي مشروع من الابتداء نسكا من مناسك الحج وضعا؛ لأنه يختص بمكة ويجب شكراً للجمع بين أداء نسكين وغيره لا اختصاص له بمكة، وينبغي أن يكون هدي القران كذلك وإنما اقتصر على الأول لذكره في القرآن وههنا قيد آخر لابد من ذكره وهو أنه في بدنة المتعة إنما يصير محرماً بالتقليد والتوجه إذا حصلا في أشهر الحج، فإن حصلا في غير أشهر الحج لا يصير محرماً ما لم يدرك الهدي ويسر معه؛ لأن التمتع قبل أشهر الحج غير معتد به .. (فتح، مستخلص) بدنة المتعة: فإنه يصير محرما بالتوجه إن نوى الإحرام قبل أن يلحقها. (ط)
And she wears sewn garments. And whoever garlands a voluntary camel, or a vowed one, or compensation for hunting and the like, and sets out with it intending Hajj, has entered ihram. If he sends it ahead and then sets out, he does not (enter ihram) until he catches up to it, except in the case of a tamattu' camel, for then he becomes a muhrim at the time he sets out, if he intends ihram before catching up to it, by istihsan. The qiyas is that he does not become a muhrim until he catches up to it or drives it, because in the absence of driving the sacrificial animal at the time of setting out, nothing existed from him except mere intention. The face of istihsan is that this sacrificial animal is legislated from the beginning as a ritual of Hajj, as it is specific to Mecca and becomes obligatory as a thank offering for combining the performance of two rituals, while other animals have no such specificity to Mecca. And the same should apply to the sacrificial animal of qiran, except that he confined himself to the first due to its mention in the Quran. And here is another condition that must be mentioned: in the case of a tamattu' camel, he becomes a muhrim by garlanding and setting out only if these occur in the months of Hajj. If they occur outside the months of Hajj, he does not become a muhrim until he catches up to the animal and goes with it, because tamattu' before the months of Hajj is not considered valid. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'The tamattu' camel: he becomes a muhrim by setting out if he intends ihram before catching up to it.' (T)
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effect of garlanding (taqlid) a sacrificial animal as a way of entering ihram. The base text states that garlanding a voluntary or vowed animal, or a compensation animal, and then setting out with it intending Hajj, constitutes entering ihram. The commentary expands with an inter-madhhab dispute: the Shafi'i school holds that only talbiyah can initiate ihram, while the Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: 'Whoever garlands his sacrificial animal has entered ihram.' The passage then explains the case where one sends the animal ahead and follows later: he does not become muhrim until he catches up, except for the animal of tamattu' (a sacrificial animal offered due to combining 'umrah and Hajj). For tamattu', by istihsan (juristic preference), he enters ihram upon setting out with intention, even before catching the animal, because the tamattu' animal is a ritual from the start and requires expressing gratitude for the combined acts. The qiyas would require catching up. The passage further adds a condition: for tamattu', the garlanding and setting out must occur during the Hajj months; if they occur before, the person does not enter ihram until he catches the animal and proceeds with it. This shows the Hanafi departure from strict analogy in favor of a more practical ruling based on the nature of the ritual.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Hanging a piece of sandal or other marker on the neck of a sacrificial animal to indicate it is consecrated.
بدنة المتعة (badanat al-tamattu'): The sacrificial animal offered by one performing tamattu' Hajj, which is obligatory as a thank offering.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departure from qiyas in favor of a more appropriate ruling based on need or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a person become a muhrim by garlanding a sacrificial animal?
A) Only when he recites talbiyah.
B) When he garlands the animal, sets out intending Hajj, and for tamattu' also within the Hajj months.
C) Only when he reaches the miqat.
D) When he slaughters the animal.

Key Takeaway
Garlanding a sacrificial animal combined with setting out and intention constitutes ihram in the Hanafi school, with a special istihsan-based exception for the tamattu' animal allowing immediate ihram upon setting out.
