Ihram by Marking a Hady: Conditions and Dispute
Explains when taqlid of a hady causes ihram and the Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which taqlid of a hady initiates ihram, explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and identify the practical difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Marking a hady with intention and proceeding substitutes for talbiyah in initiating ihram.

This lesson explores the unique Hanafi ruling that entering ihram can be achieved without verbal talbiyah by simply marking a sacrificial animal and proceeding with it. The source text details the conditions for this rule and presents the counterargument from Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes actions over speech when supported by explicit hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act (taqlid of a hady) and the three conditions required for it to cause ihram: marking, proceeding with the animal, and intention of Hajj. Note that talbiyah is not required.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (in one view) holds that ihram is only achieved by talbiyah; marking alone cannot substitute.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is qiyas: talbiyah is the verbal declaration of entering ihram, so mere marking without speech should not suffice.
This is an a priori analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school cites the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'When a man marks his hady, he has entered ihram.' This explicit text overrides analogy. Additionally, driving the marked animal is equivalent to talbiyah in demonstrating response to Allah's call.
The hadith is considered stronger because it is direct and specific.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi: a person who marks and sends a hady but does not recite talbiyah is muhrim. Shafi'i: he remains non-muhrim until he recites talbiyah. This affects when he must observe ihram restrictions.
The practical consequence is the timing of entry into ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتلبس المخيط، ومن قلد بدنة تطوع أو نذر أو جزاء صيد ونحوه وتوجّه معها يريد الحج فقد أحرم، فإن بعث بها، ثم توجّه لا، حتى يلحقها إلا في بدنة المتعة، فقد أي هو أي لا يصير محرما : وتلبس المخيط: لأن في لبس غير المخيط كشف عورتها (ع) قلّد بدنة تطوع: [التقليد أن يعلق على عنق البدنة قطعة نعل أو عروة مزادة أو لحاء شجر مما يكون علامة على أنه هدي (ع) بيان لما يقوم مقام التلبية؛ لأن المقصود من التلبية إظهار الإجابة للدعوة وهو حاصل بتقليد الهدي، وإذا اشترك جماعة في بدنة فقلّدها أحدهم صاروا محرمين إن كان ذلك بأمر البقية وساروا معها، وقوله: أو جزاء صيد أي قتله في الحرم أو في إحرام سابق بأن قتل في الحرم أو محرم صيدا ووجبت قيمته فاشترى بها بدنة في سنة أخرى، فقلّدها وساقها إلى مكة، وقوله: "فقد أحرم" أي بإتيان القيود الثلاث التي ذكرت من قبل وهي التقليد ،والتوجه، وإرادة الحج، فأفاد أنه لو واحد منها لا يكون محرما، وقال الشافعي في قول: لا يصير محرما إلا بالتلبية وهو القياس، ولنا: قول ابن عمر ا: "إذا قلد الرجل هديه فقد أحرم ، وهو محمول على ما ساقه؛ لأن سوقه بعد التقليد في معنى التلبية. (عيني، فتح) فقد أحرم أي صار محرماً؛ لقوله عليها: "من قلد بدنة فقد أحرم". (مستخلص) بعث بها : أي بالبدنة بعد التقليد. (ط) حتى يلحقها الأنه إذا أدركها فقد اقترنت نيته بعمل هو من خصائص الحج فيصير محرما كما لو ساقها من الابتداء. (ع] لأنه إذا لم يكن بين يديه هدي يسوقه عند التوجه لم يوجد منه إلا مجرد النية، وبمجرد النية لا يصير محرماً، ولو وصل إلى الميقات ولم يلحقها لزمه الإحرام بالتلبية من الميقات، ولا أثر للحوق بعد ذلك، قال في "المبسوط": اختلف الصحابة في هذه المسألة على ثلاثة أقوال : منهم من يقول إذا قلدها صار محرما، ومنهم من يقول: إذا توجه في أثرها صار محرماً، ومنهم من يقول: إذا أدركها وساقها صار محرما، فأخذنا بالمتيقن من وقلنا: إذا أدركها وساقها صار محرما. وقوله: "إلا في بدنة "المتعة استثناء من قوله حتى يلحقها فإنه يصير محرما حين توجه إذا نوى الإحرام قبل أن يلحقها استحساناً، والقياس أن لا يصير محرما حتى يدركها أو يسوقها؛ لأن عند عدم سوق الهدي وقت التوجه لم يوجد منه إلا مجرد النية، ووجه الاستحسان أن هذا الهدي مشروع من الابتداء نسكا من مناسك الحج وضعا؛ لأنه يختص بمكة ويجب شكراً للجمع بين أداء نسكين وغيره لا اختصاص له بمكة، وينبغي أن يكون هدي القران كذلك وإنما اقتصر على الأول لذكره في القرآن وههنا قيد آخر لابد من ذكره وهو أنه في بدنة المتعة إنما يصير محرماً بالتقليد والتوجه إذا حصلا في أشهر الحج، فإن حصلا في غير أشهر الحج لا يصير محرماً ما لم يدرك الهدي ويسر معه؛ لأن التمتع قبل أشهر الحج غير معتد به .. (فتح، مستخلص) بدنة المتعة: فإنه يصير محرما بالتوجه إن نوى الإحرام قبل أن يلحقها. (ط) ذلك
And she wears sewn clothes, and whoever marks a voluntary or vowed badanah or a compensation for hunting and the like, and proceeds with it intending Hajj, has entered ihram. If he sends it ahead then proceeds, no, until he catches up with it, except in the case of the tamattu' badanah. So 'he has entered ihram' means he becomes muhrim. And she wears sewn clothes: because wearing unsewn clothes would expose her awrah. Marking a voluntary badanah: [Taqlid is to hang on the neck of the badanah a piece of sandal or a strap of a waterskin or tree bark, as a sign that it is a hady. Explanation of what substitutes for talbiyah; because the purpose of talbiyah is to show response to the call, and that is achieved by marking the hady. If a group shares a badanah and one of them marks it, they all become muhrim if that was by the command of the rest and they proceed with it. And His saying: 'or compensation for hunting' means killing it in the Haram or in a previous ihram, such that he killed in the Haram or while muhrim a game animal and its value became obligatory, so he bought a badanah with it in another year, marked it and drove it to Makkah. And His saying: 'has entered ihram' means by fulfilling the three conditions mentioned before: marking, proceeding, and intention of Hajj. It indicates that if any one is missing, he does not become muhrim. Al-Shafi'i said in one view: he does not become muhrim except by talbiyah, and that is the analogy. Our proof: the saying of Ibn Umar: 'When a man marks his hady, he has entered ihram.' And it is interpreted as concerning what he drives; because his driving after marking is in the meaning of talbiyah. (Ayni, Fath) 'He has entered ihram' means he becomes muhrim due to his saying: 'Whoever marks a badanah has entered ihram.' (Mustakhlas) 'He sends it ahead' means the badanah after marking. (T) 'Until he catches up with it' because if he overtakes it, his intention has been connected to an act that is specific to Hajj, so he becomes muhrim as if he had driven it from the start. (A) Because if there is no hady before him when he proceeds, nothing exists from him except mere intention, and by mere intention he does not become muhrim. If he reaches the miqat and has not caught up with it, he must enter ihram with talbiyah from the miqat, and catching up later has no effect. He said in al-Mabsut: The Companions differed on this issue in three opinions: some say when he marks it he becomes muhrim; some say when he proceeds after it he becomes muhrim; some say when he overtakes it and drives it he becomes muhrim. So we took the most certain and said: when he overtakes it and drives it he becomes muhrim. And His saying: 'except in the tamattu' badanah' is an exception from 'until he catches up with it'; he becomes muhrim when he proceeds if he intends ihram before catching up with it, by istihsan. The analogy is that he does not become muhrim until he overtakes it or drives it because at the time of proceeding there is no driving of the hady, only mere intention. The ground for istihsan is that this hady is legislated from the beginning as a rite of Hajj by placement; because it is specific to Makkah and is obligatory as thanks for combining two rites, while other hady is not specific to Makkah. And the hady of qiran should be similar, but he restricted to the first because of its mention in the Quran. Here there is another condition that must be mentioned: in the tamattu' badanah, he becomes muhrim by marking and proceeding only if they occur in the months of Hajj. If they occur outside the months of Hajj, he does not become muhrim until he overtakes the hady and drives with it, because tamattu' before the months of Hajj is not valid. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Tamattu' badanah: he becomes muhrim by proceeding if he intends ihram before catching up with it. (T) That.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of entering ihram through marking (taqlid) a sacrificial animal (hady). It begins with two matn statements: first, that a woman in ihram wears sewn clothes (to cover her awrah), and second, that a person who marks a badanah (camel or cow) for voluntary offering, vow, or compensation for hunting, and then proceeds towards Makkah with it intending Hajj, becomes muhrim. The commentary explains that taqlid substitutes for talbiyah because both indicate response to Allah's call. If a group is sharing a badanah and one marks it with their permission, all become muhrim. The conditions for ihram are three: marking (taqlid), proceeding (tawajjuh), and intention (niyyah). If one sends the animal ahead and later proceeds without catching it, he is not muhrim until he overtakes it and drives it, except in the case of tamattu' hady, where by istihsan he becomes muhrim upon proceeding with intention even before catching up. The text then presents the Shafi'i view that ihram requires talbiyah, and refutes it with the hadith of Ibn Umar and the explanation that driving the marked animal is equivalent to talbiyah. The commentary also cites a report from al-Mabsut that the Companions had three opinions, and the Hanafi school adopted the most cautious position: ihram occurs only when one catches up and drives the animal. For tamattu', istihsan is applied because the hady is a specific rite of Hajj from the beginning. Additionally, the tamattu' hady requires that marking and proceeding occur in the months of Hajj to cause ihram.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Hanging a piece of sandal, strap, or tree bark around the neck of a sacrificial animal as a sign that it is a hady.
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial animal, specifically a camel or cow, offered during Hajj.
متعة (tamattu'): Performing 'Umrah during the months of Hajj and then Hajj in the same year with a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement to become muhrim by taqlid of a hady?
A) Merely marking the animal
B) Marking the animal and reciting talbiyah
C) Marking the animal, proceeding with it, and intending Hajj
D) Catching up to the animal and driving it to Makkah

Key Takeaway
Ihram by taqlid requires three conditions: marking, proceeding, and intention; the Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar, and the Shafi'i objection based on qiyas is refuted by the explicit text.

Actions That Do Not Affect Ihram: Covering, Ish'ar, and Marking a Sheep
Ruling on actions that do not cause ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three actions that do not cause ihram (jall, ish'ar, and taqlid of a sheep) and explain why they are not considered rites of Hajj, including the Hanafi intra-madhhab difference on ish'ar.

Core Idea
Covering, ish'ar, and marking a sheep are not rites of Hajj; they do not create or break ihram.

This lesson examines a passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that clarifies which actions performed on a sacrificial animal do not affect one's ihram. Understanding this helps distinguish between recommended practices and those that have legal effect on the state of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions
From the text, list the three actions: jall (covering), ish'ar (slitting the hump), and taqlid of a sheep (marking).
These are mentioned in the first line of the matn.
2
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that none of these are specific to Hajj; even if recommended, they may be done for non-ritual reasons like protection from weather or treatment.
Ish'ar is particularly discussed: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh because it involves wounding, while Sahibayn consider it good but still not a rite.
3
Apply the ruling
The consequence is that performing these actions does not make one a muhrim; ihram is only established by intention and specific acts like talbiyah or proceeding to Mina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جلّلها أو أشعرها أو قلد شاةً لم يكن محرماً، والبدن من الإبل والبقر. أي وضع الجل على البدنة أو أشعرها: من الإشعار، وهو الطعن في سنام الهدي من جانبها الأيمن أي أدماها بجرح ليعلم أنها هدي. (ط،ع) لم يكن محرماً لأن شيئاً من ذلك ليس من خصائص الحج؛ إذ التجليل وإن ندب إليه إلا أنه قد يكون لدفع الأذى كالحر والبرد، والإشعار مكروه عند الإمام أي الإدماء بالجرح، فلا يكون من النسك، وعندهما: وإن كان حسنا إلا أنه قد يفعل للمعالجة، وتقليد الشاة ليس بسنة غير معتاد والتقليد أحب من التجليل لذكره في القرآن. (فتح، مستخلص) والبدن: بضم الباء جمع بدنة وهي عندنا من الإبل والبقر مطلقاً، سواء عجز من الإبل أو لا، وقال مالك: إن عجز من الإبل فمن البقر، وقال الشافعي: من الإبل خاصة بظاهر قوله عليه: "من راح يوم الأولى فكأنما قرب بدنة، ومن راح في الثانية فكأنما قرب بقرة فإنه يفيد التغاير بينهما، وأجيب بأن التخصيص باسم خاص لا يمنع الدخول تحت العام، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ كَانَ عَدُوّاً لِلَّهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَجِبْرِيلَ وَمِيكَالَ (البقرة:۹۸)، ولنا: حديث جابر "كنا ننحر البدنة عن سبعة، فقيل والبقرة؟ فقال: "وهل هي إلا وقال الخليل: إن البدنة ناقة أو بقرة تهدى إلى مكة، قال النووي وهو قول أكثر أهل اللغة. (عيني، فتح)
If he covers it (with a jill) or makes ish'ar on it (slitting the hump) or marks a sheep, he is not muhrim. And the budn (pl. of badanah) are from camels and cows. That is, placing the covering on the badanah or making ish'ar: from ish'ar, which is stabbing in the hump of the hady from its right side, i.e., making it bleed with a wound so that it is known as a hady. (T, A) He is not muhrim because none of that is specific to Hajj; for covering, although recommended, may be to repel harm like heat or cold, and ish'ar is disliked (makruh) according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) – i.e., causing bleeding with a wound – so it is not a rite. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), although it is good, it may be done for treatment. And marking a sheep is not a sunnah and is not customary. And taqlid is more beloved than covering because of its mention in the Quran. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And al-budn (with damma on the ba) is the plural of badanah, and in our view it is absolutely from camels and cows, whether one is unable to afford a camel or not. Malik said: if unable to afford a camel, then from cows. Al-Shafi'i said: from camels only, based on the apparent meaning of his saying: 'Whoever goes on the first day, it is as if he has offered a badanah, and whoever goes on the second day, it is as if he has offered a cow' – this indicates they are different. The response is that specifying with a specific name does not prevent inclusion under a general term, like the verse: 'And whoever is an enemy to Allah, His angels, His messengers, and Gabriel and Michael' (2:98). And our proof is the hadith of Jabir: 'We used to sacrifice a badanah for seven, and it was said, And a cow? He said: Is it not...?' And al-Khalil said: Al-badanah is a she-camel or a cow offered to Makkah. Al-Nawawi said this is the view of most linguists. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Hajj, addressing two issues: what actions do not cause ihram, and the definition of badanah. The matn states that covering (jall), making ish'ar (slitting the hump to let blood), or marking a sheep does not make one muhrim. The commentary explains that these actions are not exclusive to Hajj: covering may be for protection from weather, ish'ar is considered makruh by Abu Hanifa because it involves unnecessary wounding (though Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it good but still not a rite), and taqlid of a sheep is not a recognized sunnah. The matn then defines 'al-budn' (plural of badanah) as camels and cows. The commentary elaborates that in the Hanafi school, badanah includes both camels and cows unconditionally. It presents the positions of other schools: Malik says a cow may substitute only if one cannot afford a camel; Shafi'i says badanah is exclusively camels, citing a hadith that distinguishes between badanah and cow. The Hanafi response uses the principle that specific mention does not negate general inclusion, citing the Quranic example of mentioning Jibril and Mikail separately after 'angels'. Furthermore, the Hanafi position is supported by the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet answered 'Is it not (considered badanah)?' indicating that a cow is included. Lexical authorities like al-Khalil and al-Nawawi affirm that badanah refers to both a she-camel and a cow offered as a sacrifice to Makkah.

Key Terms
تجليل (tajlil): Covering the sacrificial animal with a cloth.
إشعار (ish'ar): Slitting the hump of the hadi to let blood as a mark.
تقليد (taqlid): Placing a garland or mark on the animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on making ish'ar (slitting the hump) of a hadi according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh
C) Wajib
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Covering, ish'ar, and marking a sheep do not cause ihram; they are not rites of Hajj.

Definition of Badanah: Camels and Cows Unconditionally – Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Definition of badanah and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of badanah (camels and cows unconditionally) and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i and Maliki, citing the proofs from hadith and linguistics.

Core Idea
Badanah includes both camels and cows unconditionally in the Hanafi school.

This lesson focuses on the definition of 'badanah' – the sacrificial animal offered during Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that it refers to both camels and cows, without condition. Other schools differ. We explore the proofs from hadith and linguistics, and the Hanafi response to the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi definition
From the text, note that 'al-budn min al-ibil wa al-baqar' meaning camels and cows, without restriction.
2
Understand the opposing views
Malik restricts cows to when camels are unavailable; Shafi'i says only camels.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
They cite a hadith that distinguishes between badanah and cow, implying they are separate.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school uses the principle that specific mention does not negate general inclusion, citing the Quranic verse and the hadith of Jabir.
5
Recognize the impact
The practical difference: a person offering a cow as hady is valid in Hanafi, not in Shafi'i.

Actions That Do Not Make One Muhrim
Ruling on tagging, branding, and collaring sacrificial animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that covering, marking, and collaring a sacrificial animal do not make one a muhrim, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on ish'ar (marking).

Core Idea
Covering, marking, and collaring sacrificial animals are not Hajj rites; they do not make one muhrim.

You might think that performing any action related to a sacrificial animal during Hajj would bring you into the state of ihram. But the Hanafi school clarifies that covering the animal, marking it by cutting its hump, or putting a collar around its neck are not specific to Hajj. They may be done for practical reasons like protection from weather or medical treatment. However, the school differs on whether the specific marking (ish'ar) is disliked or permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions
The text mentions three actions: covering (tajlil), marking by stabbing the hump (ish'ar), and putting a collar on a sheep (taqlid).
These are actions related to sacrificial animals, not to the pilgrim.
2
State the ruling
None of these actions make one a muhrim. The ruling is that the person remains in his ordinary state.
The text explicitly says: 'لَم يَكُن مُحرِمًا' (he is not a muhrim).
3
Understand the reason
These acts are not specific to Hajj; they may be done for other purposes such as protection from heat/cold (tajlil) or medical treatment (ish'ar).
This distinguishes them from actual Hajj rites like talbiyah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar (wounding) to be makruh (disliked), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it hasan (good). However, both agree it does not affect ihram.
The difference is about the praiseworthiness of the act, not its effect on ihram.
5
Apply the ruling
If someone covers or marks their sacrificial animal, their Hajj is still valid, and they are not required to do anything extra.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position: the acts do not break ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ط،ع) لم يكن محرماً لأن شيئاً من ذلك ليس من خصائص الحج؛ إذ التجليل وإن ندب إليه إلا أنه قد يكون لدفع الأذى كالحر والبرد، والإشعار مكروه عند الإمام أي الإدماء بالجرح، فلا يكون من النسك، وعندهما: وإن كان حسنا إلا أنه قد يفعل للمعالجة، وتقليد الشاة ليس بسنة غير معتاد والتقليد أحب من التجليل لذكره في القرآن. (فتح، مستخلص) والبدن: بضم الباء جمع بدنة وهي عندنا من الإبل والبقر مطلقاً، سواء عجز من الإبل أو لا، وقال مالك: إن عجز من الإبل فمن البقر، وقال الشافعي: من الإبل خاصة بظاهر قوله عليه: "من راح يوم الأولى فكأنما قرب بدنة، ومن راح في الثانية فكأنما قرب بقرة فإنه يفيد التغاير بينهما، وأجيب بأن التخصيص باسم خاص لا يمنع الدخول تحت العام، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ كَانَ عَدُوّاً لِلَّهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَجِبْرِيلَ وَمِيكَالَ﴾ (البقرة:۹۸)، ولنا: حديث جابر "كنا ننحر البدنة عن سبعة، فقيل والبقرة؟ فقال: "وهل هي إلا وقال الخليل: إن البدنة ناقة أو بقرة تهدى إلى مكة، قال النووي وهو قول أكثر أهل اللغة. (عيني، فتح)
If he covers it (the sacrificial animal) with a cloth, or marks it by cutting its hump, or ties a collar on a sheep, he is not a muhrim. And al-budn are from camels and cows. i.e., placing a covering on the budnah. And if he drives it, it is considered legally valid. Or marks it: from ish'ar, which is stabbing the hump of the sacrificial animal on its right side, i.e., wounding it to let know that it is a sacrificial animal. (T, A) He is not a muhrim because none of these are specific characteristics of Hajj; for covering, although recommended, may be to repel harm like heat or cold, and ish'ar is disliked according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) i.e., wounding by cutting, so it is not part of the ritual. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): although it is good, it may be done for medical treatment. And tying a collar on a sheep is not a sunnah, not customary, and tying a collar is more beloved than covering because it is mentioned in the Quran. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And al-budn: with damma on ba', plural of badanah, which according to us (Hanafis) applies to camels and cows absolutely, whether he is unable (to get a camel) or not. Malik said: if unable to get a camel, then from cows. Al-Shafi'i said: from camels only, based on the apparent meaning of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Whoever goes on the first day, it is as if he sacrificed a badanah, and whoever goes on the second day, it is as if he sacrificed a cow' for it indicates differentiation between them. The response is that specification with a specific name does not prevent inclusion under the general term, like His statement: 'And whoever is an enemy to Allah and His angels and His messengers and Gabriel and Michael' (2:98). And we have the hadith of Jabir: 'We used to sacrifice a badanah for seven people.' It was said: 'And a cow?' He said: 'Is it not...' Al-Khalil said: A badanah is a she-camel or a cow that is sent to Mecca. Al-Nawawi said it is the saying of most lexicographers. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage discusses actions that do not constitute entering into the state of ihram. The core ruling is that covering a sacrificial animal (tajlil), marking it (ish'ar), or putting a collar on a sheep (taqlid) does not make one a muhrim. The reason given is that none of these acts are specific to Hajj; they may be done for other purposes like protection from weather or medical treatment. Within the Hanafi school, there is an intra-madhhab difference: Imam Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar (wounding the hump) to be makruh (disliked), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it good (hasan) though it could be for medical treatment. The passage then defines 'badanah' (pl. budn) as a sacrificial animal. According to the Hanafis, it includes both camels and cows absolutely. The opposite views of Malik (cows only if unable to get camels) and al-Shafi'i (camels only) are presented and refuted using textual evidence: a hadith from Jabir shows that a badanah was shared by seven people, and the response to al-Shafi'i's argument from the reported hadith about 'first day' and 'second day' is that specification with a specific name does not prevent inclusion under the general term, citing Quran 2:98 where Gabriel and Michael are mentioned separately yet are included under 'angels'. Lexicographical support from al-Khalil and al-Nawawi confirms the broader definition.

Key Terms
البدن (al-budn): Plural of badanah, referring to sacrificial animals; according to the Hanafis, includes both camels and cows.
الإشعار (al-ish'ar): Marking a sacrificial animal by stabbing its hump on the right side to wound it, so it is known to be a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does covering a sacrificial animal with a cloth make one a muhrim?
A) Yes, because it is a recommended act of Hajj.
B) No, because covering may be done for other reasons like protection from heat or cold.
C) Yes, if it is done with the intention of Hajj.
D) No, only if the animal is a camel.

Key Takeaway
Covering, marking, and collaring sacrificial animals do not make one muhrim because they are not Hajj-specific rites; the intra-Hanafi difference on ish'ar does not change this.

Definition of Badana (Sacrificial Animal) and Associated Disputes
Definition of badana (sacrificial animal) and cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define badana according to the Hanafi school, explain the cross-madhhab disputes on its scope, and evaluate the evidence used.

Core Idea
Badana includes both camels and cows according to Hanafis, contrary to Malik and Shafi'i who restrict it.

What exactly counts as a 'badana' (sacrificial animal)? The Hanafi school takes a broad view, including both camels and cows unconditionally. This lesson examines the definition, the evidence from hadith and Quran, and the disagreements with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools. Understanding this definition impacts which animals can be used for certain rituals.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi definition
According to the text, 'al-budn' (plural of badanah) applies to camels and cows absolutely, regardless of ability to procure a camel.
The phrase 'مطلقاً' (absolutely) indicates no condition.
2
Identify the opposing views
Malik restricts badana to cows only if one cannot get a camel. Al-Shafi'i restricts it to camels exclusively.
Both opponents rely on linguistic or textual arguments.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i evidence
Al-Shafi'i cites a hadith mentioning 'badana' and 'cow' separately, implying they are different. The Hanafi response is that specification with a specific name does not exclude from the general category.
The Quranic example of mentioning Gabriel and Michael after 'angels' is used as proof.
4
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafis cite the hadith of Jabir: 'We used to sacrifice a badanah for seven people' and then equate a cow to a badanah. Additionally, lexicographers like al-Khalil define badanah as a she-camel or a cow.
This directly supports the broader definition.
5
Determine the practical impact
According to Hanafis, a cow is a valid badana for collective sacrifice (e.g., seven people sharing one animal). Shafi'is would require a camel for such collective sharing.
This affects the permissibility of using cows in certain Hajj rites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن جلّلها أو أشعرها أو قلد شاةً لم يكن محرماً، والبدن من الإبل والبقر. أي وضع الجل على البدنة وإن ساقها تعتبر شرعا أو أشعرها: من الإشعار، وهو الطعن في سنام الهدي من جانبها الأيمن أي أدماها بجرح ليعلم أنها هدي. (ط،ع) لم يكن محرماً لأن شيئاً من ذلك ليس من خصائص الحج؛ إذ التجليل وإن ندب إليه إلا أنه قد يكون لدفع الأذى كالحر والبرد، والإشعار مكروه عند الإمام أي الإدماء بالجرح، فلا يكون من النسك، وعندهما: وإن كان حسنا إلا أنه قد يفعل للمعالجة، وتقليد الشاة ليس بسنة غير معتاد والتقليد أحب من التجليل لذكره في القرآن. (فتح، مستخلص) والبدن: بضم الباء جمع بدنة وهي عندنا من الإبل والبقر مطلقاً، سواء عجز من الإبل أو لا، وقال مالك: إن عجز من الإبل فمن البقر، وقال الشافعي: من الإبل خاصة بظاهر قوله عليه: "من راح يوم الأولى فكأنما قرب بدنة، ومن راح في الثانية فكأنما قرب بقرة فإنه يفيد التغاير بينهما، وأجيب بأن التخصيص باسم خاص لا يمنع الدخول تحت العام، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ كَانَ عَدُوّاً لِلَّهِ وَمَلائِكَتِهِ وَرُسُلِهِ وَجِبْرِيلَ وَمِيكَالَ﴾ (البقرة:۹۸)، ولنا: حديث جابر "كنا ننحر البدنة عن سبعة، فقيل والبقرة؟ فقال: "وهل هي إلا وقال الخليل: إن البدنة ناقة أو بقرة تهدى إلى مكة، قال النووي وهو قول أكثر أهل اللغة. (عيني، فتح)
If he covers it (the sacrificial animal) with a cloth, or marks it by cutting its hump, or ties a collar on a sheep, he is not a muhrim. And al-budn are from camels and cows. i.e., placing a covering on the budnah. And if he drives it, it is considered legally valid. Or marks it: from ish'ar, which is stabbing the hump of the sacrificial animal on its right side, i.e., wounding it to let know that it is a sacrificial animal. (T, A) He is not a muhrim because none of these are specific characteristics of Hajj; for covering, although recommended, may be to repel harm like heat or cold, and ish'ar is disliked according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) i.e., wounding by cutting, so it is not part of the ritual. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): although it is good, it may be done for medical treatment. And tying a collar on a sheep is not a sunnah, not customary, and tying a collar is more beloved than covering because it is mentioned in the Quran. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And al-budn: with damma on ba', plural of badanah, which according to us (Hanafis) applies to camels and cows absolutely, whether he is unable (to get a camel) or not. Malik said: if unable to get a camel, then from cows. Al-Shafi'i said: from camels only, based on the apparent meaning of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Whoever goes on the first day, it is as if he sacrificed a badanah, and whoever goes on the second day, it is as if he sacrificed a cow' for it indicates differentiation between them. The response is that specification with a specific name does not prevent inclusion under the general term, like His statement: 'And whoever is an enemy to Allah and His angels and His messengers and Gabriel and Michael' (2:98). And we have the hadith of Jabir: 'We used to sacrifice a badanah for seven people.' It was said: 'And a cow?' He said: 'Is it not...' Al-Khalil said: A badanah is a she-camel or a cow that is sent to Mecca. Al-Nawawi said it is the saying of most lexicographers. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage discusses actions that do not constitute entering into the state of ihram. The core ruling is that covering a sacrificial animal (tajlil), marking it (ish'ar), or putting a collar on a sheep (taqlid) does not make one a muhrim. The reason given is that none of these acts are specific to Hajj; they may be done for other purposes like protection from weather or medical treatment. Within the Hanafi school, there is an intra-madhhab difference: Imam Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar (wounding the hump) to be makruh (disliked), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it good (hasan) though it could be for medical treatment. The passage then defines 'badanah' (pl. budn) as a sacrificial animal. According to the Hanafis, it includes both camels and cows absolutely. The opposite views of Malik (cows only if unable to get camels) and al-Shafi'i (camels only) are presented and refuted using textual evidence: a hadith from Jabir shows that a badanah was shared by seven people, and the response to al-Shafi'i's argument from the reported hadith about 'first day' and 'second day' is that specification with a specific name does not prevent inclusion under the general term, citing Quran 2:98 where Gabriel and Michael are mentioned separately yet are included under 'angels'. Lexicographical support from al-Khalil and al-Nawawi confirms the broader definition.

Key Terms
البدن (al-budn): Plural of badanah, referring to sacrificial animals; according to the Hanafis, includes both camels and cows.
الإشعار (al-ish'ar): Marking a sacrificial animal by stabbing its hump on the right side to wound it, so it is known to be a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, absolutely, as stated in the text.
B) No, only camels.
C) Yes, but only if one cannot find a camel.
D) No, because the hadith separates badana and cow.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines badana as including both camels and cows unconditionally, supported by hadith, linguistic evidence, and usul principles.

The Superiority of Qiran: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on the best form of Hajj: qiran, tamattu', or ifrad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the best form of Hajj and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah, completing both, and involves an additional sacrifice – hence it is best.

Which form of Hajj brings the greatest reward? The Hanafi school holds that combining Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram (qiran) is superior to performing them separately (ifrad) or with a break (tamattu'). In this lesson, we examine the textual and analogical proofs that support this preference, and see how the Hanafis respond to the Shafi'i argument that ifrad is better. We also note a lone narration from Abu Hanifa that ifrad may be superior, yet the relied-upon position remains qiran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of muhrim
Before analyzing the dispute, learn the definitions: mufrid bi al-Hajj, mufrid bi al-Umrah, qarin, and mutamatti'. Note their key features and conditions.
This classification is essential for understanding the disagreement.
2
State the Hanafi position on superiority
The text explicitly says qiran is better than tamattu' and ifrad (أفضل من التمتع والإفراد). This is the mufta bihi position.
There is a lone narration from Abu Hanifa that ifrad is better, but it is not the relied-upon view.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that ifrad involves more acts (talbiyah, travel, halq) and cites a hadith: 'Qiran is a concession, ifrad is determination.' This is also a narration from Abu Hanifa.
The objection challenges the basis of the Hanafi preference.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis provide multiple proofs: Quran 2:196 interpreted by the Companions as performing both together; the Prophet's own practice (hadith of Anas and Ali); the analogy of combining acts of worship; the additional blood sacrifice in qiran. They reinterpret the 'rukhsah' hadith as a refutation of pre-Islamic practice, not as a downgrade.
Pay attention to the technical distinctions: talbiyah is unlimited, travel is not the objective, and halq is exiting worship.
5
Note the practical difference and Malik's view
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis recommend qiran, Shafi'is recommend ifrad. Malik considers tamattu' best. The disagreement is about the most rewarding form, not validity.
All three forms are valid in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(رمز الحقائق: ١٦٥/١) مصدر قرن بين الحج والعمرة إذا جمع بينهما في الإحرام والاسم القران مثل كتاب من باب "نصر"، وفي لغة من باب "ضرب" و وهو قارن، والمحرمون أنواع أربعة مفرد بالحج وهو أن يحرم بالحج من الميقات أو قبله في أشهر الحج أو قبلها، وذكر الحج بلسانه عند التلبية وقصد بقلبه أو لم يذكره بلسانه ونوى بقلبه، ويأتي بأفعال الحج كما مر ، والركن . شيئان، الوقوف بعرفة وطواف الزيارة، والإحرام شرط. ومفرد بالعمرة: وهو أن يحرم بها من الميقات أو قبله في أشهر الحج أو قبلها ذكر العمرة بلسانه عند التلبية وقصد بقلبه أو لم يذكر بلسانه ونوى بقلبه، وطاف لها قبل أشهر الحج أو فيها، ولم يحج في عامه ذلك أو حج فيه لكن ألم بأهله بينهما إلماما صحيحا بأن يرجع : إلى أهله حلالا . وأفعالها أربعة: الإحرام والطواف والسعي والحلق الأول شرط الأداء، والآخر شرط الخروج، والباقيان ركناها، وقارن: وهو أن يجمع بينهما في الإحرام من الميقات أو قبله في أشهر الحج أو قبلها، يذكر الحج والعمرة بلسانه عند التلبية ويقصدهما أو لا يذكر باللسان وينوي بالقلب ومتمتع وهو أن يحرم بالعمرة من الميقات أو قبله في أشهر الحج أو قبلها، ويعتمر في أشهر الحج أو يكون أكثر طوافه في أشهر الحج، ويتحلل ويحرم للحج، ويحج من . عامه ذلك قبل أن يلم بأهله إلماما صحيحا. (مسكين، فتح) أفضل من التمتع والإفراد ولذا قدمه. (ط، ع)] وقال الشافعي: الإفراد أفضل؛ لأن في الإفراد زيادة بالتلبية والسفر والحلق، وهذا لا يكون إلا بالإحرام لكل من الحج والعمرة، فإفراد كل منهما أفضل من الجمع بينهما، ولأنه عليه قال: "القران رخصة والإفراد عزيمة" وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ اللهِ ﴾ (البقرة : ١٩٦) وإتمامهما أن يحرم بهما من دويرة أهله كذا فسره الصحابة وهو القرآن، وحديث أنس له أنه قال: سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول : لبيك عمرة وحجاً لبيك عمرة و حجاً"، رواه البخاري ومسلم. وعن علي الله قال: أتيت النبي الله فقال : "كيف أهللت "؟ قلت: "أهللتُ بإهلالك"، فقال: "إني سقت الهدي وقرنت"، رواه أبو داود والنسائي، وقال عليها: "يا آل محمد! أهلوا بالعمرة والحج معاً"، ولأن فيه جمعا بين العبادتين فأشبه الصوم والاعتكاف والحراسة في سبيل الله مع صلاة الليل، والتلبية غير محصورة فيمكن أن يزيد القارن على المفرد والسفر غير مقصود، والحلق خروج عن العبادة فلا يرجّح، وقوله علي: "القرآن رخصة" نفي قول أهل الجاهلية: إن العمرة في أشهر الحج من أفجر الفجور، أو المراد بسقوط سفر العمرة صار رخصة رمز الحقائق: ١٦٥/١] وأيضاً في القران زيادة نسك، وهو إراقة الدم، وفيه امتداد إحرامهما، بخلاف المتمتع ،والمفرد وقال مالك: التمتع أفضل
Chapter of Qiran: [It is a verbal noun from 'qarana' between two things, meaning you combine them, and al-qarin is the one who combines Hajj and Umrah. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:165) A verbal noun from 'qarana' between Hajj and Umrah when he combines them in ihram, and the noun is qiran like kitab from the pattern of 'nasara', and in a dialect from the pattern of 'daraba', and he is a qarin. The muhrimun are four types: Mufrid bi al-Hajj: he assumes ihram for Hajj from the miqat or before it in the months of Hajj or before them, mentioning Hajj with his tongue at the talbiyah and intending with his heart, or does not mention it with his tongue and intends with his heart, and performs the actions of Hajj as mentioned. The rukn are two: standing at Arafah and the visitation tawaf, and ihram is a condition. Mufrid bi al-Umrah: he assumes ihram for Umrah from the miqat or before it in the months of Hajj or before them, mentioning Umrah with his tongue at the talbiyah and intending with his heart, or does not mention it with his tongue and intends with his heart, and performs tawaf for it before the months of Hajj or during them, and does not perform Hajj that same year or performs Hajj but returns to his family between them properly by becoming halal. Its actions are four: ihram, tawaf, sa'i, and halq. The first is a condition for performance, the last is a condition for exit, the remaining two are its pillars. Qarin: he combines both in ihram from the miqat or before it in the months of Hajj or before them, mentioning Hajj and Umrah with his tongue at the talbiyah and intending both, or does not mention with the tongue and intends with the heart. Mutamatti': he assumes ihram for Umrah from the miqat or before it in the months of Hajj or before them, and performs Umrah in the months of Hajj or most of his tawaf is in the months of Hajj, and becomes halal, then assumes ihram for Hajj, and performs Hajj in that same year before returning to his family properly. (Miskin, Fath) It (Qiran) is better than tamattu' and ifrad, therefore he (the author) presented it first. (T, A) Al-Shafi'i said: Ifrad is better because in ifrad there is additional talbiyah, travel, and halq, and this is only achieved by separate ihram for each of Hajj and Umrah, so performing each individually is better than combining them. Also because he (peace be upon him) said: 'Qiran is a concession and ifrad is a determination' – this is also a narration from Abu Hanifah. Our proof is the statement of Allah: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (2:196). Completing them is to assume ihram for both from one's home district – this is the interpretation of the Companions – and that is qiran. Also the hadith of Anas that he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: 'Labbayk bi Umrah wa Hajj, Labbayk bi Umrah wa Hajj' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he said: 'How did you enter ihram?' I said: 'I entered ihram with your ihram.' He said: 'I have driven the sacrificial animal and performed qiran' narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'O family of Muhammad! Enter ihram for Umrah and Hajj together.' Also because it combines two acts of worship, so it resembles fasting and i'tikaf and guarding in the path of Allah with night prayer. Talbiyah is not limited, so the qarin can increase over the mufrid, and travel is not the objective, and halq is exiting from worship so it is not a preference. And his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Qiran is a concession' refutes the statement of the people of Jahiliyyah that Umrah in the months of Hajj is the most wicked of wicked acts, or the meaning is that due to the elimination of the journey for Umrah it became a concession (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:165). Also in qiran there is an additional ritual, which is blood sacrifice, and it includes extension of both ihrams, unlike the mutamatti' and the mufrid. Malik said: Tamattu' is better.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). It defines the four categories of muhrim: mufrid bi al-Hajj (separate Hajj), mufrid bi al-Umrah (separate Umrah), qarin (combining both), and mutamatti' (performing Umrah first then Hajj in the same year). The main point of dispute is which of these three forms (ifrad, tamattu', qiran) is superior. The Hanafi position, as stated in the text, is that qiran is best, then tamattu', then ifrad. The author presents this preference and then gives the proof. Al-Shafi'i argues that ifrad is better because it involves more acts of worship (additional talbiyah, travel, halq) and because of a hadith that qiran is a rukhsah (concession) while ifrad is azimah (determination). There is even a narration from Abu Hanifa that ifrad is better. However, the Hanafi response counters with several proofs: Quran 2:196 ('Complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah') interpreted by the Companions as performing both together from home (qiran); the hadith of Anas where the Prophet performed qiran; the hadith of Ali where the Prophet combined; the hadith 'O family of Muhammad! Perform Umrah and Hajj together'; the analogy of combining two acts of worship being like combining fasting and i'tikaf; and the point that additional talbiyah is not limited. The Hanafis reinterpret the hadith about qiran being a concession as a refutation of the pre-Islamic view that Umrah in the Hajj months was wicked, or that it is a concession because it removes the need for a separate journey. Additionally, qiran involves a blood sacrifice (dam) which increases devotion, and the state of ihram is extended. Malik's view that tamattu' is better is mentioned but not refuted in this passage.

Key Terms
القارن (al-qarin): One who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram.
المتمتع (al-mutamatti'): One who performs Umrah first, becomes halal, then assumes ihram for Hajj in the same year before returning home.
المفرد (al-mufrid): One who performs only Hajj (or only Umrah) without combining them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which form of Hajj is considered the best?
A) Ifrad (separate Hajj only)
B) Tamattu' (Umrah then Hajj with a break)
C) Qiran (combined Hajj and Umrah)
D) All are equally meritorious

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds qiran as the best form of Hajj because it completes both Hajj and Umrah together as commanded, involves an additional sacrifice, and is supported by the Prophet's own practice.

6 min
The Virtue of Hajj al-Qiran: Combining Hajj and Umrah in One Ihram
Defines Qiran and argues its superiority with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Hajj al-Qiran, explain the Hanafi proof for its superiority from Surah al-Baqarah, and address the objection that Tamattu' is explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Core Idea
Qiran is the best Hajj because it fulfills the command to complete Hajj and Umrah with a single continuous ihram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram (Qiran) is the most virtuous form. The text defines Qiran, provides the proof from the Quran, and answers a key objection. Understanding this ruling clarifies the school's preference and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of Hajj
List Ifrad, Tamattu', and Qiran, noting their key differences in timing and ihram.
Ifrad: Hajj only; Tamattu': Umrah then Hajj with break; Qiran: both with continuous ihram.
2
Analyze the definition of Qiran
From the text, extract the specific conditions: ihram from miqat, intention for both, and the sequence of rituals (tawaf, sa'y, then Hajj).
The intent is declared as 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah'.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The verse 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (2:196) is used as a dalil. The imperative 'atimmū' (complete) indicates the obligation to perform both acts; Qiran fulfills this with continuous ihram from the start.
Tamattu' has a break in ihram, so it does not fully satisfy the command.
4
Evaluate the objection and response
The text addresses a potential criticism: if Qiran is best, why is Tamattu' explicitly mentioned in the Quran? The Hanafi response: knowledge of combination (Qiran) depends on first understanding individual acts (Ifrad). The Quran mentions Tamattu' as a permissible option, not as the best.
The absence of the word 'Qiran' does not negate its virtue.
5
Note the cross-madhhab context
Recognize that other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki) consider Ifrad the best form. The Hanafi position is based on the continuity of ihram and the verse of completion.
All forms are valid; the difference is in virtue (afdaliyyah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القران تم الإفراد وهو أن يهلّ بالعُمرة والحج من الميقات ويقول: اللهم إني أريد الحج والعمرة أي القرآن أي صفته أي يحرم معا أو قبله بل هو الأفضل بعد ركعتي الإحرام فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني، ويطوف ويسعى لها، ثم يحج كما مرّ، فإن طاف لهما طوافين كان أي للعمرة أي يأتي بأفعال الحج أي للعمرة والحج لأن له ذكراً في القرآن وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا أَمِنْتُمْ فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجَّ﴾ (البقرة:١٩٦)، ولا ذكر للقرآن، ولنا: أن في القران تعجيلاً للإحرام واستدامة إلى أن يفرغ منهما كما ذكرنا في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ﴾ (البقرة : ١٩٦) ولا كذلك التمتع، فكان القران أولى. فإن قيل: لما كان القرآن أفضل من الإفراد حقه أن يقدم في البيان؟ قلنا: معرفة القرآن وهو الجمع موقوفة على الإفراد. (مستخلص، فتح) من الإفراد: بالحج أفضل من الإفراد بالعمرة. (ط)
Chapter of Qiran. Ifrad is completed by entering into ihram for 'umrah and Hajj from the miqat and saying: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and 'umrah.' (Meaning of Qiran: its description, i.e., he enters ihram for both together or one before the other, but it is the best after the two rak'ahs of ihram) 'make them easy for me and accept them from me.' He performs tawaf and sa'y for them, then performs Hajj as mentioned. If he performs two tawafs for them (meaning for 'umrah, he performs the actions of Hajj; meaning for 'umrah and Hajj) because it has mention in the Qur'an, namely His statement: 'Then when you are secure, whoever performs 'umrah [and then] Hajj' (al-Baqarah 2:196), and there is no mention of Qiran. Our proof: In Qiran there is early ihram and continuity until completion of both, as we mentioned concerning His statement: 'And complete the Hajj and 'umrah for Allah' (al-Baqarah 2:196). This is not so for Tamattu', thus Qiran is more virtuous. If it is said: Since Qiran is better than Ifrad, it should have been mentioned first in the exposition? We say: Knowledge of Qiran, which is combination, depends on [understanding] Ifrad. (From al-Mustakhlas, Fath) Concerning Ifrad: performing Hajj alone is better than performing 'umrah alone.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the definition and superiority of Hajj al-Qiran. The text defines Qiran as combining Hajj and 'umrah in a single ihram from the miqat, with the pilgrim declaring intention for both. It asserts that Qiran is the most virtuous form after the two-rak'ah prayer of ihram. The proof is derived from two Qur'anic verses: (1) 'Then when you are secure, whoever performs 'umrah [and then] Hajj' (2:196) refers to Tamattu', not Qiran; but (2) 'And complete the Hajj and 'umrah for Allah' (2:196) implies that both acts are to be completed together, which is achieved by Qiran's continuous ihram from the start. The text then addresses an objection: if Qiran is best, why is it not named in the Qur'an? The answer is that the name 'Qiran' (combination) depends on first understanding the individual acts (Ifrad). The passage concludes with a note from al-Mustakhlas and Fath that performing Hajj alone (Ifrad) is better than performing 'umrah alone.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): The form of Hajj where one enters ihram for both Hajj and 'umrah together from the miqat.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without 'umrah.
التمتع (al-tamattu): Performing 'umrah first, then Hajj separately in the same year, with a break in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
Hajj al-Qiran is the most virtuous form in the Hanafi school because it involves continuous ihram from the miqat, fulfilling the Quranic command to 'complete Hajj and Umrah'.

Manner of Entering Ihram for Qiran
Explains how to pronounce intention and the ruling on precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of initiating ihram for Qiran and identify the ruling when the order is reversed.

Core Idea
Reversing the ihram order for Qiran is valid but blameworthy and requires a compensatory dam.

This lesson explains the proper sequence for a Qarin to enter ihram. The ideal method is to begin with 'umrah then add Hajj. If reversed, the act remains valid but incurs blame and a compulsory sacrificial compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ideal sequence
The Qarin should first enter ihram for 'umrah, then for Hajj before completing four circuits of tawaf for 'umrah.
2
Recognize the reversed sequence
If one enters ihram for Hajj first, then adds 'umrah, the action is permitted but considered blameworthy (isā'a).
Reversal is valid but not preferred.
3
Determine the consequence
A compensatory sacrifice (dam jabar) becomes wajib, not a thank-offering (dam shukr).
Dam jabar compensates for the deficiency in order.
4
Understand the rationale
'Umrah should precede Hajj in action, so it should also precede in intention. Thus, reversing the intention order is blameworthy.
5
Note textual variation
In some commentaries, 'umrah is mentioned first in the supplication; but the matn mentions Hajj first for blessing from the Quranic verse (Baqarah 2:196).
This does not change the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يهل بالعمرة والحج حقيقة أو حكماً بأن يحرم بالعمرة أولاً، ثم بالحج قبل أن يطوف للعمرة أربعة أشواط، وعكسه بأن يدخل إحرام العمرة على الحج قبل أن يطوف للقدوم وإن أساء، ولزمه دم أي دم جبر لا دم شكر، ووجه الإساءة تقديم إحرام الحج على إحرام العمرة؛ لأنها مقدمة فعلاً فكذا إحراماً، ولهذا تقدم العمرة بالذكر إذا أحرم بهما معاً، وكذا تقدم في دعاء التيسير كما وقع في نسخ الشروح "أريد العمرة والحج، لكن في نسخة المتن "أريد الحج والعمرة" بتقديم الحج تبركاً بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ ﴾ (البقرة: ١٩٦). (فتح)
He enters ihram for 'umrah and Hajj in reality or legally by first entering ihram for 'umrah, then for Hajj before he has performed four circuits of tawaf for 'umrah. The reverse is [permissible] by adding ihram for 'umrah onto Hajj before performing tawaf al-qudum, though he does wrong, and a dam is required, i.e., a compensatory dam, not a thank-offering. The reason for the wrongdoing is the precedence of Hajj over 'umrah in ihram, since 'umrah is performed first in action, so it should be first in ihram. Thus, 'umrah is mentioned first when entering ihram for both together, and similarly it is given precedence in the supplication for ease as found in copies of the commentaries: 'I intend 'umrah and Hajj'. However, in the matn version it is 'I intend Hajj and 'umrah' giving precedence to Hajj for blessing based on His statement: 'And complete the Hajj and 'umrah for Allah' (al-Baqarah 2:196). (Fath)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing how the Qarin should enter ihram. Ideally, one should first intend 'umrah, then add intention for Hajj before completing four circuits of tawaf for 'umrah. If one reverses the order (intending Hajj first, then adding 'umrah), the action is valid but blameworthy (isā'a), and a compensatory dam (dam jabar) becomes wajib, not a thank-offering (dam shukr). The reason for blame is that 'umrah should precede Hajj in action and thus in intention. The text notes a variant: in some commentaries the supplication mentions 'umrah first, but in the matn (original text) Hajj is mentioned first to seek blessing from the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jabar): A compensatory sacrifice required to make up for a deficiency or error in the rituals.
الإساءة (al-isā'a): Doing something blameworthy but not sinful enough to invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is valid and no dam is required
D) It is mandatory to repeat the ihram

Key Takeaway
The Qarin should ideally start with 'umrah then Hajj; if reversed, the ihram remains valid but requires a compensatory dam (dam jabar).

Tawaf and Sa'y for the Qarin
Inter-madhhab dispute on tawaf and sa'y requirements for Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required number of tawafs and sa'ys for the Qarin, identify the opposing school's view and its evidence, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal using hadith criticism and the principle of no overlapping in worship.

Core Idea
The Qarin must perform two separate tawafs and sa'ys—one for 'umrah and one for hajj—as worship cannot overlap.

This passage presents a fundamental inter-madhhab dispute in Hajj rituals: how many tawafs and sa'ys must the Qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together) perform? The Hanafi school insists on two separate sets, while the Maliki and Shafi'i schools hold that one set suffices. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'ys: one set for 'umrah and one for hajj.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that one tawaf and one sa'y suffice.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They cite a hadith from Ibn 'Umar reported by al-Tirmidhi: 'Whoever enters ihram for Hajj and 'Umrah, one tawaf and one sa'y are sufficient.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis present a contradictory hadith from Ibn 'Umar via al-Daraqutni where he performed two tawafs and two sa'ys and attributed it directly to the Prophet. They prefer this narration because of explicit prophetic attribution and confirmatory action. They also argue by principle: Qiran means combination, so acts cannot overlap, as in prayer and fasting.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi Qarin must perform six additional circuits (one full tawaf and one sa'y) compared to the Shafi'i/Maliki Qarin, making the rituals lengthier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويطوف أي إذا دخل مكة يبدأ بطواف العمرة، فيطوف سبعة أشواط يرمل في الثلاثة الأولى، ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة، وهذه أفعال العمرة، وتقديم العمرة على الحج واجب، فلو طاف أولاً لحجته لها، فطوافه الأول وسعى وسعيه يكون للعمرة، ونيته لغو، ولا يلزمه دم؛ لأن التقديم والتأخير في المناسك لا يوجب الدم عندهما، أبي حنيفة: طواف التحية سنة، وتركه لا يوجب الدم فتقديمه أولى، ولو طاف قارن لعمرته ثم حلق فعليه دمان، وعند ويسعى سعياً ولا يحل من عمرته بالحلق (فتح) لها : أي للعمرة أولاً ولا يحلق بخلاف المتمتع الذي لم يسق الهدي. (ط) كما مر : [ أي في باب المفرد، ويسعى وهذا الترتيب واجب. (ط، ع)] فيبدأ بطواف القدوم ويسعى بعده إن شاء، فعندنا للقارن طوافان وسعيان، طواف للعمرة وطواف للحج، وهكذا السعي وقال مالك والشافعي القارن يطوف طوافاً واحداً، واحداً؛ لما روي عن ابن عمر لهما أنه قال: من أحرم بالحج والعمرة أجزأه طواف واحد وسعي واحد"، رواه الترمذي، ولنا ما ورد عن ابن عمر لها أنه جمع بين الحج والعمرة، فطاف لهما طوافين وسعى سعيين، وقال: "هكذا رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصنع كما صنعت"، رواه الدار قطني؛ ولأن القران هو الجمع، فمن لم يفعل لم يكن جامعاً؛ ولأنه لا تداخل في العبادة كالصلاة والصوم والرواية عن ابن عمر لما قد اختلفت، لكن ترجّحت رواية الدار قطني بفعل ابن عمر ما وتصريحه بقوله: "رأيت رسول الله" إلخ، بخلاف رواية الترمذي؛ إذ لم يصرح فيها بما يفيد الرفع إليه عليه. (فتح) طوافين متواليين من غير أن يتخلل بينهما سعي العمرة. (ط) وسعى سعيين جاز وأساء
He performs tawaf: i.e., when he enters Makkah, he begins with tawaf al-'umrah, performing seven circuits, walking briskly (ramal) in the first three, and performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of 'umrah. Giving precedence to 'umrah over Hajj is wajib. If he first performed tawaf for his Hajj, then his first tawaf and sa'y are for 'umrah, and his intention is void, and no dam is required according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because precedence and delay in rituals do not necessitate a dam according to them. Abu Hanifa: Tawaf al-tahiyyah is sunnah, and omitting it does not require a dam, so giving precedence is better. If a Qarin performed tawaf for his 'umrah then shaved, he owes two dams. And he does not become free from his 'umrah by shaving. (Fath) 'for her' i.e., for 'umrah first, and he does not shave, unlike the Mutamatti' who did not bring a sacrificial animal. (T) 'as mentioned' [i.e., in the chapter on Ifrad, and he performs sa'y, and this order is wajib. (T, 'A)] So he begins with tawaf al-qudum and then performs sa'y if he wishes. According to us, the Qarin has two tawafs and two sa'ys: one tawaf for 'umrah and one for Hajj, and similarly for sa'y. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: The Qarin performs only one tawaf and one sa'y, based on what is narrated from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'Whoever enters ihram for Hajj and 'umrah, one tawaf and one sa'y are sufficient for him,' narrated by al-Tirmidhi. Our proof: what is reported from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he combined Hajj and 'umrah, performing two tawafs and two sa'ys, and said: 'Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) do as I have done,' narrated by al-Daraqutni. Also because Qiran means combination, so whoever does not do two of each has not combined. Also because there is no overlapping in worship, like prayer and fasting. The two narrations from Ibn 'Umar conflict, but the narration of al-Daraqutni is preferred because of Ibn 'Umar's action and his explicit statement 'I saw the Messenger of Allah,' unlike al-Tirmidhi's narration which does not explicitly attribute it to the Prophet. (Fath) Two consecutive tawafs without sa'y al-'umrah in between. (T) He performed two sa'ys; this is permissible but blameworthy.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of tawaf and sa'y required for the Qarin. The Hanafi position is that the Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'ys: one set for 'umrah and one for Hajj. The text begins by explaining the order: upon entering Makkah, the Qarin starts with tawaf and sa'y for 'umrah, then later performs tawaf al-qudum and sa'y for Hajj. If he inadvertently performs tawaf first with the intention of Hajj, it counts for 'umrah, and his intention is considered void but no dam is required according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa takes a different view: since tawaf al-tahiyyah is sunnah, giving precedence is better. It then narrates the opposing view: Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that only one tawaf and one sa'y are sufficient, citing a hadith from Ibn 'Umar reported by al-Tirmidhi. The Hanafi rebuttal uses another hadith from Ibn 'Umar reported by al-Daraqutni where Ibn 'Umar explicitly performs two tawafs and two sa'ys and states he saw the Prophet do so. The Hanafis argue that since Qiran means combination, one must perform the acts for each ritual separately, as there is no overlapping in worship (like prayer and fasting). They also prefer the Daraqutni narration because it includes explicit attribution to the Prophet. Finally, the text notes that performing two consecutive tawafs (without sa'y in between) and two sa'ys is permissible but blameworthy.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon entering Makkah for Hajj.
لا تداخل في العبادة (lā tadākhul fī al-'ibādah): No overlapping in worship; each act of worship must be performed separately without combining intentions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two tawafs
C) Three tawafs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the Qarin to perform two tawafs and two sa'ys, based on the stronger hadith and the principle that acts of worship cannot overlap.

Sacrifice and Fasting for the Qarin
Rulings on dam, sharing in sacrifice, and fasting as substitute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on the Qarin's sacrifice and fasting substitute and apply the Hanafi proofs for sharing a badanah and fasting in Makkah.

Core Idea
The Qarin's dam is a thank-offering; if unable, fasting three during Hajj and seven after is wajib.

This lesson covers the sacrifice (dam) required of the pilgrim performing Qiran (combining Hajj and 'umrah). You will learn the ruling, the permissibility of sharing a camel or cow, and the fasting substitute for those unable to sacrifice. We will also examine the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 2:196 that allows fasting in Makkah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation of the Qarin
The Qarin must perform one of three options: slaughter a sheep, share in a camel or cow (one-seventh), or fast if unable. The sacrifice is a thank-offering (dam shukr) and the pilgrim may eat from it.
2
Apply the ruling on sharing a badanah
A camel or cow can be shared by up to seven people, provided all intend devotion (qurbah). The text cites Jabir's hadith that they slaughtered a camel for seven with the Prophet.
Malik opposed this, but the Hanafi proof is the hadith and the principle of concession.
3
Derive the fasting substitute from the Quranic verse
Quran 2:196 prescribes three days of fasting during Hajj and seven after return. The phrase 'that is ten complete' removes any illusion of choice between the three and seven.
The verse was revealed for Tamattu', but Qiran is analogous as both combine two rites.
4
Analyze the dispute on 'when you return'
Al-Shafi'i interprets 'return' literally, requiring the seven-day fast to be observed after reaching home. Hanafi interprets it as 'completion of Hajj', allowing fasting in Makkah even without intending to reside.
The Hanafi response uses linguistic principle: the cause (completion) is used to refer to the effect (return).
5
Trace the intra-Hanafi difference on order
If the pilgrim shaves before slaughtering, Abu Hanifa requires a dam, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not. The relied-upon position is that reversing the order without a valid reason is makruh but does not require a dam.
The practical consequence: a pilgrim who inadvertently shaves first does not need to repeat the sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا رمى يوم النحر ذبح شاةً أو بدنةً أو سُبُعها، وصام العاجز عنه ثلاثة، جمرة العقبة من الإبل والبقر البدنة جاز لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه رمز الحقائق: ١٦٥/١] وأساء بتأخير سعي العمرة وتقديم طواف التحية عليه، ولا يلزمه بذلك شيء. [رمز الحقائق: ١٦٥/١] ذبح شاة: أي وجوباً قبل الحلق بشرط أن يقع الذبح في يوم من أيام النحر، فإن حلق قبل الذبح لزمه دم عند الإمام، والذبح قبل الرمي لا يجوز؛ لوجوب الترتيب غير أنه لا يلزمه الدم بعكس الترتيب عندهما، وعنده يجب، وهذا دم القرآن شكراً فيأكل منه، وقوله: "أو سبعها" إيماء إلى أن البدنة من الإبل والبقر يمكن أن يشترك فيها سبعة وقال مالك: لا تجزئ البدنة إلا عن واحد، ولنا: قول جابر انه "حججنا مع رسول الله لا فنحرنا البعير عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، والجزور أفضل من البقرة والاشتراك في البقرة أفضل من الشاة فيما إذا كانت حصة من البقرة أكثر قيمة من الشاة، والمسألة مقيدة بإرادة الكل للقربة وإن اختلفت ،جهتها، حتى لو أراد أحدهم اللحم دون القربة لم يجز، وكل دم وجب جبراً لا يكفي فيه سبع البدنة بخلاف دم الشكر. (عيني، فتح) شاة: وهذا دم القرآن وهو واجب شكراً؛ لما أنعم الله تعالى حيث وفق لأداء النسكين، ولو ذبح قبل الرمي لم يجز. ط، مسكين سبعها : أي أعطى سبع البدنة بأن ذبحت لسبعة. (ط) العاجز عنه أي الفقير العاجز عن الهدي. ثلاثة [ أي ثلاثة أيام في الحج ولو متفرقة. (ط)] أي الفقير إذا عجز عن الذبح لفقره أو فقد ما يذبحه صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج وسبعة إذا فرغ بحيث يكون آخر ثلاثة أيام يوم عرفة، وهو الأفضل، والأصل في صوم الأيام العشرة قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ﴾ (البقرة: ١٩٦)، وإنما شرط أن يكون آخرها يوم عرفة؛ لأن الصوم بدل عن الدم يستحب تأخيره إلى آخر وقته رجاء أن يقدر على الأصل، وهذا بيان الأفضلية، فإن صام قبل ذلك أجزأه لإطلاق النص، وهذه الآية وإن وردت في التمتع فالقران مثله؛ لأنه ترفق بأداء النسكين كالتمتع. فإن قيل: إذا قال تعالى: ﴿فَصِيَامُ ثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ﴾ (البقرة : ١٩٦) علم أن المجموع عشرة أيام، فأي فائدة في قوله: ﴿تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَة﴾؟ قلنا: الواو قد تستعمل بمعنى "أو" فلو اقتصر على ذكر الثلاثة والسبعة ربما توهم متوهم أنه مخير بين الثلاثة والسبعة. فقال: وتِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ إعلاماً بأن الواجب كلها، وقيل: كان في العرب قلة معرفة بالحساب، وإذا كان الرجل خاطباً صاحبه بأعداد متفرقة جمعها ليسرع فهمه إليها، فالآية من ذلك القبيل، وهو كثير في أقوال الشعراء، و"لو" في قوله : "ولو بمكة" متصلة أي وإن كان صام هذه السبعة بمكة متصلة فإنه يجوز، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز إلا أن ينوي الإقامة فيها، هو يقول: إن المراد بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ١٩٦) حقيقة الرجوع، ونحن نقول: رَجَعْتُمْ بمعنى فرغتم عن أفعال الحج، والفراغ سبب الرجوع، فأطلق المسبب على السبب. واعلم أن أول وقت الصوم بعد الإحرام بالعمرة في أشهر الحج، وشرط من جوازه وجود الإحرام، وأن يكون في أشهر الحج؛ لأن كونه متمتعاً شرط بالنص، وقبل الإحرام لا ينعقد سببه هذه هذا
When he throws the pebbles on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep, or a camel or cow, or a seventh of it. And the one unable to do so fasts three days. (Jamrat al-'Aqabah; camel and cow are badanah; it is permissible because he has done what is required of him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/165] And he acts wrongly by delaying sa'y al-'umrah and advancing tawaf al-tahiyyah, but nothing is required of him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/165] Slaughtering a sheep: i.e., it is wajib before shaving, provided the slaughter occurs on one of the days of Nahr. If he shaves before slaughtering, a dam is required according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. Slaughtering before throwing is not permissible due to the required order, but according to the two, the dam is not required for reversing the order; according to him it is required. This dam of Qiran is a thank-offering, so he eats from it. His statement 'or a seventh of it' indicates that a badanah from camels or cows can be shared by seven. Malik said: A badanah is not sufficient except for one person. Our proof: the statement of Jabir: 'We performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah and we slaughtered a camel for seven and a cow for seven,' reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim. A male camel is better than a cow, and sharing in a cow is better than [slaughtering] a sheep if the share of the cow is more valuable than the sheep. The matter is conditioned on all intending devotion even if their intentions differ; if one intends meat without devotion, it is not permissible. Every dam that is wajib as compensation is not sufficient with a seventh of a badanah, unlike the dam of thanks. ('Ayni, Fath) 'Sheep': This is the dam of Qiran, and it is wajib as thanks for the blessing of being enabled to perform both rites. If he slaughters before throwing, it is not permissible. (T) 'Masakin sub'aha': i.e., he gives a seventh of the badanah, as it is slaughtered for seven. (T) 'The one unable': i.e., the poor person unable to afford the sacrificial animal. 'Three' [i.e., three days during Hajj, even if separate. (T)] i.e., the poor person if unable to slaughter due to poverty or lack of an animal, fasts three days during Hajj and seven after completion, such that the last of the three days is the Day of 'Arafah, which is best. The basis for fasting ten days is His statement: 'But whoever cannot find [a sacrifice], then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete [days]' (al-Baqarah 2:196). The condition that the last of them be the Day of 'Arafah is because the fast is a substitute for the dam; it is recommended to delay it to the end of its time hoping to be able to perform the original. This is a statement of preference; if he fasts before that, it suffices due to the absolute wording of the text. This verse, though revealed regarding Tamattu', Qiran is like it because it is a concession for performing both rites like Tamattu'. If it is said: When Allah says 'then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return' (2:196), it is known the total is ten days, so what benefit is there in His saying 'that is ten complete'? We say: The conjunction 'and' (waw) is sometimes used in the sense of 'or'. If He only mentioned three and seven, one might mistakenly think he has a choice between three and seven. So He said 'that is ten complete' to inform that all are required. It is also said that the Arabs had little knowledge of arithmetic, and when a speaker addresses his companion with separate numbers, he combines them to expedite understanding; the verse is of this type, and this is common in poetry. The word 'law' in His statement 'even if in Makkah' is connected, meaning even if he fasts these seven in Makkah continuously, it is permissible. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible unless he intends to stay there. He holds that the meaning of His statement 'when you return' (2:196) is the literal return. We say: 'return' means you have completed the actions of Hajj, and completion is the cause of return, so the cause is used to refer to the effect. Know that the beginning time for the fast is after entering ihram for 'umrah in the months of Hajj, and the condition for its validity is the existence of ihram and that it be in the months of Hajj, because being a Mutamatti' is a condition by the text. Before ihram, its cause is not established.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering the sacrifice (dam) required of the Qarin and the substitute of fasting. The Qarin must slaughter a sheep, or share in a camel or cow (one-seventh), on the Day of Nahr after throwing pebbles, before shaving. The dam is a thank-offering (dam shukr) and the pilgrim may eat from it. If one cannot afford it, fasting three days during Hajj (preferably ending on the Day of 'Arafah) and seven days after completion is required, based on the Quranic verse (2:196). The passage discusses details: the order of slaughter relative to shaving and throwing; Abu Hanifa requires a dam if shaving precedes slaughter, while the Sahibayn do not. Sharing in a camel or cow with up to seven people is allowed, based on Jabir's hadith, and Malik's opposing view is rejected. The fatwa on fasting: the seven days can be fasted in Makkah even if one does not intend to reside, contrary to al-Shafi'i. The text also explains the linguistic point of the Quranic verse to remove doubt about choice between three and seven days. The fast is valid from the time of ihram in the months of Hajj.

Key Terms
دم القرآن (dam al-qiran): The sacrifice required from a Qarin as a thank-offering for combining Hajj and 'umrah.
البدنة (al-badanah): A camel or cow that can be shared by up to seven people in sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many people may share in a badanah (camel or cow) for the Qarin's sacrifice?
A) One person only
B) Two people
C) Seven people
D) No sharing is allowed

Key Takeaway
The Qarin must sacrifice or fast; the dam is a thank-offering; sharing a camel/cow with up to seven is valid; the fast may be completed in Makkah.
